\title{\textit{Working Notes on Modular Koszul Duality}}
\author{Raeez Lorgat}
\date{2024--2026}

\begin{document}
\maketitle

\begin{abstract}
One form $\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$, one relation (Arnold),
and residue extraction.  These three ingredients build the chiral
bar complex~$\bar{B}_X(\cA)$, force~$d^2 = 0$, and produce
everything that follows: the bar-cobar adjunction
on~$\mathrm{Ran}(X)$, Koszul inversion, the Lagrangian
decomposition at genus~$g \ge 1$, the modular
characteristic~$\kappa(\cA)$ with its $\hat{A}$-genus generating
function, and the shadow Postnikov obstruction tower whose algebraic degree and
depth class are determined by three genus-$0$ invariants.
\end{abstract}

\begin{quote}
\itshape
These notes are about what happens when you compute with a
$1$-form, what it teaches you when you fail, and why the failures
contain more information than the successes.
\end{quote}

\tableofcontents


% =================================================================
\section{A 1-form}
\label{sec:one-form}
% =================================================================

\begin{equation}\label{eq:seed}
\eta_{ij} \;=\; d\log(z_i - z_j).
\end{equation}

This is the simplest meromorphic $1$-form on the configuration
space $\mathrm{Conf}_2(X)$ of two distinct points on a smooth
curve.  It has a first-order pole along $z_i = z_j$, with
residue~$1$.  Not residue~$k$.  Not residue depending on the
curve, the algebra, or anything.  Just~$1$.

A double pole $dz/(z-w)^2$ carries no coordinate-independent
residue.  A regular form extracts nothing at the collision locus.
The logarithmic derivative threads the needle: strong enough to
detect the collision, mild enough to be canonical.

For three points:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:arnold}
\eta_{12} \wedge \eta_{23}
\;+\; \eta_{23} \wedge \eta_{31}
\;+\; \eta_{31} \wedge \eta_{12}
\;=\; 0.
\end{equation}
This is Arnold's relation.  It holds because
\[
\frac{1}{(z_1 - z_2)(z_2 - z_3)}
+ \frac{1}{(z_2 - z_3)(z_3 - z_1)}
+ \frac{1}{(z_3 - z_1)(z_1 - z_2)}
\;=\; 0,
\]
the partial-fractions identity: three terms, each a product of two
simple poles, summing to zero.  The identity is elementary (clear the
denominator and observe that the numerator vanishes).  It is the only
relation in $H^*(\mathrm{Conf}_n(\C),\C)$, replicated in all higher
degrees by the same mechanism.

\sep

A fool starts here.  One form, one relation, and an extraction
of residues.

Place elements $\phi_1, \ldots, \phi_n$ of a chiral algebra
$\cA$ at $n$ points on $X$.  Dress them in logarithmic forms.
Define a differential by extracting residues at collisions.
Arnold's relation kills every triple residue.  So $d^2 = 0$:
the \textbf{chiral bar complex} $\B_X(\cA)$.

Under a coordinate change $z \mapsto w(z)$, the propagator
transforms as
$\eta_{ij} \mapsto \eta_{ij} +
d\log\frac{w(z_i) - w(z_j)}{z_i - z_j}$.
Near the diagonal this becomes $d\log w'(z_i)$: the standard
cocycle for $\mathrm{Diff}(X)$.  The propagator is a BRST ghost
for diffeomorphisms.  One does not postulate this.  It follows
from the form of $\eta$.


% =================================================================
\section{Two poles}
\label{sec:two-poles}
% =================================================================

The Heisenberg OPE $\alpha(z)\alpha(w) = k/(z-w)^2$ has
one pole.  The bar differential extracts a scalar and
stops.  Everything works.

Kac--Moody has two:
\[
J^a(z) J^b(w) \;=\; \frac{k\kappa^{ab}}{(z-w)^2}
  \;+\; \frac{f^{ab}{}_c\, J^c(w)}{z-w} \;+\; \mathrm{reg}.
\]
The simple pole is the Lie bracket.  The double pole is
the invariant form.  The differential splits: $d = d_{\mathrm{br}}
+ d_{\mathrm{lev}}$.

$d_{\mathrm{br}}^2 \neq 0$ whenever both poles are present.
This was verified across all $2048$ sign conventions arising
from eleven independent binary choices (grading, suspension,
contraction, Koszul signs, ordering, \ldots).  No convention
saves it.

What happens: iterated residues at a triple collision produce
cross-terms between bracket and level.  Jacobi cancels the
bracket-bracket part.  The bracket-level cross-terms survive.
The identity is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cross-term}
d_{\mathrm{br}}^2 \;=\; -\{d_{\mathrm{br}},\, d_{\mathrm{lev}}\}.
\end{equation}
The pair $(d_{\mathrm{br}}, d_{\mathrm{lev}})$ does not form a
bicomplex.  The total $d$ squares to zero not by Jacobi but by
the Borcherds identity, which governs all poles at once.  This
identity is the algebraic shadow of Stokes' theorem on the
Fulton--MacPherson compactification $\overline{C}_n(X)$: at the
corner where three points collide, the two adjacent codimension-$1$
faces carry opposite orientations.  The cancellation is topological.

This is the conformal anomaly.  The classical BRST operator does
not square to zero.  The quantum correction restores nilpotence.
The BV quantum master equation
$\hbar\Delta S + \tfrac{1}{2}\{S,S\} = 0$ is the same equation.

The obstruction to $d_{\mathrm{br}}^2 = 0$ is not an obstruction
to the theory.


% =================================================================
\section{Three logarithms}
\label{sec:three-logs}
% =================================================================

On $\bP^1$ the propagator is single-valued, and $d^2 = 0$ by
Arnold.  On an elliptic curve $E_\tau$, the function $z_1 - z_2$
is not single-valued.  Replace it by the odd theta function, with
the correction forced by double-periodicity:
\[
\eta^{(1)}_{12} = d\log\vartheta_1(z_1 - z_2 \mid \tau)
  + \frac{2\pi i\,\operatorname{Im}(z_1 - z_2)}
    {\operatorname{Im}\tau}\, d\bar{z}_1.
\]
Arnold's relation fails.  What remains is the Arakelov
$(1,1)$-form:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:curvature}
\dfib^{\,2} = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \omega_g.
\end{equation}
One number, $\kappa(\cA)$, extracted from the leading OPE
coefficient, controls the curvature.

\sep

Three differentials act on the genus-$g$ bar complex.

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{(i)} $\dzero$: genus-$0$ collision differential.
Built from $\eta_{ij}$ on $\bP^1$.  Squares to zero by Arnold.
This is classical Koszul duality.

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{(ii)} $\dfib$: fiberwise differential on a fixed curve
$\Sigma_g$.  $\dfib^{\,2} = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \omega_g \neq 0$.

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{(iii)} $\Dg{g}$: total corrected differential, with
$A$-period parameters $t_k = \oint_{A_k}\omega_k$.
$\Dg{g}^2 = 0$.

\medskip

The correction that restores nilpotence is a Lagrangian
splitting.  The $A$-cycles form a Lagrangian subspace of
$H^1(\Sigma_g, \C)$ for the intersection pairing; the curvature
lies in the symplectic complement; the $A$-period corrections
project it to zero.  Nilpotence comes from the symplectic topology
of the surface.

In the curved $\Ainf$ framework: $m_0 = \kappa \cdot \omega_g$,
and $m_1^2(a) = [m_0, a]$ (the commutator, with its sign).
The condition $\kappa = 0$ is simultaneously: $\dfib^2 = 0$;
the bar complex being an honest (uncurved) derived object.
For the bosonic string, the relevant vanishing is
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = \kappa(\mathrm{matter})
+ \kappa(\mathrm{ghost}) = 0$ at $c = 26$: the curvature of
the \emph{combined} system vanishes, not that of a single
algebra.  When $\kappa \neq 0$ the bar complex is curved,
and the curvature is the invariant.

\sep

These are three levels of a single logarithm.

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}ll@{}}
Single-valued on $\bP^1$
  & $\dzero^2 = 0$ at genus~$0$ \\[3pt]
Multi-valued on $\Sigma_g$; monodromy $2\pi i$
  & $\dfib^{\,2} = \kappa \cdot \omega_g$ at genus $g \geq 1$ \\[3pt]
Trivialised on universal cover
  & $\Dg{g}^2 = 0$ (Gauss--Manin correction)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

At genus~$1$ the tadpole amplitude is $\kappa \cdot E_2(\tau)$.
The Eisenstein series transforms as
$E_2(-1/\tau) = \tau^2 E_2(\tau) + 6\tau/(\pi i)$, and the
anomalous term is controlled by $\kappa$.

For uniform-weight algebras (all generators of the same
conformal weight), the obstruction classes at all genera are
controlled by a single generating function:
\[
\sum_{g \geq 1} \kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g \cdot \hbar^{2g}
\;=\;
\kappa(\cA) \cdot \Bigl(\hat{A}(i\hbar) - 1\Bigr).
\]
The $\hat{A}$-genus, from index theory.  The Bernoulli numbers
encode the failure of Arnold's relation at higher genus, and
$\hat{A}(ix) = (x/2)/\sin(x/2)$ has all positive coefficients.
Each $F_g$ is positive.  At genus~$1$ the formula
$F_1 = \kappa/24$ holds unconditionally for all families;
at $g \geq 2$ for multi-weight algebras it remains open
(op:multi-generator-universality).

Nothing in the OPE data predicts the $\hat{A}$-genus.  It lives
in the geometry of $\overline{C}_n(X)$.


% =================================================================
\section{Calls from the future}
\label{sec:calls}
% =================================================================

The $1$-form contains structures it has no right to know about.
Each computation reveals one: the $\hat{A}$-genus, the
Feigin--Frenkel involution, the quantum group, the Langlands dual.
Each revelation opens onto what has not yet been computed.

The temptation is to start with the full OPE, with representation
theory, with $\infty$-categories, to import machinery.  A better
approach is to start with $\eta_{ij}$ and follow where it leads,
retaining awareness of all the directions one has not yet moved in.
The five theorems that follow are not the content of the $1$-form.
They are the first five things it was willing to say.


% =================================================================
\section{The Fourier kernel}
\label{sec:fourier}
% =================================================================

The bar construction is a Fourier transform.  This is not analogy.

\begin{definition}\label{def:cat-log}
$\log^{\mathrm{cat}}(\cA) := \B_X(\cA)$ and
$\exp^{\mathrm{cat}}(\cC) := \Omega_X(\cC)$.
\end{definition}

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\textbf{Classical Fourier} & \textbf{Chiral bar} \\
\hline
Kernel: $e^{-2\pi i x\xi}$
  & Kernel: $\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$ \\[3pt]
$\widehat{f * g} = \hat{f} \cdot \hat{g}$
  & $\mathbb{D}_{\Ran} \circ \B \simeq \B \circ (-)^!$
  \quad(Thm~A) \\[3pt]
$\hat{\hat{f}}(x) = f(-x)$
  & $\Omega(\B(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$
  \quad(Thm~B) \\[3pt]
$\|f\|^2 = \|\hat{f}\|^2$
  & $Q_g(\cA) \oplus Q_g(\cA^!) = H^*(\overline{\cM}_g, \cZ_\cA)$
  \quad(Thm~C) \\[3pt]
Char.\ fn.\ $\to$ moments
  & $\kappa(\cA) \to$ genus tower via $\hat{A}$
  \quad(Thm~D) \\[3pt]
Parseval (completeness)
  & $\ChirHoch^*(\cA)$ polynomial, Koszul-functorial
  \quad(Thm~H)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

When $X$ is a point, $\eta$ vanishes, $d_{\mathrm{res}}$
reduces to the binary bracket, and we recover the classical bar
construction of Loday--Vallette.  Operadic Koszul duality is the
zero-dimensional shadow.

For Heisenberg on $E_\tau$, the bar complex is the Fourier--Mukai
kernel on $\Jac(E_\tau) \times \Jac(E_\tau)^\vee$:
the chiral bar construction \emph{is} the Fourier--Mukai transform,
generalised from abelian to non-abelian.

\sep

The logarithm converts multiplication to addition.  The bar
construction converts the OPE (a product, with poles) to the
bar differential (nilpotent, additive).  The cobar reverses:
it inserts delta-function currents at boundary strata.  Verdier
duality on $\overline{C}_n(X)$ exchanges residues with inclusions.
Theorems A--D are four faces of this one duality.

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}ll@{}}
$\exp(\log(z)) = z$ on $|z-1| < 1$
  & $\Omega(\B(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$ on the Koszul locus \\[3pt]
$\log(1{+}z) = z - z^2/2 + \cdots$
  & PBW spectral sequence: Taylor expansion of the log \\[3pt]
Convergence radius
  & $E_2$ degeneration (Koszulness) \\[3pt]
Analytic continuation past radius
  & Coderived category \\[3pt]
$\log(ab) = \log(a) + \log(b)$
  & $Q_g(\cA) + Q_g(\cA^!) = H^*(\overline{\cM}_g, \cZ_\cA)$
  \quad(Thm~C) \\[3pt]
$\log(1) = 0$
  & $\B(k)$ is acyclic \\[3pt]
Single-valued on simply connected domain
  & $\dzero^2 = 0$ at genus $0$ \\[3pt]
Multi-valued on $\C^\times$; monodromy $2\pi i$
  & $\dfib^{\,2} = \kappa \cdot \omega_g$ at genus $g \geq 1$ \\[3pt]
Residue at branch point
  & Curvature $\kappa(\cA)$ \\[3pt]
Leading coefficient of $\log(1{+}z) = z + \cdots$
  & Modular characteristic $\kappa(\cA)$ \quad(Thm~D)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

Every row is a theorem.

\sep

At $n = 4$, the Fulton--MacPherson compactification
$\overline{M}_{0,5}$ is the del~Pezzo surface $\Bl_4(\bP^2)$,
with $10$ boundary divisors.  The relation $\partial^2 = 0$ on
this surface yields the $\Ainf$ pentagon identity.  The
coherence relations of homotopical algebra come from blowing up
$\bP^2$ four times.

For Koszul algebras: $m_k = 0$ for $k \geq 3$.  For interacting
algebras: $m_3 \neq 0$, and the pentagon is the first obstruction
to formality.  Whether a chiral algebra is Koszul is a question
about the geometry of a del~Pezzo surface.


% =================================================================
\section{The frame atom}
\label{sec:frame}
% =================================================================

The Heisenberg algebra $\cH_k$ sees all five theorems and
encounters none of the pitfalls.  Not because it is simple,
but because its OPE has one pole.

Bar cohomology at weight~$n$ has dimension $p(n-2)$ for $n \ge 2$
(the leading entry at weight~$1$ is the generator itself):
$1, 1, 1, 2, 3, 5, 7, 11, \ldots$\,---the generating function
$\prod_{n \geq 2}(1-q^n)^{-1}$, a piece of the reciprocal
Dedekind eta.  A modular form, at the simplest example.

$\cH_k$ is not self-dual: $\cH_k^! = \mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$.
This is a critical pitfall.  Heisenberg non-self-duality
is the prototype: $\cH_k^! \neq \cH_{-k}$.

The Feigin--Frenkel involution $k \mapsto -k - 2h^\vee$ on
Kac--Moody levels is Verdier duality.  The $-k$ dualises the
form; the $-2h^\vee$ comes from the canonical class of $X$.
For a Koszul pair
$(\widehat{\fg}_k,\,\widehat{\fg}_{-k-2h^\vee})$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:central-charge-sum}
c + c' \;=\; 2\dim(\fg),
\end{equation}
independent of~$k$.  This is Theorem~C at the scalar level.
The Freudenthal--de~Vries formula ensures the sum is always
an integer.  For $\fsl_2$: $c + c' = 6$ at every non-critical
level.

\sep

At the critical level $k = -h^\vee$: the Sugawara tensor is
undefined (not ``$c$ diverges''), the bar complex is uncurved
($\kappa = 0$), and
\[
H^0\bigl(\B(\widehat{\fg}_{-h^\vee})\bigr)
\;\cong\;
\Fun\bigl(\Op_{\fg^\vee}(D)\bigr):
\]
functions on the space of Langlands-dual opers.

$H^1$ gives $1$-forms on opers; $H^2$ gives $2$-forms.  At $H^3$
the Cartan transgression kills the top Lie cohomology class via
a nonzero $d_4$ differential.

Four subjects---representation theory, geometric Langlands,
bar-cobar duality, the classical limit of the BV complex---converge
on a single cochain complex with zero curvature.

At admissible levels $k = -h^\vee + p/q$, the bar complex acquires
periodic CDG structure indexed by $q$-th roots of unity.  This is
the door to logarithmic CFT.


% =================================================================
\section{The bestiary}
\label{sec:bestiary}
% =================================================================

What does the bar complex count?

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{lcll}
\textbf{Algebra} & \textbf{Dims (1--6)}
  & \textbf{Growth} & \textbf{Sequence}\\
\hline
Heisenberg & $1,1,1,2,3,5$ & $e^{C\sqrt{n}}$
  & partitions $p(n{-}2)$ \\
Free fermion & $1,1,2,3,5,7$ & $e^{C\sqrt{n}}$
  & partitions $p(n{-}1)$ \\
$bc$ ghosts & $2,3,6,13,28,59$ & $2^n$
  & --- \\
$\beta\gamma$ & $2,4,10,26,70,192$ & $3^n/\sqrt{n}$
  & A025565 \\
$\widehat{\fsl}_2$ & $3,5,15,36,91,232$ & $3^n/n^{3/2}$
  & modified Riordan \\
Virasoro & $1,2,5,12,30,76$ & $3^n/n^{3/2}$
  & Motzkin differences \\
$\widehat{\fsl}_3$ & $8,36,204,\mathbf{1352}$
  & $8^n$ & (conjectured) \\
$\cW_3$ & $2,5,16,\mathbf{52},\mathbf{171}$
  & $3.3^n$ & (conjectured) \\
$Y(\fsl_2)$ & $4,10,28,\mathbf{82}$
  & $3^n$ & $3^n + 1$ (conjectured)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{warning}\label{warn:riordan-h2}
The classical Riordan generating function
\[
R(x) \;=\; \frac{1 + x - \sqrt{(1-3x)(1+x)}}{2x(1+x)}
\]
yields $3, 6, 15, 36, 91, 232, \ldots$ for the Riordan numbers.
But $H^2(\B(\widehat{\fsl}_2)) = 5$, not~$6$.  This is proved
by explicit Chevalley--Eilenberg computation: at weight~$3$,
$\ker = 8$, $\operatorname{im} = 3$, $H^2_3 = 5$.  The generating
function that governs the bar cohomology of $\widehat{\fsl}_2$
shares the discriminant $(1-3x)(1+x)$ with the Riordan numbers
but differs at the second coefficient.  The naive formula is
wrong at $n = 2$ and correct for $n \geq 3$.
\end{warning}

After Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction to the Virasoro algebra, the
generating function rearranges into Motzkin differences
$M(n{+}1) - M(n)$: lattice paths in the half-plane.  Both come
from the same discriminant $\Delta = (1-3x)(1+x)$; the DS
reduction preserves the branch cut.

The $\fsl_3$ family has discriminant $1 - 3x - x^2$, with
roots involving $\sqrt{13}$\,---and $13 = 3^2 + 4$.  The
recurrence depth of the generating function equals
$\operatorname{rank}(\fg) + 1$ in all known cases.

\sep

Free fields have one OPE pole.  Their bar cohomology grows
sub-exponentially: partitions, $e^{C\sqrt{n}}$.  Interacting
fields have two poles, and their bar cohomology grows
exponentially: $3^n$, $8^n$.  The jump from one pole to two
is an asymptotic phase transition.


% =================================================================
\section{Five invariants}
\label{sec:five}
% =================================================================

The genus expansion of a Koszul chiral algebra $\cA$ is controlled
by a $5$-tuple:
\begin{align*}
\cC_\cA &= (\Theta_\cA,\;\kappa(\cA),\;\Delta_\cA,\;
Q_\cA,\;H_\cA).
\end{align*}
$\Theta_\cA$: universal Maurer--Cartan class.
$\kappa(\cA)$: scalar modular characteristic.
$\Delta_\cA$: spectral discriminant.
$Q_\cA$: shadow metric (the quadratic form on each primary line
controlling the entire infinite tower).
$H_\cA$: Hochschild duality,
$\mathrm{HH}^n(\cA) \cong \mathrm{HH}^{2-n}(\cA^!)^\vee
\otimes \omega_X$.

All proved.

\sep

For every simple $\fg$, cyclic cohomology forces the
Maurer--Cartan class to lie on a one-dimensional line:
$\Theta^{\min}_\cA = \eta \otimes \Gamma_\cA$ for some
tautological coefficient $\Gamma_\cA$.  On the uniform-weight
lane, the identification $\Gamma_\cA = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \Lambda$
holds at all genera.  One number, one kernel, one class.

Why: $H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\fg,\fg) = H^3(\fg) = \C$ for every
simple $\fg$.  One-dimensional.  The cubic Casimir of $\fsl_3$
lives in $H^5(\fg)$: degree $5$ in cyclic cohomology, while
the Maurer--Cartan equation lives at degree~$2$.  The degrees
do not meet.  Higher Casimirs cannot contribute, at any rank.

Genera $1$ and $2$ are rigid: no freedom beyond $\kappa$.  At
genus~$3$:
\[
l_1(\theta_3 - \kappa \cdot \mu \otimes \lambda_3)
= -\tfrac{1}{6}\, l_3(\theta_1, \theta_1, \theta_1),
\]
the first correction, purely Killing.  The $l_2$ term vanishes
by Jacobi: the first nontrivial partition of~$3$ as a sum of
smaller genera is $1 + 1 + 1$, and $l_2$ needs only two inputs.

The modular operator $\kappa(\lambda)$ on $\overline{\cM}_g$
is nilpotent: $\kappa(\lambda)^{g-1} = 0$ on $\cM_g$
(Graber--Vakil).  At $g = 2$: zero already.  At $g = 3$:
nilpotency index $\leq 2$.  The operator does not cycle.  It dies.


% =================================================================
\section{The BV identification}
\label{sec:bv}
% =================================================================

The BV bracket $\{-,-\}$ of degree $+1$ is the simple-pole OPE
residue.  The BV Laplacian $\Delta$ is the double-pole differential.
The quantum master equation
$\hbar\Delta e^{S/\hbar} = 0$ is bar-cobar Verdier compatibility.
These are identities.

The conformal anomaly is one object seen from three windows:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item the curvature $m_0 = \kappa \cdot \omega_g$ of the curved
  $\Ainf$ (the commutator $m_1^2(a) = [m_0, a]$);
\item the obstruction class in $R^*(\overline{\cM}_g)$;
\item the failure $\hbar\Delta S + \tfrac{1}{2}\{S,S\} \neq 0$
  when $c \neq 26$.
\end{itemize}

For the bosonic string: each free boson $\partial\phi$ is
a rank-$1$ Heisenberg $\cH_k$ at level $k = 1/2$
(the string-theory normalisation), with $c = 1$ and
$\kappa = k = 1/2$.  Twenty-six bosons give
$\kappa_{\mathrm{matter}} = 26 \cdot \tfrac{1}{2} = 13$.
The $bc$ ghost system has
$c = -26$ and $\kappa_{\mathrm{ghost}} = -13$.
Total: $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = 0$.  No curvature.  No anomaly.
The QME holds.

\sep

The mode sums converge for every standard family at every
$0 < q < 1$: polynomial OPE growth and subexponential sector
growth suffice.  For Heisenberg, the genus-$g$ partition function
collapses to a one-particle Bergman kernel: a Fredholm determinant,
computed from the prime form.


% =================================================================
\section{Koszulness}
\label{sec:koszulness}
% =================================================================

$U(\fg)$ is Koszul.  This says nothing about $\widehat{\fg}_k$.
The classical bar complex uses one product.  The chiral bar
complex uses the full OPE, all poles at once.  Higher poles are
not perturbations.  The Sugawara tensor
$T = \frac{1}{2(k+h^\vee)}\sum_a \normord{J^a J^a}$ produces
quartic poles in $T(z)T(w)$ via double Wick contractions.

There is a circularity.  To compute bar cohomology: assume
Koszulness (spectral sequence collapses at $E_2$).  Bar
cohomology would then verify Koszulness (via
$H_\cA(t) \cdot H_{\cA^!}(-t) = 1$).  Breaking this circle
requires an independent collapse proof, and every such proof
is specific to its family.

\medskip
\noindent\textsc{Kac--Moody.}\enspace
Whitehead's theorem ($H^n(\fg, V) = 0$ for $n = 1,2$) handles
the off-diagonal, and Killing contraction the invariant piece.
The PBW enrichment at $E_1$ is $\fg \otimes \fg$ (dimension~$9$
for $\fsl_2$), not $\Lambda^2(\fg)$ (dimension~$3$).

\medskip
\noindent\textsc{Virasoro.}\enspace
The subalgebra $\{L_{-1}, L_0, L_1\} \cong \fsl_2$ acts
independently of the central charge, because $m^3 - m = 0$ for
$m \in \{-1,0,1\}$.  The Casimir eigenvalues at every weight
$h \geq 2$ are positive.

\medskip
\noindent\textsc{Principal $\cW_N$.}\enspace
Unique weight-$2$ mechanism from the stress tensor; triangular
$d_2$ argument.

\medskip

There is no universal collapse theorem.  Each algebra must be
convicted on its own evidence.

\sep

The meta-theorem assembles twelve characterisations of chiral
Koszulness.  Among conditions (i)--(x), eight are genuinely independent
bidirectional equivalences; condition~(vi) (Barr--Beck--Lurie) is a
proved consequence of~(v); condition~(viii) (chiral Hochschild
concentration in degrees $\{0,1,2\}$) is a proved one-way consequence
on the Koszul locus.
One further characterisation---the Lagrangian criterion---requires
perfectness hypotheses.
One---D-module purity---is proved in one direction.

The eight genuinely independent bidirectional equivalences plus the two
proved consequences:
PBW degeneration;
$\Ainf$-formality;
Ext diagonal vanishing;
bar-cobar counit being a quasi-isomorphism;
Barr--Beck--Lurie comparison being an equivalence;
factorisation homology concentrated in degree~$0$;
chiral Hochschild vanishing outside degrees $\{0,1,2\}$;
Kac--Shapovalov nondegeneracy in the bar-relevant range;
FM boundary acyclicity;
shadow-formality at arities $2$, $3$, $4$.

$V_k(\fg)$ is Koszul for \emph{all}~$k$.  $L_k(\fg)$ may fail at
admissible levels.  The PBW criterion sees the universal algebra.
Failure for simple quotients comes from vacuum null vectors.


% =================================================================
\section{Two things called $\Eone$}
\label{sec:two-e1}
% =================================================================

On a smooth curve $X$:
\[
\Einf\text{-chiral}
\;\subset\; \Pinf\text{-chiral}
\;\subset\; \Eone\text{-chiral}.
\]

$\Einf$-chiral: vertex algebra.  Skew-symmetric bracket,
unordered configuration spaces.  Heisenberg, Kac--Moody,
Virasoro, $\cW$-algebras.

$\Eone$-chiral: drop skew-symmetry.  $R$-twisted locality:
$J_a(z) J_b(w) - R^{ab}_{cd}(z{-}w)\, J_d(w) J_c(z) = 0$.
When $R = P$ (permutation): $\Einf$.  When $R \neq P$: ordered
configuration spaces, Yangians, quantum lattice algebras.

Meanwhile, separately: the little $n$-disks operad $\mathsf{E}_n$
lives on real $n$-manifolds.  A complex curve is real
$2$-dimensional: the chiral bar complex lives at $n = 2$ (Arnold
relations).  Chern--Simons on a $3$-manifold lives at $n = 3$
(Totaro relations).

An $\Eone$-\emph{chiral} algebra lives on a curve.  A topological
$\Eone$-algebra lives on an interval.  These are different objects
with an overloaded name.  On an interval there are no configuration
spaces, no Arnold relation, no propagator.  The subject does not
become simpler.  It ceases to exist.

\sep

The Kazhdan--Lusztig equivalence sends $\widehat{\fg}_k$-modules
to $U_q(\fg)$-modules, with $q = e^{\pi i/(k+h^\vee)}$ and
braiding by the universal $R$-matrix.  Verdier duality on
$\overline{C}_n(X)$ reverses the braiding: $R \mapsto R^{-1}$.

Without ordering: $k \mapsto -k - 2h^\vee$ (Feigin--Frenkel).
With ordering: $R \mapsto R^{-1}$ (Drinfeld--Kohno).

\[
Y_\hbar(\fsl_N)^{!,\mathrm{ch}}
\;\cong\;
Y_{R^{-1},\hbar}(\fsl_N)^{\mathrm{ch}}.
\]

This single identity unifies three theorems.  Feigin--Frenkel is
its $\Einf$ shadow.  Drinfeld--Kohno is its monodromy.
$\Ass^! = \Ass$ is its shadow at a point.

\sep

Lattice vertex algebras make the $\Einf$/$\Eone$ transition
visible.  A $2$-cocycle $\varepsilon$ on a lattice $\Lambda$
produces $V_\Lambda^\varepsilon$.  When $\varepsilon$ is symmetric:
$\Einf$.  Otherwise: strictly $\Eone$.  Koszul duality inverts the
cocycle: $\varepsilon \mapsto \varepsilon^{-1}$.  For even
unimodular $\Lambda$: self-duality, $V_\Lambda^! \cong V_\Lambda$.
The $E_8$ lattice vertex algebra is Koszul self-dual.

A Coisson algebra (Beilinson--Drinfeld) is a Poisson vertex algebra:
a commutative $\cD_X$-algebra with $\lambda$-bracket.  The
quantisation tower runs:
\[
\text{Coisson}
\;\xrightarrow{\text{star product}}\;
\Einf\text{-chiral}
\;\xrightarrow{R\text{-matrix}}\;
\Eone\text{-chiral}.
\]
Holomorphic-topological gauge theories in $3$d produce Coisson
algebras.  Their quantisation lands at $\Einf$, not $\Eone$.
Reaching $\Eone$ requires the KZ equations on a curve: a
$2$-dimensional phenomenon.  Three dimensions is not enough.


% =================================================================
\section{What the 1-form becomes}
\label{sec:what-it-becomes}
% =================================================================

The genus-completed bar differential is
$D_\cA = d_0 + \sum_{g \geq 1} \hbar^g d_\cA^{(g)}$.

Define
\begin{equation}\label{eq:theta}
\Theta_\cA \;:=\; D_\cA - d_0.
\end{equation}

Since $d_0^2 = 0$ and $D_\cA^2 = 0$:
\[
0 = (d_0 + \Theta_\cA)^2
= [d_0, \Theta_\cA] + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta_\cA, \Theta_\cA].
\]
The Maurer--Cartan equation.  $\Theta_\cA$ is MC
because $D_\cA^2 = 0$.  No construction was needed.

Everything in these notes is a shadow of this element.
The five theorems.  The curvature.  The shadow metric.  The
sewing amplitudes.  The Riordan numbers.  The $\hat{A}$-genus.
The Polyakov effective action.  The Fredholm determinant.  The
Koszul sign.  The $6960$.

The $1$-form $\eta = d\log(z_i - z_j)$ at two points became a
differential $d$ at $n$ points.  The differential became a
genus-expanded $D_\cA$.  The genus expansion became the MC
element $\Theta_\cA = D_\cA - d_0$.  From one $1$-form, one
relation, and one extraction of residues: a universal invariant
of chiral algebras that organises the entire nonlinear structure
of the modular operad.

$D_\cA^2 = 0$ at the convolution level follows from
$\partial^2 = 0$ on $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$.  At the ambient
level, with planted-forest corrections from the log FM
compactification, $D_\cA^2 = 0$ is proved via Mok's
normal-crossings theorem on $\FM_n(X|D)$ for snc pairs.
The planted forests are $\mathrm{Trop}(\FM_n(C|D))$:
tropicalisation of the collision geometry.

\sep

The shadow Postnikov obstruction tower $\Theta_\cA^{\leq r}$ projects
$\Theta_\cA$ to arity $\leq r$.  At each finite order,
$\kappa$, $\mathfrak{C}$, $\mathfrak{Q}$ emerge as the arity-$2$,
$3$, $4$ projections.  The inverse limit converges:
all obstruction classes $[\mathfrak{o}_{r+1}]$ vanish.

The depth of the tower classifies the algebra:

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{clcl}
\textbf{Class} & \textbf{Name} & $r_{\max}$ & \textbf{Examples} \\ \hline
G & Gaussian & $2$ & Heisenberg \\
L & Lie/tree & $3$ & affine KM \\
C & contact & $4$ & $\beta\gamma$ \\
M & mixed & $\infty$ & Virasoro, $\cW_N$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

On a $1$-dimensional primary slice,
$r_{\max} \in \{2, 3, \infty\}$.  The contact class
escapes by stratum separation.  The quintic is forced:
$\mathfrak{o}^{(5)}_{\mathrm{Vir}} \neq 0$.

The shadow metric $Q_L(t) = (2\kappa + 3\alpha t)^2 + 2\Delta t^2$,
with critical discriminant $\Delta = 8\kappa S_4$, controls the
entire tower: the Riccati-type shadow equation
$H^2 = t^4 Q_L$ determines the generating function.  The metric
defines a logarithmic connection
$\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}} = d - Q_L'/(2Q_L)\,dt$ with residue $1/2$
at each zero of $Q_L$ and monodromy $-1$: the Koszul sign.

Under Koszul duality:
$\Delta(\cA) + \Delta(\cA^!) = 6960/[(5c+22)(152-5c)]$.
The numerator is a universal constant.  Self-dual at $c = 13$.


% =================================================================
\section{The weight-$4$ Gram matrix}
\label{sec:gram}
% =================================================================

Basis of the weight-$4$ vacuum Verma:
$|1\rangle = L_{-4}|0\rangle$,
$|2\rangle = L_{-2}^2|0\rangle$.

$G_{11}$: $\langle 0| L_4 L_{-4}|0\rangle
= (8 \cdot 0 + \tfrac{c}{12} \cdot 4 \cdot 15)\langle 0|0\rangle
= 5c$.

$G_{22}$: $L_2 L_{-2}|0\rangle = \tfrac{c}{2}|0\rangle$,
then $L_2 L_{-2}^2|0\rangle = (8+c)L_{-2}|0\rangle$, so
$L_2^2 L_{-2}^2|0\rangle = \tfrac{c(c+8)}{2}|0\rangle$.

$G_{12}$: $L_4 L_{-2}^2|0\rangle = 6 \cdot \tfrac{c}{2}|0\rangle
= 3c$.

\[
G = \begin{pmatrix} 5c & 3c \\ 3c & \tfrac{c(c+8)}{2} \end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det G = \frac{c^2(5c+22)}{2}.
\]

Quasi-primary: $|\Lambda\rangle = L_{-2}^2|0\rangle
- \tfrac{3}{5}L_{-4}|0\rangle$.  The coefficient $-3/5$
(not $-3/10$) because the state corresponding to
$\partial^2 T$ is $2L_{-4}|0\rangle$.
Norm: $\langle\Lambda|\Lambda\rangle = c(5c+22)/10$.

\sep

The $\cW_4$ structure constant:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:c334}
c_{334}^2 = \frac{42\,c^2(5c+22)}{(c+24)(7c+68)(3c+46)}.
\end{equation}

Numerator zeros $=$ Gram determinant zeros $= c^2(5c+22)$:
where a null vector collapses $\Lambda$ onto $\partial^2 T$,
eliminating room for $W^{(4)}$.

Denominator zeros $=$ higher Kac determinant zeros:
$c = -24$, $c = -68/7$, $c = -46/3$.

Overall coefficient $42$: fixed by the classical
$c \to \infty$ limit.

The quartic contact invariant is
$Q^{\mathrm{ct}}_{\mathrm{Vir}} = 10/[c(5c+22)]$, with poles at
$c = 0$ and $c = -22/5$---precisely the zeros of $\det G$.
The shadow obstruction tower's poles are the representation theory's zeros.


% =================================================================
\section{The $\widehat{\fsl}_3$ barrier}
\label{sec:sl3-barrier}
% =================================================================

$H^4(\B(\widehat{\fsl}_3)) = 1352$.  Conjectured.

The rational generating function
\[
  H_{\B}(x) \;=\; \frac{4x(2 - 13x - 2x^2)}{(1-8x)(1-3x-x^2)}
\]
fits $H^1$ through $H^3$ and predicts $H^4 = 1352$.

What is proved:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item \textbf{Koszul dual from series inversion.}
$b_n = [1,8,28,140,392,2884,2716,75488]$.  All positive through
degree~$7$.  Chiral excess
$\varepsilon_n = b_n - \binom{8}{n}$: $[0,0,0,84,322,\ldots]$.

\item \textbf{No quadratic model.}
The chiral OPE is not a quadratic algebra.  The gap
$204 - 120 = 84$ equals $\varepsilon_3 = 140 - 56$.

\item \textbf{$d_{\mathrm{br}}^2 \neq 0$.}
All $2048$ sign conventions.  Rank of $d_{\mathrm{br}}^2$ is~$8$.

\item \textbf{Casimir decomposition.}
At $n = 4$ ($\dim 4096$): the three highest $3C_2$-eigenspaces
($108, 120, 144$, dimensions $112 + 486 + 125 = 723$) have
bracket rank~$0$.  Entirely in the kernel.
Invariant tensor dims: $0, 1, 2, 8$ at $n = 1,2,3,4$.

\item \textbf{Inverse vacuum character.}
$c_H = [q^H]\prod_{n \geq 1}(1-q^n)^8$:
$[1,-8,20,0,-70,64,56,0,-125,\ldots]$.
Convolution $\sum_{j=0}^H c_j V_{H-j} = \delta_{H,0}$
verified through weight~$8$.
\end{enumerate}

Where the computation is stuck: the derivative-residue operator
$R^{(1)}_{ij}$ maps outside the Orlik--Solomon algebra.
No finite-dimensional extension closes under $R^{(1)}$.  The
$R^{(1)}$ barrier is structural: the OPE is not a binary operation
on a fixed vector space but a family of operations parametrised by
the formal disc.  The correct framework is configuration-space
integrals on FM compactifications.

The number $84$ appears three ways:
$204 - 120$ (chiral minus quadratic);
$140 - 56$ (Koszul dual excess);
$\dim(\mathrm{ad}^{\otimes 3})^\fg_{\text{beyond-antisym}}$.
It measures the departure of a chiral algebra from a universal
enveloping algebra.


% =================================================================
\section{$\cW_\infty$ scalar saturation}
\label{sec:winfty}
% =================================================================

\begin{theorem}\label{thm:winfty-scalar}
$\dim H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\cW_\infty, \cW_\infty) = 1$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1.}  For each $N$, BRST pullback along
$\cW_N^k \leftarrow \widehat{\fsl}_{N,k}$ sends cyclic
$2$-cocycles to $H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\fsl_N) \cong H^3(\fsl_N)
\cong \C$.  The ghost contribution vanishes: the exterior algebra
$\bigwedge^*\fn_+$ is Koszul self-dual with no nontrivial cyclic
deformations.  The level direction provides a nonzero cocycle.
$\dim H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\cW_N) = 1$.

\emph{Step 2.}  Truncation $\cW_{N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \cW_N$
preserves the unique central-charge direction.  Both sides
one-dimensional: isomorphism.

\emph{Step 3.}  Sectorwise stabilisation ($N \geq w$ suffices
for weight~$w$) gives Mittag--Leffler, killing $\varprojlim^1$:
$H^2(\cW_\infty) = \varprojlim \C = \C$.

\emph{Cross-check.}  $H^*(\fsl_\infty)
= \bigwedge(x_3, x_5, x_7, \ldots)$ by Borel stability;
$\dim H^3(\fsl_\infty) = 1$.
\end{proof}


% =================================================================
\section{The tower, computed}
\label{sec:tower-computed}
% =================================================================

The shadow metric
$Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) = (c + 6t)^2 + 80t^2/(5c + 22)$ determines
the entire infinite tower.  The generating function
$H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)}$ gives
$\mathrm{Sh}_r = a_{r-2}/r$ where $a_n$ satisfies the
convolution recursion
\begin{equation}\label{eq:convolution}
a_0 = c, \quad a_1 = 6, \quad
a_2 = \frac{40}{c(5c{+}22)}, \quad
a_n = -\frac{1}{2c}\sum_{j=1}^{n-1} a_j\, a_{n-j}
\qquad(n \geq 3).
\end{equation}
This is a finite computation at each arity.

\subsection*{$\alpha = 2$}

The cubic shadow coefficient $\alpha$ for the Virasoro algebra
is~$2$, independent of the central charge.  This is not assumed.
It is \emph{determined}.

The shadow growth rate is
$\rho = \sqrt{9\alpha^2 + 2\Delta}/(2|\kappa|)$, and
$\rho = 1$ gives
\[
9\alpha^2 + \frac{80}{5c+22} = c^2.
\]
Clearing denominators:
$5c^3 + 22c^2 - 45\alpha^2 c - (198\alpha^2 + 80) = 0$.
The known critical cubic is
$5c^3 + 22c^2 - 180c - 872 = 0$.  Matching:
$45\alpha^2 = 180$ and $198\alpha^2 + 80 = 872$.  Both give
$\alpha^2 = 4$.

Three independent confirmations: (i)~the critical cubic;
(ii)~back-derivation from $S_5$ via
$\alpha = -5\kappa S_5/(6S_4) = 2$; (iii)~the Sugawara
self-coupling $C_{TT}^T = 2$ in the Virasoro OPE.

\subsection*{The first ten shadows}

\begin{align*}
S_2 &= \frac{c}{2} \\
S_3 &= 2 \\
S_4 &= \frac{10}{c(5c+22)} \\
S_5 &= \frac{-48}{c^2(5c+22)} \\
S_6 &= \frac{80(45c+193)}{3\,c^3(5c+22)^2} \\
S_7 &= \frac{-2880(15c+61)}{7\,c^4(5c+22)^2} \\
S_8 &= \frac{80(2025c^2 + 16470c + 33314)}{c^5(5c+22)^3} \\
S_9 &= \frac{-1280(2025c^2 + 15570c + 29554)}{3\,c^6(5c+22)^3} \\
S_{10} &= \frac{256(91125c^3 + 1050975c^2 + 3989790c + 4969967)}{c^7(5c+22)^4}
\end{align*}

Verified by three independent implementations: the convolution
recursion~\eqref{eq:convolution}, the master equation recursion
$S_r = -(1/(rc))\sum_{3 \leq j \leq k,\, j+k=r+2}
\varepsilon(j,k)\,jk\,S_j S_k$, and the existing
\texttt{ds\_shadow\_higher\_arity} module.  $67$~tests, all passing.

\subsection*{The denominator theorem}

\begin{theorem}\label{thm:denom-pattern}
For all $r \geq 4$:
$\mathrm{denom}(S_r)
= (\mathrm{const}) \cdot c^{r-3}(5c+22)^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Taylor coefficient $a_n$ of $\sqrt{Q_L}$ satisfies
$a_n = -(1/(2c))\sum a_j a_{n-j}$.  By induction:
$\mathrm{denom}(a_n) = c^{n-1}(5c{+}22)^{\lfloor n/2\rfloor}$
for $n \geq 2$.  Base: $a_2 = 40/[c(5c{+}22)]$.  Step: the
product $a_j a_{n-j}$ contributes $c^{n-2}$ in the denominator
and $(5c{+}22)^{\lfloor j/2\rfloor + \lfloor(n-j)/2\rfloor}$;
the inequality $\lfloor j/2\rfloor + \lfloor(n{-}j)/2\rfloor
\leq \lfloor n/2\rfloor$ is saturated by $j = 2$ (for $n$ even)
or $j = 1$ (for $n$ odd), making the bound exact.
Division by $2c$ raises the $c$-power to $n - 1$.
\end{proof}

No Kac determinant zeros beyond weight~$4$ appear.  The shadow
tower sees only the first Gram determinant.

\subsection*{The phase slip}

The branch points of $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}$ have argument
$\theta(c) \in (\pi/2, \pi)$ for all $c > 0$, since
$\mathrm{disc}(Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}) = -320c^2/(5c{+}22) < 0$
forces complex roots with $\operatorname{Re} < 0$,
$\operatorname{Im} > 0$.  The Darboux transfer theorem gives
approximate sign alternation in $S_r$, with beat period
$\pi/(\pi - \theta)$.  As $c \to \infty$,
$\theta \to \pi$ and the alternation becomes permanent.
At finite~$c$, the pattern has a finite lifetime:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{rrl}
$c$ & $\theta$ & first sign break \\ \hline
$1$ & $164^\circ$ & $r = 17$ \\
$10$ & $170^\circ$ & $r \gg 30$ \\
$13$ & $171^\circ$ & $r \gg 30$ \\
$26$ & $173^\circ$ & $r = 35$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The sign breaks at $c = 1$ ($r = 17$) and $c = 26$ ($r = 35$)
are verified by exact rational computation.

\sep

The shadow metric contains the entire tower.  What the computation
teaches: the denominators know only one Gram determinant, the
numerators know the shadow radius, and the signs know the
argument of the nearest branch point.  The tower is a Taylor
expansion of one quadratic form.

\subsection*{The $\cW_3$ tower: two variables}

For $\cW_3$ with generators $T$ (weight~$2$) and $W$ (weight~$3$),
the shadow lives on a $2$-dimensional deformation space
$(x_T, x_W)$ with propagator
$P = \mathrm{diag}(2/c,\, 3/c)$.  The tower is computed from the
same master equation, now as a $2$d $H$-Poisson bracket:
$\{f, g\}_H = (\partial_T f)(2/c)(\partial_T g)
+ (\partial_W f)(3/c)(\partial_W g)$.

Initial data:
$\mathrm{Sh}_2 = (c/2)\,x_T^2 + (c/3)\,x_W^2$,\enspace
$\mathrm{Sh}_3 = 2x_T^3 + 3 x_T x_W^2$,\enspace
$\mathrm{Sh}_4 = \tfrac{10}{c(5c{+}22)}\,x_T^4
+ \tfrac{960}{c(5c{+}22)^2}\,x_T^2 x_W^2
+ \tfrac{2560}{c(5c{+}22)^3}\,x_W^4$.

Computed through arity~$7$ by the multi-variable master equation.
Two structural results:

\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item \emph{Zero Coxeter anomaly on the $T$-line.}
  $\mathrm{Sh}_r(\cW_3)|_{x_W=0} = \mathrm{Sh}_r(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$
  exactly, through arity~$7$.  The $W$-generator does not
  backreact on the $T$-sector.

\item \emph{$(5c{+}22)$-power increases with $W$-degree.}
  At arity~$r$, the coefficient of $x_T^{r-2k} x_W^{2k}$ has
  $(5c{+}22)$ to power $\geq \lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor + k$ in its
  denominator (with equality at arities~$4$ and~$5$).
  Each pair of $W$-insertions costs at least one extra factor.
\end{enumerate}

The $T$-line is the Virasoro shadow metric.  The $W$-line carries
the non-abelian correction: the $\cW_3$ shadow ``lives over'' the
Virasoro shadow, with the additional $(5c{+}22)$ factors encoding
the coupling between the two generators through the weight-$4$
Gram matrix.




% =================================================================
\section{The vast openness}
\label{sec:openness}
% =================================================================

Everything in \S\ref{sec:one-form}--\S\ref{sec:tower-computed}
can be said in two sentences.

A $1$-form with a simple pole on $\mathrm{Conf}_2(X)$ satisfies
Arnold's relation, induces a nilpotent differential on dressed
configuration spaces, and, when deformed from genus~$0$ to
genus~$g$, acquires a curvature $\kappa(\cA) \cdot \omega_g$
controlled by the leading OPE coefficient.  The genus-completed
differential $D_\cA$ satisfies $D_\cA^2 = 0$, so
$\Theta_\cA := D_\cA - d_0$ is a universal Maurer--Cartan
element whose finite-arity projections are the shadow Postnikov
tower.

That is what the $1$-form told us.  What follows is what it
does when you push it harder: into deeper strata of moduli
space, along ordered paths, through the prime factorisation of
its sewing amplitudes, past the death of the derived category
at genus~$1$, into the bulk on the other side of the boundary.
Each direction is a computation that did not quite finish.


% =================================================================
\section{The second boundary}
\label{sec:second-boundary}
% =================================================================

At genus~$0$, $D^2 = 0$ is Arnold's relation: three simple
poles, opposite orientations at the codimension-$1$ faces of
$\overline{C}_3(\bP^1)$.

At genus~$1$, $D^2 \neq 0$.  The failure is
$\kappa \cdot \omega_1$: one scalar, one K\"ahler form,
from the monodromy of the theta function around its period.

At genus~$2$, $D^2$ is again not zero on the nose.  The
correction that restores nilpotence requires the
\textit{planted forest}: a new kind of boundary stratum in the
moduli space, invisible at genera~$0$ and~$1$.

\sep

Here is the geometry.  The Fulton--MacPherson compactification
$\FM_n(\bP^1)$ resolves collisions of points on the projective
line.  At genus $g \geq 1$ the curve has handles, and the
collision geometry changes: a bubble can grow from a node
where the curve degenerates.  These bubbles are the
\textit{planted trees}---rooted trees whose vertices carry
genus labels $g(v) \geq 0$, growing out of nodes of $\Sigma_g$.

The correct compactification is Mok's logarithmic
Fulton--MacPherson space $\FM_n(X|D)$ for simple normal
crossings pairs $(X,D)$.  Its tropicalisation
$\mathrm{Trop}(\FM_n(C|D))$ produces planted forests.  The
total differential $D_\cA$ acquires three components:
\begin{alignat*}{2}
d_{\mathrm{sew}} &:\quad
  &&\text{self-sewing (identify two punctures, gain a handle)} \\
d_{\mathrm{pf}} &:\quad
  &&\text{planted-forest degeneration (bubble tree grows)} \\
\hbar\Delta &:\quad
  &&\text{non-separating degeneration (BV Laplacian)}
\end{alignat*}
Each is a residue correspondence on the boundary divisors of
$\FM_n(X|D)$.  The identity $D^2 = 0$ at the ambient level
reduces to \textbf{codimension-$2$ cancellation}: every
codimension-$2$ stratum appears as the intersection of exactly
two codimension-$1$ faces with opposite orientations.  This is
Mok's normal-crossings theorem.

\medskip

Every stable graph $\Gamma$ in the modular bar complex
carries a tridegree $(g, n, d)$: loop genus, arity, log
boundary depth.  The depth~$d$ counts internal edges of the
planted-forest part---how far into the boundary of
$\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ the stratum lies.  The
\textbf{genus spectral sequence} has $E_1^{p,*}$ isolating
data at loop genus~$p$, with differentials
$d_r\colon E_r^{p,q} \to E_r^{p+r,q-r+1}$ that are
obstruction maps raising genus.  This filtration is by loop
number, not bar degree---it is distinct from the PBW spectral
sequence.

Two explicit results:

\begin{proposition}[Genus-$2$ planted-forest correction]
\begin{equation}\label{eq:delta-pf-genus2}
\delta_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(2,0)}
\;=\; \frac{S_3(10 S_3 - \kappa)}{48}.
\end{equation}
For Virasoro: $(40-c)/48$.  For Heisenberg: $0$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}[Self-loop parity vanishing]
A single-vertex graph of type $(0, 2k)$ with $k$ self-loops
has amplitude $I_\Gamma = 0$ for all $k \geq 2$, by an
odd-parity involution on $\overline{\cM}_{0,2k}$.
\end{proposition}

The \textbf{shadow visibility genus}
$g_{\min}(S_r) = \lfloor r/2 \rfloor + 1$ is a selection
rule: $S_4$ first contributes at genus~$3$; $S_6$ at genus~$4$.
Each new shadow arity requires a new handle.  The combinatorics
of non-separating self-sewings on~$\Sigma_g$ permit at most
$2g-2$ such operations, and arity~$r$ requires
$\lfloor r/2 \rfloor$ of them.


% =================================================================
\section{One quadratic form}
\label{sec:one-quadratic-form}
% =================================================================

Look at the ten shadows of \S\ref{sec:tower-computed} again.
The denominators are $c^{r-3}(5c+22)^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}$.
The numerators are polynomials in~$c$ with integer coefficients.
The signs oscillate with a period that depends on the argument
of one complex number.  Ten invariants, each a rational function
of~$c$, each determined by one convolution recursion.  Why
should one recursion control everything?

Because the recursion coefficients are the Taylor coefficients
of one quadratic form.

\medskip

The \textbf{shadow metric} on a $1$-dimensional primary
line~$L$ of the cyclic deformation complex is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:shadow-metric-wn}
Q_L(t) \;=\; (2\kappa + 3\alpha t)^2 + 2\Delta\, t^2,
\qquad \Delta \;=\; 8\kappa S_4.
\end{equation}
The Maurer--Cartan equation projected to arity~$r$, on $L$,
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}\label{eq:riccati}
H^2 \;=\; t^4\, Q_L.
\end{equation}
The generating function $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_L(t)}$ satisfies
this identically.  Its Taylor coefficients \textit{are} the
shadow obstruction tower.

This has a geometric meaning.  Define the logarithmic
connection
\begin{equation}\label{eq:shadow-nabla-wn}
\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}} \;=\;
d - \frac{Q_L'(t)}{2\,Q_L(t)}\,dt.
\end{equation}
It has simple poles at the zeros of $Q_L$, residue $1/2$ at
each, and monodromy~$-1$: the Koszul sign.  The function
$\Phi(t) = \sqrt{Q_L(t)/Q_L(0)}$ is a \textit{flat section}
of $\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}}$, and the shadow generating function
$H(t) = 2\kappa\,t^2\,\Phi(t)$ is its parallel transport
weighted by $t^2$.  The shadow obstruction tower is not a sequence of
independent invariants.  It is the Taylor expansion of a
single algebraic function of degree~$2$.

\sep

Koszul duality acts on the discriminant:
\[
\Delta(\cA) + \Delta(\cA^!)
\;=\; \frac{6960}{(5c+22)(152-5c)}.
\]
At $c = 13$ both factors equal $87$, and
$\Delta_{\mathrm{Vir}}(13) = 40/87$.  The numerator
$6960 = 2^4 \cdot 3 \cdot 5 \cdot 29$ is universal.

The shadow growth rate
$\rho = \sqrt{9\alpha^2 + 2\Delta}\,/\,(2|\kappa|)$
governs asymptotics:
$S_r \sim A\,\rho^r\, r^{-5/2}\cos(r\theta + \varphi)$.
Setting $\rho = 1$ gives the critical cubic
$5c^3 + 22c^2 - 180c - 872 = 0$ with positive root
$c^* \approx 6.125$.

The depth classification is forced by~$Q_L$:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $Q_L$ constant ($\alpha = \Delta = 0$):
  class~G, $r_{\max} = 2$.  Heisenberg.
\item $Q_L$ a perfect square ($\Delta = 0$):
  class~L, $r_{\max} = 3$.  Affine Kac--Moody.
\item $Q_L$ irreducible ($\Delta \neq 0$):
  class~M, $r_{\max} = \infty$.  Virasoro, $\cW_N$.
\item Stratum separation (rank-one escape):
  class~C, $r_{\max} = 4$.  $\beta\gamma$.
\end{itemize}
One quadratic form, four classes, an infinite tower or a
finite death.  The shadow metric is the complete invariant
of shadow depth on each primary line.


% =================================================================
\section{The monodromy}
\label{sec:monodromy}
% =================================================================

Move $z_1$ around $z_2$ on the curve.

If the OPE is commutative---$\phi_1(z)\phi_2(w) =
\phi_2(w)\phi_1(z)$---nothing happens.  The propagator
$\eta_{12} = d\log(z_1 - z_2)$ is symmetric.  The bar complex
does not see the ordering.  This is the $\Einf$-chiral world:
vertex algebras.

If the OPE carries a braiding---
\[
J_a(z)\, J_b(w) - R^{cd}_{ab}(z{-}w)\, J_d(w)\, J_c(z)
\;=\; 0
\]
---the propagator acquires a monodromy.  The bar complex on
ordered configuration spaces uses $R$-twisted Arnold relations.
This is the $\Eone$-chiral world: Yangians, quantum lattice
algebras, the KZ equations.

The $R$-matrix is the genus-$0$ binary shadow of $\Theta_\cA$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rmatrix-shadow-wn}
r(z) \;=\;
\Res^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}\bigl(\Theta_\cA\bigr).
\end{equation}
For Kac--Moody:
$r(z) = k\,\Omega_\fg/z$, where
$\Omega_\fg = \sum_a J^a \otimes J_a$ is the Casimir.
For Virasoro:
$r(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$, a quasi-trigonometric solution
of the CYBE.  The full MC element $\Theta_\cA$
lives on the modular operad; its restriction to genus~$0$,
arity~$2$, with ordering, is~$r(z)$.

\sep

Without ordering: Feigin--Frenkel,
$k \mapsto -k - 2h^\vee$.  With ordering:
$R \mapsto R^{-1}$.  In a single identity:
\[
\Ydg_\hbar(\fsl_N)^{!,\mathrm{ch}}
\;\cong\;
\Ydg_{R^{-1},\hbar}(\fsl_N)^{\mathrm{ch}}.
\]
Thick generation of the Yangian derived category is proved for
all simple types via multiplicity-free $\ell$-weights
(Chari--Moura): $V_n \otimes L^- \cong \bigoplus_{j=0}^n
L^-(n-2j)$ at the character level, verified to depth~$60$.

The \textbf{jet principle}: the reduced-weight-$q$ bar window
$K_q(\cA)$ determines $r(z)$ through order $z^{-q}$.  This is
finite-dimensional linear algebra at each jet order---the
ordered analogue of the shadow visibility genus.

The $\widehat{\fsl}_3$ barrier of
\S\ref{sec:sl3-barrier} has a Yangian reading.  The
derivative-residue operator $R^{(1)}$ that maps outside the
Orlik--Solomon algebra is the obstruction to closing the first
jet in a finite-dimensional quotient.  The jet principle says:
do not close $R^{(1)}$ in finite dimensions.  Compute $K_q$
windowwise.  The $\fsl_3$ window at $q = 4$ has
$\dim K_4 = 4096$: a computation in a \textit{fixed} vector
space.  The barrier is not the computation.  It is the
expectation that the answer should have finitely many terms.
The answer has infinitely many terms.  They stabilise
windowwise.


% =================================================================
\section{Prime factorisation}
\label{sec:prime-factorisation}
% =================================================================

Sew the Heisenberg bar complex into a torus.  The partition
function $Z_{\cH}(\tau) = q^{-\kappa/24}\prod_{n \geq 1}
(1-q^n)^{-1}$ has Fourier coefficients~$a(N)$.

Are they multiplicative?

Yes.  The one-particle Bergman reduction factors the sewing
determinant prime-by-prime: the Dirichlet series
$S_{\cH}(u) = \sum a_{\cH}(N)\, N^{-u}$ admits an Euler
product, with each local factor a $2 \times 2$ matrix
determinant.

Now ask about Virasoro.
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-dirichlet-wn}
S_{\mathrm{Vir}}(u) \;=\;
\zeta(u{+}1)\bigl(\zeta(u) - 1\bigr).
\end{equation}
The Euler product is broken.  The ratio
$S_{\mathrm{Vir}}/S_{\cH}$ has singularities at the
nontrivial zeros of $\zeta$: the Virasoro sewing
coefficients carry arithmetic structure that the
Heisenberg coefficients do not.

\sep

The \textbf{arithmetic packet connection}
$\nabla^{\mathrm{arith}}_\cA$ is a flat meromorphic connection
on the module $M_\cA = \bigoplus_\chi M_\chi$ over the
spectral $s$-line, decomposing into an arithmetic skeleton
$\mathrm{Ask}(\cA) = M_\cA^{\mathrm{ss}}$ (semisimple) and
an algebraic defect
$\mathrm{Def}_{\mathrm{alg}}(\cA) = \bigoplus N_\chi M_\chi$
(unipotent monodromy).

The principle: \textit{arithmetic is semisimple; homotopy
defect is unipotent}.

The total depth decomposes:
$d(\cA) = 1 + d_{\mathrm{arith}} + d_{\mathrm{alg}}$.
Algebraic depth $d_{\mathrm{alg}} \in \{0, 1, 2, \infty\}$.
At $d_{\mathrm{arith}} \geq 4$: cusp forms of weight
$\geq 12$ contribute; the Ramanujan $\tau(n)$ enters the
shadow obstruction tower.  No standard family has
$d_{\mathrm{arith}} \geq 4$.  Whether such families exist is
open.


% =================================================================
\section{Two categories}
\label{sec:two-categories}
% =================================================================

The derived category of a curved differential graded algebra
is zero.

This is not an eventual failure or an asymptotic statement.
It is Positselski's acyclicity theorem: if
$m_1^2(a) = [m_0, a] \neq 0$---which is the case whenever
$\kappa \neq 0$---then every bounded complex is acyclic.
The cone of every morphism is exact.  Homological algebra dies.

At genus~$0$, $\kappa$ does not appear.  At genus $g \geq 1$,
$m_0 = \kappa \cdot \omega_g$ is the curvature.  The bar
complex is curved, and the ordinary derived category is zero.

What replaces it: the \textbf{coderived category}
$D^{\mathrm{co}}(\cA\text{-mod})$, which replaces cones by
totalised products.  The shadow invariants $Q_g(\cA)$ live
there, not in $D^b$.

The formal series $\Theta_\cA = \sum \Theta^{(g)} \hbar^g$
converges \emph{$2$-dimensionally}: in both genus and arity.
Genus convergence: Bernoulli decay $1/(2\pi)^{2g}$.  Arity
convergence: the shadow growth rate~$\rho$ from
\S\ref{sec:one-quadratic-form}.  The partition function of the
$1$-form is the value of a convergent double series.  The
partition function of the \textit{string} (genus-factorial
growth $(2g)!$) diverges: it requires resummation.

For Heisenberg, the sewing reduces to a Fredholm determinant:
\[
Z_g(\cH_\kappa;\,\tau) \;=\;
\det\nolimits'_{\mathrm{Fred}}
\bigl(1 - K_\tau^{(g)}\bigr)^{-\kappa}
\]
where $K_\tau^{(g)}$ is the genus-$g$ Bergman kernel operator,
computed from the prime form on~$\Sigma_g$.

\sep

Three objects remain conjectural:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item When does a formal MC element $\Theta_\cA$ lift to the
  completed sewing envelope?  Sufficient conditions are proved
  (polynomial OPE $+$ subexponential growth); necessity is open.
\item The analytic bar coalgebra $\B^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA)$
  should form an analytic Koszul pair with
  $\B^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA^!)$.  The algebraic pair is proved;
  the analytic closure is not.
\item Moriwaki's $\mathrm{IndHilb}$-valued factorisation
  homology works for conformally flat surfaces.  Extension to
  genus $g \geq 2$ requires a curved $\mathrm{IndHilb}$
  framework that does not yet exist.
\end{enumerate}


% =================================================================
\section{The bulk}
\label{sec:bulk}
% =================================================================

The bar differential extracts residues when points collide
along the curve---the $\C$-direction.  The bar coproduct
extracts residues when points collide along the
boundary---the $\mathbb{R}$-direction.  Together: four
kinds of collision.
\begin{alignat*}{2}
d_{\mathrm{res}} &:\quad
  &&\text{bulk points collide (OPE residue)} \\
d_{\Ainf} &:\quad
  &&\text{boundary points collide (Stasheff)} \\
d_{\mathrm{mix}} &:\quad
  &&\text{bulk point hits boundary (bubbling)} \\
d_{\mathrm{clutch}} &:\quad
  &&\text{curve degenerates (nodal clutching)}
\end{alignat*}
Total: $d_{\mathrm{mod}} = d_{\mathrm{res}} + d_{\Ainf}
+ d_{\mathrm{mix}} + d_{\mathrm{clutch}}$, with
$d_{\mathrm{mod}}^2 = 0$ at genus~$0$ and
$d_{\mathrm{mod}}^2 = m_0$ at genus $g \geq 1$.

This is the \textbf{Swiss-cheese operation space} on
$\FM_k(\C) \times \mathrm{Conf}_m(\mathbb{R})$.
The ordered bar complex extracted from it remains a
single-coloured $E_1$-chiral coalgebra; the genuine
$\SCchtop$ datum lives on the derived-center pair
$(\cC^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA,\cA), \cA)$.

\medskip

On the other side of the boundary lives the \textbf{chiral
derived center}
$\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
= H^*(\cC^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA, \cA), \delta)$:
the universal bulk algebra.  It classifies bulk operators
acting on the boundary---\emph{not} twisting morphisms
between $\cA$ and $\cA^!$ (which is what bar-cobar
classifies).  This is a critical distinction.  Bar-cobar is
about couplings.  The derived center is about the operators
that the boundary algebra does not know it has.

The \textbf{open/closed MC element}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:oc-mc-wn}
\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA \;:=\;
\Theta_\cA + \sum_{j=1}^r \mu^{\cM_j}
\end{equation}
packages both: $\Theta_\cA$ (bar-intrinsic) and $\mu^{\cM_j}$
($\Ainf$-module structures at punctures).  Its MC equation
decomposes into: pure closed, pure open, mixed bulk-boundary,
and clutching.

The \textbf{completed modular Koszul datum}
\[
\Pi^{\mathrm{oc}}_X(\cA) \;=\;
\bigl(\B_X,\; \Omega_X,\; \Theta_\cA,\;
\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}},\;
\mathrm{Tr}_\cA,\;
\mathrm{HH}_*,\;
\mathfrak{R}_\bullet^{\mathrm{oc}},\;
\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}\bigr)
\]
assembles eight components---bar coalgebra, cobar algebra,
universal MC class, derived center, annulus trace, Hochschild
homology, nonlinear resonance tower, holographic
connection---from one $\lambda$-bracket.

This is the constructive endpoint: given any chiral algebra,
compute $\Pi^{\mathrm{oc}}_X$.  Theorems A--H are structural
properties of $\Pi^{\mathrm{oc}}_X$.  The non-perturbative
content is its analytic completion.  That is the frontier.


% =================================================================
\section{Window by window}
\label{sec:window}
% =================================================================

At weight~$4$, the Gram matrix of \S\ref{sec:gram} determines
everything: the quasi-primary~$\Lambda$, the structure constant
$c_{334}^2$, the quartic contact invariant
$Q^{\mathrm{ct}} = 10/[c(5c+22)]$.  Two basis vectors, one
$2 \times 2$ matrix, one determinant $c^2(5c+22)/2$.

At weight~$6$: one new quasi-primary enters.  Its norm
involves $c(5c+22)$ and an $S_4$-corrected composite.  A
$3 \times 3$ Gram matrix.

At weight~$8$: two new quasi-primaries.  A $5 \times 5$ matrix.

Each weight is a finite linear algebra problem.  The Koszul
dual of Virasoro is the inverse limit of these windows.  The
question of convergence is the deepest question in the theory.

\sep

$\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$ is the depth-zero approximation, not
the genuine dual.  Self-duality at $c = 13$, \textbf{not}
$c = 26$.  The critical dimension $c = 26$ is where the
\textit{dual} curvature vanishes:
$\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}) = 0$.  The genuine dual is
the completed tower of quasi-primary composites, stabilised
one weight window at a time.  Whether the inverse limit
converges to a recognisable vertex algebra depends on whether
the Gram spectrum is uniformly bounded away from zero---which
is exactly Kac--Shapovalov nondegeneracy in the bar-relevant
range, one of the ten Koszulness equivalences.

\medskip

The \textbf{resonance rank} $\rho(\cA)$ measures the
dimension of $V_0 = B(\cA)_0 \cap \ker(d_{\barBch})$ in the
completed bar complex.

\begin{theorem}[Resonance completion]
Every positive-energy chiral algebra has
$\rho(\cA) < \infty$.
\end{theorem}

\noindent
Positive energy implies finite-dimensional weight spaces;
weight-by-weight SDR (the chiral propagator preserves weight)
bounds $\rho$ by $\dim V_0 < \infty$.  For Virasoro:
$\rho = 1$.  For $\cW_3$: $\rho = 1$.  For affine KM:
$\rho = 0$.

The MC4 completion splits: MC4${}^+$ (positive towers:
$\cW_{1+\infty}$, affine Yangians---solved by weight
stabilisation) versus MC4${}^0$ (resonant towers: Virasoro,
non-quadratic $\cW_N$---reduced to a finite resonance problem).

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The non-principal corridor.}\enspace
Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction for arbitrary nilpotent
$f \in \fg$ produces $\cW_k(\fg, f)$.  The algebra exists.
The obstruction is proving that bar-cobar and Koszul duality
\emph{commute} with non-principal reduction.  Hook-type
nilpotents in type~A are proved.  The Coxeter anomaly: DS can
increase shadow depth (affine at~$3 \to \cW_3$ at~$\infty$).
The type~A transpose conjecture:
\[
\cW_k(\fsl_N, f_\lambda)^!
\;\simeq\;
\cW_{k^\vee_\lambda}(\fsl_N, f_{\lambda^{\mathrm{t}}}).
\]

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The factorisation envelope.}\enspace
Nishinaka's construction produces $U_X(L)$ from a Lie
conformal algebra~$L$: the enveloping vertex algebra on~$X$.
The \textbf{modular Koszul datum}
$\Pi_X(L) = (\mathcal{F}_X, \barB_X, \Theta_L,
\mathcal{L}_L, (V^{\mathrm{br}}, T^{\mathrm{br}}),
R_4^{\mathrm{mod}})$ assembles factorisation algebra, bar
coalgebra, MC class, obstruction Lie algebra, branch data,
modular quartic class---from one Lie conformal algebra.

The modular envelope $U^{\mathrm{mod}}_X(L)$ should be
left adjoint of $\mathrm{Prim}^{\mathrm{mod}}$.  Its
existence is conjectural.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The grand cumulant transform.}\enspace
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grand-cumulant-wn}
M(\cA) \;=\;
\bigl(\mathrm{Cum}_c(\cA),\;\; D_\cA,\;\;
\tau_\cA,\;\; r_\cA(z),\;\; \Theta_\cA\bigr).
\end{equation}
Components 1--3 proved.  Component~4 proved windowwise.
Component~5 proved.  The question: does $M(\cA)$ determine
$\cA$ up to quasi-isomorphism?

\sep

What remains is not a single problem but a boundary: where
algebra meets analysis, where formal series meet convergent
functions, where the $1$-form's predictions become the
theory's theorems.  The modular Koszul datum $\Pi_X(L)$ is the
algebraic side.  The sewing envelope $\cA^{\mathrm{sew}}$
is the analytic side.  The bridge between them is the
completion problem.  It is finite at each stage and infinite
in the limit.


% =================================================================
\section{The sixth movement}
\label{sec:sixth-movement}
% =================================================================

The first five movements of \S\ref{sec:one-form}--\S\ref{sec:openness}
take a single input
\[
\{T{}_\lambda T\} \;=\; \partial T + 2T\lambda + \frac{c}{12}\,\lambda^3
\]
and extract the complete perturbative holographic dictionary of
three-dimensional quantum gravity: the infinite $\Ainf$ tower, the
Koszul dual $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$, the gravitational $R$-matrix
$r(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$, the genus tower
$\sum_{g \geq 1} F_g\,\hbar^{2g}
= \tfrac{c}{2}\bigl(\hat{A}(i\hbar) - 1\bigr)$,
and the BTZ entropy $S = 2\pi\sqrt{ch/6}$.  Movements I--V are
perturbative.  Movement~VI is not.

\sep

The standard approach to the non-perturbative partition function
of 3d gravity is: sum over bulk topologies.  Pick a boundary (say
the torus $T^2$).  Sum over all 3-manifolds $M$ with
$\partial M = T^2$: handlebodies, their $SL(2,\Z)$ images, and
whatever non-handlebody geometries one can classify.  Weight each
by $e^{-S_{\mathrm{EH}}[M]}$.  This is the Maloney--Witten programme.

The sum fails.  For generic~$c$, the Poincar\'e series
$Z_{\mathrm{MW}} = \sum_{\gamma \in \Gamma_\infty \backslash
SL(2,\Z)} Z_0(\gamma \cdot \tau)$ produces negative Fourier
coefficients.  No physical Hilbert space has a negative number
of states.

Every proposed repair introduces something from outside:
ensemble averaging (Cotler--Jensen), non-handlebody corrections
(Maxfield--Turiaci), specific Poincar\'e seeds
(Benjamin--Collier--Maloney).  They ask: \emph{which topologies
should we include?}

The MC element asks a different question.

\sep

\noindent\textbf{The replacement.}
The universal Maurer--Cartan element
$\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$ of the modular convolution algebra
satisfies
\[
D_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}(\Theta) + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta, \Theta] = 0.
\]
This is not a sum over anything.  It is a single algebraic identity
whose genus-$g$ component reads
\[
d^{\mathrm{tree}} \Theta^{(g)}
\;=\;
-\!\!\sum_{\substack{g_1+g_2=g \\ g_i < g}}\!\!
[\Theta^{(g_1)}, \Theta^{(g_2)}]
\;-\; \Theta^{(g-1)}_{\mathrm{clutch}}.
\]
The right side involves only genera strictly below~$g$.  The
left side is the tree-level differential.  On the Koszul locus
(which is where Virasoro lives: one-loop exactness implies
Koszulness), the tree-level complex is acyclic and carries a
contracting homotopy~$h$.  So $\Theta^{(g)} = -h(\text{source})$
is determined uniquely.

No free parameters at any genus.  No choice of which topologies
to include.  The MC equation determines the partition function
at genus~$g$ from the genus-$0$ $\lambda$-bracket, exactly as
$d^2_{\barB} = 0$ is the boundary-of-boundary identity on
$\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$.  The sum over topologies is not repaired.
It is \emph{replaced} by algebraic induction from one quartic pole.

\sep

\noindent\textbf{The anomaly datum.}
The Koszul dual is $B = \mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$, with curvature
$\lambda = \kappa(B) \cdot \omega_1 = \tfrac{26-c}{2}\,\omega_1$.
The \textbf{transgression algebra}
\[
B_\lambda \;=\; B\langle\eta\rangle \,\big/\,
\bigl(\eta^2 - \lambda\bigr),
\qquad |\eta| = 1,\quad d_{B_\lambda}(\eta) = 0,
\]
adjoins a degree-$1$ generator $\eta$ with $\eta^2 = \lambda$
(Clifford, not exterior) and differential
$d_{B_\lambda}(b) = d_B(b) + [\eta, b]$ for $b \in B$.
The secondary anomaly
\[
u \;=\; \eta^2 \;=\; \lambda \;=\; \tfrac{26-c}{2}\,\omega_1
\]
is closed, central, and acts as the scalar $(26-c)/2$ on
standard modules.  The genus-$g$ Clifford completion
\[
\mathfrak{G}_g^{\mathrm{grav}}(c) \;=\;
\mathfrak{G}_g(B_\Theta)
\]
adjoins $2g$ handle operators $\alpha_1, \beta_1, \ldots,
\alpha_g, \beta_g$ with $\alpha_i\beta_j + \beta_j\alpha_i
= \delta_{ij}\,u$.

\sep

\noindent\textbf{The dichotomy.}
The Clifford anticommutator controlled by $u$ splits quantum
gravity into two regimes.

\emph{When $u \neq 0$} (i.e.\ $c \neq 26$): the Clifford algebra
is a matrix algebra after inverting $u$.  Genus-$g$ is Morita
equivalent to genus-$0$.  All genus corrections are resummable.
The $\hat{A}$-genus captures everything.  This is the perturbative
regime: different genera see the same module category.

\emph{When $u = 0$} (i.e.\ $c = 26$): the Clifford anticommutator
vanishes.  The handle operators become exterior generators on
$H_1(\Sigma_g)$.  The theory sees genuine surface topology.
The genus tower collapses ($\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = 0$), and
gravity becomes topological: $Z_{\mathrm{grav}} = 1$.

Different values of $c$ are different theories, not different
phases of one theory.  The transition at $c = 26$ is a parametric
bifurcation in the algebraic structure: as the parameter $c$
crosses $26$, the Clifford algebra degenerates from
$2^g$-dimensional matrix factors to $2^{2g}$-dimensional exterior
algebras.  The secondary anomaly $u$ is the bifurcation parameter.

\begin{observation}
The two critical values of $c$ play distinct roles:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $c = 13$: Koszul self-duality
  ($\mathrm{Vir}_{13}^! = \mathrm{Vir}_{13}$).  The dichotomy
  parameter is $u = 13/2 \neq 0$: self-duality lives in the
  perturbative regime.
\item $c = 26$: anomaly cancellation ($u = 0$).  The
  Clifford/exterior bifurcation.  This is the bosonic string.
\end{itemize}
Self-duality is a symmetry enhancement.  Anomaly cancellation is
a structural bifurcation.  They are separated by $13$ units of
central charge.
\end{observation}

\sep

\noindent\textbf{Complementarity as entanglement.}
Theorem~C of the main work gives, at every genus~$g$,
\[
H^\ast(\overline{\cM}_g,\, \cZ(\mathrm{Vir}_c))
\;=\;
Q_g(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \;\oplus\; Q_g(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}).
\]
The $+1$-eigenspace of the Verdier involution is the boundary
sector.  The $-1$-eigenspace is the bulk sector.  The
$(-(3g-3))$-shifted symplectic structure makes both Lagrangian.

In gravity, this is holographic entanglement:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item The boundary sector $Q_g(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ is the CFT
  contribution.
\item The bulk sector $Q_g(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c})$ is the
  gravitational (Koszul dual) contribution.
\item The symplectic pairing between the Lagrangian subspaces
  is the entanglement between boundary and bulk at genus~$g$.
\end{itemize}
At genus~$1$: $Q_1(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = k \cdot \kappa$
(with $\kappa = c/2$)
and $Q_1(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}) = k \cdot \lambda_1$, with
$\langle \kappa, \lambda_1 \rangle = 1$.
The BTZ partition function factorises into boundary and bulk with
unit entanglement.  The Bekenstein--Hawking entropy
$S = 2\pi\sqrt{ch/6}$ is the saddle-point asymptotic of the
modular $S$-transform applied to this factorisation.

Whether the Ryu--Takayanagi formula is a consequence of the
Lagrangian structure is an open question.  At genus~$1$, the
structures match: $\langle \kappa_1, \lambda_1
\rangle = 1$ on $\overline\cM_{1,1}$ reproduces the BTZ
factorisation.  At higher genus
the identification is conjectural.

\sep

\noindent\textbf{Unitarity as a quasi-isomorphism.}
The bar-cobar equivalence
\[
\Omega(\barB(\mathrm{Vir}_c)) \;\simeq\; \mathrm{Vir}_c
\]
is Theorem~B.  It says: the bar coalgebra $\barB(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$
classifies twisting morphisms (couplings between $\mathrm{Vir}_c$
and its Koszul dual $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$), and the cobar
$\Omega(\barB(\mathrm{Vir}_c)) \simeq \mathrm{Vir}_c$ recovers
the boundary algebra itself.  The bulk is not~$\barB(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$
but the derived centre $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c,
\mathrm{Vir}_c)$~(AP34).

No information is lost.  A state that enters a BTZ black hole
(encoded as an MC deformation $\delta\alpha$ at weight~$h$) can
be recovered from the boundary via the cobar functor.  This is
not a statement about evaporation dynamics; it is a statement
about the algebraic invertibility of the holographic map.

The information paradox, at this level of structure, takes a
precise form: the bar-cobar equivalence guarantees that no
\emph{cohomological} information is lost in the holographic
encoding.  Whether this implies that no \emph{dynamical}
information is lost (as in black hole evaporation) depends on
the relationship between the algebraic encoding and the
physical Hamiltonian; the algebraic framework
does not address this relationship.  The quasi-isomorphism is a necessary
condition for no-information-loss, not a sufficient one.

\sep

\noindent\textbf{The architecture, in one paragraph.}
Start from $\{T_\lambda T\} = \partial T + 2T\lambda +
(c/12)\lambda^3$.  The quartic pole forces an infinite $\Ainf$
tower.  The bar complex encodes it as a dg coalgebra; Koszul
duality produces $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$.  The Koszul dual
curvature $\kappa(B) = (26-c)/2$ controls the transgression.
The anomaly completion of the Koszul dual by this curvature
produces the transgression algebra $(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c})_\Theta$
with secondary anomaly $u = \lambda = \kappa(B) \cdot \omega_1
= \tfrac{26-c}{2}\,\omega_1$.  The
genus-$g$ Clifford completion
$\mathfrak{G}_g^{\mathrm{grav}}(c)$ is the exact
genus-$g$ line-operator algebra: Morita-trivial for $c \neq 26$,
exterior for $c = 26$.
The MC recursion determines the partition function
$Z_g = \operatorname{str}_{\mathfrak{G}_g/B_\Theta}(\Theta^{(g)})$
(the super-trace of the MC element through the Clifford factor)
at every genus from genus-$0$ data alone.  This is the bridge:
the partition function (a section on $\overline{\cM}_g$) and the
line-operator algebra (a Clifford extension of $B_\Theta$) are
connected by the super-trace.
Complementarity gives a Lagrangian decomposition of the
genus-$g$ cohomology into boundary and bulk sectors.
Bar-cobar equivalence gives algebraic invertibility of the
holographic encoding.  One quartic pole, six movements:
the proved algebra, and an honest accounting of the
interpretive identifications it suggests.

\sep

What the Maloney--Witten programme treats as a problem of
\emph{enumeration} (which topologies to sum over), the MC element
treats as a problem of \emph{algebra} (which Maurer--Cartan
equation to solve).  The sum over topologies is a shadow of the
genus expansion of $\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$.  But $\Theta$
exists before the expansion.  The partition function is the
character of $\mathfrak{G}_g^{\mathrm{grav}}$, not a sum over
fillings.

\begin{question}
Does the graded character
$\hat{Z}_1^{\mathrm{grav}}(c;\tau) :=
\chi_{\mathrm{gr}}(\mathfrak{G}_1^{\mathrm{grav}}(c);\,q)$
have non-negative Fourier coefficients for all $c > 1$?
If so, the Maloney--Witten negativity is resolved by the
algebraic construction.  If not, the violation would identify the
precise obstruction to a unitary 3d gravity at that value of~$c$.
\end{question}

\begin{question}
What is the explicit genus-$2$ gravitational partition function
$Z_2(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ computed by the MC recursion?  The stable
graph combinatorics of $\overline{\cM}_2$ (seven stable graphs at
$(g{=}2, n{=}0)$, including the banana graph with
$|\mathrm{Aut}| = 8$) should yield a computable answer.
Does it agree with the $\hat{A}$-genus prediction
$F_2 = (c/2) \cdot 7/5760 = 7c/11520$?
\end{question}

\begin{question}
The complementarity decomposition at genus~$g \geq 2$ has not been
computed for Virasoro.  What is $\dim Q_2(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$?  At
genus~$2$, $\dim H^\ast(\overline{\cM}_2) = 8$ (Poincar\'e
polynomial $1 + 3t^2 + 3t^4 + t^6$), so the Verdier
involution splits this $8$-dimensional space into two
$4$-dimensional Lagrangian halves.  The boundary/bulk partition
is determined by $\kappa = c/2$: which Mumford--Morita--Miller
classes land in which eigenspace?
\end{question}


% =================================================================
\section{The inner music}
\label{sec:coda}
% =================================================================

The $1$-form does not describe bar-cobar duality from outside, as a
functor between categories.  It constructs it from inside, as an
extraction of residues at collisions.  The functor is a consequence
of the construction, not the other way around.

\sep

The following are all the same object:

\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item the curvature $m_0 = \kappa \cdot \omega_g$ of the curved
  $\Ainf$ structure on the genus-$g$ bar complex;
\item the conformal anomaly of the bosonic string;
\item the failure of the classical BRST operator to square to zero;
\item the obstruction class in $R^*(\overline{\cM}_g)$;
\item the leading coefficient of the Taylor expansion of the
  categorical logarithm;
\item the residue at the branch point of the multi-valued
  propagator on $\Sigma_g$;
\item the modular characteristic $\kappa(\cA)$ in Theorem~D;
\item the genus-$1$ Eisenstein coefficient;
\item the $\hat{A}$-genus generating function evaluated at the
  leading OPE coefficient;
\item the scalar projection of the universal MC element
  $\Theta_\cA = D_\cA - d_0$;
\item the curvature of the Koszul dual:
  $\kappa(B) = (26{-}c)/2$, vanishing at $c = 26$;
\item the bifurcation parameter for the Clifford/exterior
  dichotomy: $u = \eta^2 = \lambda$, acting by
  $\kappa(B)$ on standard modules;
\item the Clifford anticommutator of handle operators:
  $\alpha_i \beta_j + \beta_j \alpha_i = \delta_{ij}\,u$;
\item the cosmological constant, measured in units of the
  Lagrangian splitting between the $\pm 1$-eigenspaces
  of the Verdier involution;
\item the source term in the MC recursion that determines
  $\Theta^{(g)}$ from $\Theta^{(g-1)}$;
\item the obstruction to Morita triviality of the genus-$g$
  Clifford completion.
\end{itemize}

\medskip

Most items (1, 3--10, 15) are the algebraic modular
characteristic $\kappa(\cA)$, an invariant of any chiral algebra.
Items 11--14 and 16 involve the Koszul dual curvature
$\kappa(B) = (26{-}c)/2$, which is the curvature of the
dual algebra $B = \mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$.
For the bosonic string, the effective curvature
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = \kappa(\mathrm{matter})
+ \kappa(\mathrm{ghost}) = c/2 + (-13) = (c{-}26)/2$
vanishes at $c = 26$; note the opposite sign:
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = -\kappa(B)$.
Item~2 (the conformal anomaly \emph{of the bosonic string}) is
likewise a gravitational quantity: the worldsheet anomaly that
determines the critical dimension is $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}$, not
the bare $\kappa(\cA)$.  The two scalars coincide only when the
algebra is the full bosonic string.  The list records not a
tautology but a convergence: the same scalar organises both the
algebraic engine and the gravitational application.

\sep

\begin{quote}\itshape
A $1$-form with a simple pole.

A relation among three.

The rest follows.
\end{quote}


% =================================================================
\section{Three roads to a shadow}
\label{sec:three-roads}
% =================================================================

On a primary line $L$ of the cyclic deformation complex, the
shadow coefficients $S_r$ can be computed by three independent
methods.  Each method is exact.  Each method is finite at every
arity.  Their agreement is a theorem.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The algebraic road.}\enspace
The shadow metric $Q_L(t) = 4\kappa^2 + 12\kappa\alpha\,t
+ (9\alpha^2 + 2\Delta)\,t^2$ is a quadratic polynomial.  The
generating function $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_L(t)}$ gives
\begin{equation}\label{eq:algebraic-road}
S_r \;=\; \frac{1}{r}\,[t^{r-2}]\,\sqrt{Q_L(t)}.
\end{equation}
One square root, infinitely many coefficients.  The quadratic
has two roots; the square root is algebraic of degree~$2$; the
entire tower is determined by three numbers $(\kappa, \alpha,
\Delta)$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The recursive road.}\enspace
The MC equation projected to arity $r+2$ expresses $S_{r+2}$
as a polynomial in $S_2, \ldots, S_r$.  The recursion has
the form
\begin{equation}\label{eq:recursive-road}
S_{r+2} \;=\; -\frac{1}{(r{+}2)\kappa}
\sum_{\substack{j+k=r+4 \\ 3 \leq j \leq k}}
\varepsilon(j,k)\,jk\,S_j\,S_k,
\end{equation}
where $\varepsilon(j,k) = 1$ for $j < k$ and
$\varepsilon(j,j) = 1/2$.  This recursion \emph{is} the
condition $H^2 = t^4 Q_L$, expanded order by order.  The
algebraic identity between the two roads is the identity
between a closed form and its Taylor expansion.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The analytic road.}\enspace
The Borel transform $\mathcal{B}(s) = \sum_{r \geq 2}
S_r\,s^r/\Gamma(r+1)$ has singularities at the zeros of
$Q_L(1/s)$.  These are the branch points of the algebraic
function $\sqrt{Q_L}$, transplanted to the Borel plane by the
inversion $t \mapsto 1/s$.  The Stokes constants encode the
discontinuity across the branch cut: the non-perturbative content
of the shadow obstruction tower.  For class~M algebras (Virasoro, $\cW_N$),
$Q_L$ is irreducible and the branch points are complex
conjugate; the Stokes constants are nonzero and produce the
oscillatory decay $S_r \sim A\,\rho^r\,r^{-5/2}\cos(r\theta +
\varphi)$.

\sep

Three methods, one answer.  The agreement is not accidental: the
algebraic road solves the Riccati equation $H^2 = t^4 Q_L$; the
recursive road is its power-series expansion; the analytic road
is its Borel resummation.  The three roads meet at $Q_L$.

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
& \textbf{Shadow obstruction tower}
  & \textbf{Bessel function} \\
\hline
Closed form
  & $t^2\sqrt{Q_L(t)}$
  & $\sqrt{2/(\pi z)}\cos(z - \nu\pi/2 - \pi/4)$ \\[3pt]
Power series
  & $\sum S_r\,t^r$ via MC recursion
  & $\sum (-1)^k (z/2)^{\nu+2k}/(k!\,\Gamma(\nu{+}k{+}1))$ \\[3pt]
Integral/Borel
  & Borel transform with branch cut
  & $\int_0^\pi \cos(\nu\theta - z\sin\theta)\,d\theta/\pi$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

The analogy with classical special functions is exact at the
structural level: ODE, power series, integral representation.
What distinguishes the shadow obstruction tower is that the ODE is
\emph{algebraic} (degree~$2$, not transcendental), and the
three invariants $(\kappa, \alpha, \Delta)$ that parametrise
$Q_L$ are themselves computable from the OPE.
