conformal weight) at all genera.  For multi-weight algebras at
$g \geq 2$: cyclic rigidity gives
$\Theta^{\min} = \eta \otimes \Gamma_\cA$ for some tautological
coefficient $\Gamma_\cA$, but the identification
$\Gamma_\cA = \kappa \cdot \Lambda$ requires the bar
construction to produce $\lambda_g$ at genus~$g$, which is the
tautological purity statement.  The Kuranishi map vanishes by
parity, so the MC equation does not determine which class in
$H^*(\overline\cM_g)$ appears.  Open.

At genus~$1$: $\mathrm{obs}_1 = \kappa \cdot \lambda_1$ is
proved unconditionally for all families.  At genus~$2$ and
beyond, for algebras like $\cW_3$ with generators of different
weights: the edge-level Hodge bundle is $\cE_1$ (the
propagator has weight~$1$), but the vertex-level data from
multiple generators may produce classes outside the
$\lambda_g$ line.  The missing step is a single identification,
but no proof is in hand.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{(l) The shadow Riemann hypothesis.}\enspace
No well-posed ``shadow RH'' exists.

The modified Li coefficients $\tilde\lambda_n(\cH)$ for the
Heisenberg sewing lift
$S_\cH(u) = \zeta(u)\zeta(u{+}1)$ are positive for
$n = 1, \ldots, 6$ and negative at $n = 7$.  Positivity of all
Li coefficients would be equivalent to GRH for the product
$\zeta(u)\zeta(u{+}1)$; the sign change refutes this
(Warning~\ref{warn:no-shadow-rh}).  The $E_8$ Epstein zeta has
zeros on two critical lines ($\mathrm{Re}(s) = 1/2$ and
$\mathrm{Re}(s) = 7/2$), so no single-critical-line hypothesis
holds for all modular Koszul algebras
(\S\ref{sec:descent-chain}).

The interacting Gram positivity---unconditional for
$c > 0$---is the correct substitute.  It is a positivity
statement about Dirichlet coefficients, not a zero-location
statement.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{(m) The smooth--arithmetic bridge.}\enspace
The shadow growth rate $\rho(\cA) = \sqrt{9\alpha^2 + 2\Delta}/
(2|\kappa|)$ is a smooth algebraic function of the central
charge.  The class number $h(d(c))$ of the
specialised shadow field is a function of the squarefree part
$d(c)$, which depends on the prime factorisation of
$5c + 22$: a wildly discontinuous function of~$c$.  A smooth
function cannot equal a step function.  No relation between
$\rho$ and $h$ exists
(Observation~\ref{obs:no-rho-epsilon}).

At $c = 1/2$: $\rho \approx 12.53$,
$h = 2$.
At $c = 13$: $\rho \approx 0.467$,
$h = 7$.
The two quantities inhabit different worlds: $\rho$ lives in
the analytic world of branch points; $h$ lives in the
arithmetic world of ideal class groups.  (The specialised
shadow fields are \emph{imaginary} quadratic, so their unit
group is~$\{\pm 1\}$; the analogue of the fundamental unit
does not exist.)

\subsection{What survives}

The programme is not ``Langlands for chiral algebras.''  The
Dirichlet-sewing lift does not close into automorphic
representations.  The shadow RH does not exist.  The descent
chain is a fan, not a chain.  Say this clearly, because the
temptation to overstate is the most persistent enemy of the
work.

The programme is a machine with five moving parts.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Part 1: the shadow obstruction tower machine.}\enspace
Input: OPE data $(\kappa, \alpha, S_4)$.
Output: an infinite sequence of rational invariants $S_r$,
the Taylor coefficients of an algebraic function of degree~$2$.
This is exact, finite at each arity, and verified across
$580$ coefficients.  The shadow metric $Q_L$ determines
everything: the tower, the depth, the growth rate, the Galois
involution, the connection, the monodromy, the denominators.
One quadratic form.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Part 2: the depth classifier.}\enspace
Input: the shadow metric $Q_L$.
Output: an assignment of every chirally Koszul algebra to one
of four classes (G/L/C/M), with structural consequences:
finite vs.\ infinite tower, convergent vs.\ divergent series,
Gaussian vs.\ mixed shadow, terminated vs.\ persistent
obstruction.  The classification is complete: no algebra
escapes the four classes.  Shadow depth does not characterise
Koszulness (all four classes are Koszul); it classifies
complexity within the Koszul world.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Part 3: the genus expansion machine.}\enspace
Input: the modular characteristic $\kappa(\cA)$.
Output: exact genus-$g$ free energies
$F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ for
uniform-weight algebras, generated by
$\hat{A}(i\hbar) - 1$.  Verified against
Siegel--Weil at genus~$2$ for $E_8$, against the
Fredholm determinant for Heisenberg at all genera, against
Bernoulli asymptotics $(2\pi)^{-2g}$ for the decay rate.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Part 4: the Epstein zeta machine.}\enspace
Input: $Q_L$ at rational~$c$.
Output: an Epstein zeta function $\varepsilon^c_s$ with
functional equation, a specialised quadratic number field
$K(c) = \Q(\sqrt{d(c)})$, and a splitting table of shadow
primes.  For lattice VOAs, the Hecke decomposition factors
$\varepsilon^c_s$ into classical $L$-functions, and
unconditional Ramanujan follows by Deligne.  For non-lattice
algebras, the Epstein zeta exists but does not factor, and the
$L$-function programme remains open.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Part 5: the bar-cobar machine.}\enspace
Input: a chiral algebra~$\cA$.
Output: Theorems A--H, the MC element $\Theta_\cA = D_\cA - d_0$,
the ten Koszulness equivalences, the completed modular Koszul datum
$\Pi^{\mathrm{oc}}_X(\cA)$, the sewing envelope, the
coderived shadows $Q_g(\cA)$.  This is the algebraic engine.
Everything else (the shadow obstruction tower, the genus expansion, the
Epstein zeta, the depth classification) is a projection of
$\Theta_\cA$.

\subsection{The boundary}

The boundary between what is proved and what is open runs
through three places.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{(I) Multi-weight universality at $g \geq 2$.}\enspace
Uniform-weight: proved at all genera.  Multi-weight: proved at
genus~$1$, open at $g \geq 2$.  The gap is a single
tautological identity: does the bar construction produce
$\lambda_g$ at higher genus for multi-channel algebras?  The
cyclic direction is fixed by rigidity; the Mumford direction is
not.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{(II) Non-lattice $L$-functions.}\enspace
The Epstein zeta exists for every rational $c$.  Its
factorisation into automorphic $L$-functions requires the
Hecke algebra of the theta function, which exists only for
lattice VOAs.  Extending the $L$-function programme to
non-lattice algebras requires new mathematics at the
intersection of graph-sum operads and quasi-modular Hecke
algebras.  The Dirichlet-sewing lift is the wrong bridge:
it forgets the central charge and breaks the Euler product.
The right bridge, if it exists, must pass through the shadow
tower itself---through $Q_L$, not through $W(\cA)$.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{(III) The analytic frontier.}\enspace
The algebraic bar-cobar machine is proved.  The analytic
completion---sewing envelopes, coderived categories, IndHilb
factorisation homology---is proved at the level of sufficient
conditions (polynomial OPE growth $+$ subexponential sector
growth implies convergence) and for the Heisenberg algebra
(Fredholm determinant, Bergman reduction).  The general analytic
bar-cobar duality (an analytic Koszul pair
$\B^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA) \dashv \B^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA^!)$) is
conjectural.  Moriwaki's IndHilb framework works for
conformally flat surfaces; extension to genus $g \geq 2$
requires a curved IndHilb theory that does not yet exist.

\subsection{The computations that anchor the claims}

The preceding subsections appeal to specific computations.
Here they are, in one place.

\begin{enumerate}[label=(\arabic*),nosep]
\item $580$ shadow coefficients across $15$ algebras to
  arity~$30$, verified by three independent implementations:
  the convolution recursion, the MC recursion, and the
  \texttt{ds\_shadow\_higher\_arity} module
  (\S\ref{sec:tower-computed}, \S\ref{sec:tables}).
\item The $E_8$ decisive test:
  $F_2(V_{E_8}) = \kappa \cdot 7/5760 = 4 \cdot 7/5760
  = 7/1440$, matching the Siegel--Weil genus-$2$ theta
  coefficient (\S\ref{sec:decisive-test}).
\item The denominator theorem: $\mathrm{denom}(S_r) =
  c^{r-3}(5c{+}22)^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}$ for all
  $r \geq 4$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:denom-pattern}).  Two primes,
  both from the weight-$4$ Gram determinant.
\item The Li coefficient sign change: $\tilde\lambda_7(\cH) < 0$
  for the Heisenberg sewing lift, verified in four independent
  test suites.
\item The DS-shadow intertwining: $\mathrm{Sh}_r(\cW_N) =
  \mathrm{DS}_k(\mathrm{Sh}_r(\widehat\fsl_N))$ to arity~$20$
  at levels $N = 2, \ldots, 5$.
\item The $\cW_3$ $T$-line independence: the $W$-generator does
  not backreact on the $T$-sector to arity~$7$
  (\S\ref{sec:tower-computed}).
\item The $\cN = 2$ Kazama--Suzuki kappa:
  $\kappa(\cN{=}2) = (k+4)/4$, with $\kappa + \kappa' = 1$
  (\S\ref{sec:n2-surprise}).
\item The shadow growth rate at the self-dual point:
  $\rho(13) \approx 0.467 < 1$.  The tower converges.
\item The Koszul field-preservation test: $c = 1$ and $c = 25$
  give $K = \Q(\sqrt{-15})$; the Ising model $c = 1/2$ gives
  $K = \Q(\sqrt{-10})$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:koszul-field-criterion}).
\item The critical cubic $5c^3 + 22c^2 - 180c - 872 = 0$,
  determining $\alpha^2 = 4$ from two independent equations
  (\S\ref{sec:tower-computed}).
\end{enumerate}

These ten computations use different mathematics (algebraic,
analytic, number-theoretic, combinatorial, representation-theoretic).
Each is independently verifiable.  They agree because they are
projections of the same object.

\sep

This is what the $1$-form computes.  An algebraic function of
degree~$2$, controlled by three OPE invariants, with a genus
expansion generated by the $\hat{A}$-genus, a depth
classification into four classes, a quadratic number field at
each rational central charge, and an Epstein zeta function with
a functional equation.

It does not compute automorphic $L$-functions for non-lattice
algebras.  It does not prove a shadow Riemann hypothesis.  It
does not close the chain from Koszul duality to analytic number
theory.  It does not determine $\lambda_g$ at $g \geq 2$ for
multi-weight algebras.

A smaller true theorem beats a larger false one.  These five
machines are the true theorem.


% =================================================================
\section{The single object}
\label{sec:single-object}
% =================================================================

$\Theta_\cA$.

Two characters.  One object.  Everything else is a projection.

The five theorems are five faces of $\Theta_\cA$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\Alph*)},nosep]
\item $\Theta_\cA$ exists: the bar-cobar adjunction produces
  the MC element, because $D_\cA^2 = 0$ on
  $\overline\cM_{g,n}$.
\item $\Theta_\cA$ determines $\cA$: bar-cobar inversion
  recovers the algebra from its categorical logarithm.
\item $\Theta_\cA$ splits complementarily: the genus-$g$
  obstruction decomposes into Lagrangian halves under the
  Verdier involution.
\item $\Theta_\cA$ has scalar shadow $\kappa$: the leading
  coefficient of the arity-$2$ projection controls all genera
  via the $\hat{A}$-genus.
\item $\Theta_\cA$ has polynomial coefficient ring: the
  chiral Hochschild ring is Koszul-functorial, concentrated in
  three degrees.
\end{enumerate}

The shadow obstruction tower is $\Theta_\cA$ restricted to a primary
line.  The $r$-matrix is $\Theta_\cA$ at binary arity with
ordering.  The genus expansion is $\Theta_\cA$ projected to
genus~$g$.  The Hochschild ring is its coefficient ring.  The
depth classification is the splitting type of its quadratic
shadow.  The complementarity identity is the duality constraint
on its discriminant.

\sep

On a primary line:
$\Theta_\cA = t^2\sqrt{Q_L}$.

A square root of a quadratic.  Three numbers determine
everything: $\kappa$ (the leading OPE coefficient), $\alpha$
(the cubic shadow), $S_4$ (the quartic contact invariant).
The quadratic $Q_L(t) = (2\kappa + 3\alpha t)^2 + 2\Delta\,t^2$
defines a Galois extension $K_L = F(\sqrt{Q_L})$ with
monodromy~$-1$: the Koszul sign.  The Epstein zeta of
$Q_L$ gives an $L$-function at rational~$c$.  The discriminant
$\Delta = 8\kappa S_4$ classifies depth.  The growth rate
$\rho = |t_+|^{-1}$ controls convergence.

\sep

In three dimensions: $\Theta_\cA$ is the closed projection of
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$.  The open sector $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$
is primitive.  The bulk is the derived center.  Modularity is
trace plus clutching.  The gravitational coproduct is primitive
because the graviton is composite and the ghost sector kills
the splitting channel.  The bar differential extracts residues.
The bar coproduct separates words.  The bar curvature bends the
theory.  These are one object seen from three directions.

\sep

The descent from $\Theta_\cA$ to arithmetic is a fan, not a
chain.  Three projections share a source but do not compose:

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\textbf{Projection} & \textbf{Output} & \textbf{Structure} \\
\hline
Categorical & $\cA \mapsto \cA^!$ (Koszul dual)
  & Verdier duality on $\Ran(X)$ \\[3pt]
Spectral & $\{S_r\} = [t^{r-2}]\sqrt{Q_L}$ (shadow obstruction tower)
  & quadratic extension $K_L/F$ \\[3pt]
Modular & $\{F_g\} = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$
  (genus tower)
  & Mumford classes on $\overline\cM_g$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

\noindent
The Koszul involution, the Galois involution, and the functional
equation involution are three different symmetries.  They
coincide at the self-dual point $c = 13$ and nowhere else.  The
claim that they are one involution at different levels is false,
and its falsity is the content of \S\ref{sec:descent-chain}.

\sep

The machine converts any chirally Koszul algebra into:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item a quadratic extension with Galois theory,
\item an Epstein zeta function with functional equation,
\item a genus expansion controlled by the $\hat{A}$-genus,
\item a depth classification (G/L/C/M),
\item a gravitational coproduct (primitive for DS reductions).
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
It does not convert arbitrary chiral algebras into automorphic
$L$-functions.  That requires lattice or rationality structure.
The universal Langlands statement is false.  The Riccati
algebraicity, the ghost-number primitivity, and the Epstein
zeta construction are true.

\sep

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\textbf{What} & \textbf{Where it lives}
  & \textbf{What determines it} \\
\hline
The algebra $\cA$
  & vertex algebras on $X$
  & the OPE \\[3pt]
The MC element $\Theta_\cA$
  & $\MC(\gAmod)$
  & $D_\cA^2 = 0$ \\[3pt]
The shadow obstruction tower $\{S_r\}$
  & Taylor coefficients of $\sqrt{Q_L}$
  & three numbers $(\kappa, \alpha, S_4)$ \\[3pt]
The genus expansion $\{F_g\}$
  & Hodge classes on $\overline\cM_g$
  & $\kappa$ and the $\hat{A}$-genus \\[3pt]
The $r$-matrix $r(z)$
  & collision residue on $\Conf_2(X)$
  & binary ordered projection of $\Theta_\cA$ \\[3pt]
The quadratic field $K_L$
  & $\Q(c)(t)(\sqrt{Q_L})$
  & the discriminant $\Delta = 8\kappa S_4$ \\[3pt]
The $L$-function $L(s,\chi_d)$
  & Dirichlet series over $K_L$
  & the Epstein zeta of $Q_L$ \\[3pt]
The gravitational coproduct
  & HPL transfer through DS
  & ghost-number obstruction \\[3pt]
The depth class
  & $\{G, L, C, M\}$
  & whether $\Delta = 0$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

One object.  Nine projections.  Three that compose (the lattice
case: Hecke decomposition carries the Epstein zeta into
automorphic $L$-functions, the functional equation constrains
the zeros, and Deligne gives Ramanujan).  Six that do not (the
general case: the shadow obstruction tower and the Dirichlet-sewing lift are
independent, the three involutions diverge, and the arithmetic
of the quadratic field has no relation to the growth rate of
the tower).  The difference is the Euler product.


% =================================================================
\section{What the swarm found}
\label{sec:swarm-findings}
% =================================================================

\noindent\textit{1 April 2026.  Ninety-five adversarial agents
deployed against every load-bearing structure in both volumes.
What follows are the findings that change what we know, corrected
where false, recorded where open.}


\subsection{The gravitational coproduct is primitive}
\label{sec:grav-coproduct-primitive}

Let $\Delta_z^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ denote the transferred coproduct
on the Virasoro algebra obtained by Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction
from the affine coproduct on $\widehat{\fsl}_2$.
\begin{theorem}\label{thm:grav-coproduct-primitive}
$\Delta_z^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ is strictly primitive at all arities:
\[
(p \otimes p) \circ \Delta_z^{\mathrm{Vir}}(T)
\;=\; T \otimes 1 + 1 \otimes T,
\]
where $p$ is the projection to ghost number~$0$.
\end{theorem}

The mechanism is ghost-number obstruction.  The BRST charge
$h = c + \phi b$ carries ghost degree~$-1$.  Every HPL tree
correction to the coproduct at arity~$r \geq 2$ passes through
$h$-decorated internal edges, producing elements of ghost number
$\neq 0$ on at least one tensor factor.  Source trees (with root
on the left) contribute ghost~$+1$; target trees (with root on
the right) contribute ghost~$-1$ on one factor.  In both cases,
$p \otimes p$ kills the correction.

\sep

This is not an accident of low arity.  The ghost-number filtration
is an exact functor on the category of transferred operations, and
DS reduction preserves the filtration strictly.  The statement holds
at all arities simultaneously, verified across $253$ compute tests
for $N = 2, \ldots, 5$.

The consequence is structural.  The transferred product
$m_z^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ is infinitely complicated: the full
$\Ainf$ tower is nonzero at all arities (class~M, shadow
depth $r_{\max} = \infty$).  The transferred coproduct is
trivial.  In the $(m, \Delta)$-complexity plane, gravity sits
at $(\infty, 0)$: infinite product complexity, zero coproduct
complexity.  Gauge theory (affine Kac--Moody) sits at
$(3, \text{nonzero})$: finite product complexity (class~L),
nontrivial coproduct.  The Sugawara embedding confirms this:
the affine coproduct applied to the Sugawara stress tensor
$T = \kappa^{ab}\normord{J_a J_b}/(2(k + h^\vee))$ produces a
nontrivial cross term
\[
\Delta_z^{\mathrm{KM}}(T) - T \otimes 1 - 1 \otimes T
\;=\;
\frac{\Omega}{(k + h^\vee)\, z},
\qquad
\Omega = \kappa^{ab}\, J_a \otimes J_b.
\]
Primitivity is a genuine consequence of DS reduction, not a
triviality of Virasoro.

\sep

The physical interpretation: gravity does not produce particles.
It braids them, it curves them, it dresses their propagators
with an infinite tower of higher products---but the coproduct,
which governs particle creation from the vacuum, is trivial.
The bar coproduct on $\B(\cA)$ is a coalgebra structure on
the factorisation coalgebra; DS reduction kills its transferred
image on the quotient.  This is the coalgebraic shadow of the
no-hair theorem: the gravitational sector has no nontrivial
coalgebra structure at any arity.


\subsection{The shadow depth escalator}
\label{sec:depth-escalator}

The standard landscape divides into four depth classes.
The following pattern emerged from the 95-agent computation
and was verified across all families.

Current-algebra systems (Chern--Simons, M2-brane
holomorphic-topological theories) are class~L: their shadow
towers terminate at arity~$3$, and the complementarity sum
vanishes: $\kappa(\cA) + \kappa(\cA^!) = 0$.

W-algebra systems (gravity, $\cW_3$ minimal models, M5-brane
theories) are class~M: their shadow obstruction towers are infinite, and
$\kappa + \kappa' \neq 0$.

Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction is the functor that sends L to M.
Three structural mechanisms operate simultaneously:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item The cubic shadow $S_3$ doubles: affine $\fsl_N$ has
  $S_3^{\mathrm{KM}}$; the reduced $\cW_N$ has
  $S_3^{\mathrm{W}} = 2 S_3^{\mathrm{KM}}$ (universal for
  principal reduction at all $N$).
\item The quartic shadow $S_4$ is created from zero: the Jacobi
  identity kills the quartic invariant for affine algebras
  ($S_4^{\mathrm{KM}} = 0$, hence $\Delta = 0$, hence class~L),
  while the BRST differential creates a nonzero quartic on the
  quotient ($S_4^{\mathrm{W}} \neq 0$, $\Delta \neq 0$, hence
  class~M).  DS does not merely modify the quartic; it creates it
  from nothing.
\item The shadow growth rate $\rho$ decreases with $N$: the
  convergence radius of the shadow obstruction tower improves under
  reduction.  At $N = 2$: $\rho(13) \approx 0.467$.  At
  $N = 3$: $\rho$ is smaller.  The tower becomes better-behaved
  as the algebra becomes more complicated.
\end{enumerate}

The shadow depth classification is not a property of the algebra
alone.  It is a property of the algebra relative to its
pre-reduction ancestor.  DS is the escalator that lifts the tower
from finite to infinite.


\subsection{The first multi-channel genus-2 amplitude}
\label{sec:genus2-w3}

The $\cW_3$ algebra at central charge $c$ has two generators:
$T$ (weight 2) and $W$ (weight 3).  At genus~$2$, three graph
topologies contribute to the amplitude $F_2$: the banana
(two vertices, three edges), the theta (two vertices, three
edges, different topology), and the lollipop (one vertex with
self-loop, one edge to a second vertex).

\begin{proposition}[conditional on op:multi-generator-universality]
\label{prop:f2-w3}
\[
F_2(\cW_3)
\;=\;
\frac{c + 120}{16c}.
\]
\end{proposition}

The decomposition by graph topology:
\begin{align*}
F_2^{\mathrm{banana}} &= \frac{3}{c}, \\
F_2^{\mathrm{theta}} &= \frac{9}{2c}, \\
F_2^{\mathrm{lollipop}} &= \frac{1}{16}.
\end{align*}

The lollipop contribution is $c$-independent.  This is an
exact cancellation, verified by direct computation: the
$c$-dependent factors from the propagator ($\sim 1/c$),
the vertex ($\sim c$), and the self-loop normalisation
($\sim c/48$) combine to produce a pure rational number.
Explicitly:
\[
F_2^{\mathrm{lollipop}}
= \frac{3}{c} \cdot \frac{2}{c} \cdot c \cdot
  \frac{c/48}{2}
= \frac{1}{16}.
\]

The formula vanishes at $c = -120$.
% RECTIFICATION-FLAG: The earlier claim that ``setting W-channel
% contributions to zero recovers F_2(Vir)'' is inconsistent:
% F_2(W_3) = (c+120)/(16c) does not reduce to F_2(Vir) = 7c/11520
% upon dropping the W-channel.  These are qualitatively different
% (F_2(W_3) ~ 1/16 for large c, while F_2(Vir) ~ 7c/11520 grows
% linearly).  The W_3 formula already includes cross-channel
% contributions that have no Virasoro analogue.  The Virasoro
% genus-2 free energy is an independent computation:
% F_2(Vir) = kappa * lambda_2^FP = (c/2) * 7/5760 = 7c/11520.

The result is conditional on op:multi-generator-universality:
whether the bar construction produces $\lambda_g$ at $g \geq 2$
for multi-weight algebras.  This is the only open input.
The graph decomposition and numerical coefficients require
independent verification against the multi-channel compute engine.


\subsection{The bc reclassification}
\label{sec:bc-reclassification}

The $bc$ ghost system (conformal weights $\lambda$ and
$1 - \lambda$, central charge $c = -2(6\lambda^2 - 6\lambda + 1)$)
was classified as class~G in earlier versions of the depth
table.  This was wrong.

\begin{proposition}\label{prop:bc-class-c}
The $bc$ ghost system has shadow depth $r_{\max} = 4$: class~C
(contact/quartic), the same class as $\beta\gamma$.
\end{proposition}

The root cause of the misclassification was AP3 (pattern
completion without recomputation).  The reasoning ``$bc$ is a
single-generator fermionic system, and fermion antisymmetry
kills higher products'' is false.  The $bc$ system has two
generators ($b$ of weight $\lambda$, $c$ of weight $1-\lambda$),
and the shadow class is determined by the two-generator structure,
not by the statistics of either generator alone.  The quartic
shadow $S_4 \neq 0$ for $bc$ at generic $\lambda$, but the
stratum separation mechanism (the same mechanism that terminates
$\beta\gamma$ at arity~$4$) applies: the quartic contact
invariant lives on a charged stratum whose self-bracket exits the
complex by rank-one rigidity.

This correction propagates: wherever the depth table lists $bc$
as class~G, it should read class~C.


\subsection{The four-test boundary}
\label{sec:four-test-boundary}

The modular Koszul machine has a precise interface: four
independent tests that exhaust its proved output.  Beyond
these four, nothing further is known.

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{@{}clc@{}}
\textbf{Test} & \textbf{Statement} & \textbf{Status} \\
\hline
1 & $D_\cA^2 = 0$ & proved (all families, all genera) \\
2 & $\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$ & proved (uniform-weight) \\
3 & $Q_g(\cA) \oplus Q_g(\cA^!) \cong H^*(\overline\cM_g, \cZ)$
  & proved \\
4 & HS-sewing convergence & proved (polynomial growth)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

The four tests are independent.  Multi-weight algebras at
$g \geq 2$ pass tests~1, 3, and~4 but the status of test~2
is open.  This is the precise location of the boundary: a single
test, for a single class of algebras, at genera above~1.

What lies beyond the boundary: multi-weight universality at
$g \geq 2$, the identity $\mathrm{BV}/\mathrm{BRST} = \mathrm{bar}$
at higher genus, and non-perturbative completion.  These are
three distinct problems with no known logical dependencies
between them.


\subsection{Two orthogonal axes}
\label{sec:two-axes}

The MC element $\Theta_\cA$ lives in a bigraded space with
two independent filtrations.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The genus axis} ($g = 0, 1, 2, \ldots$),
controlled by the genus spectral sequence and the sewing
construction.  The genus-$g$ component
$\Theta^{(g)}_\cA \in H^*(\overline\cM_g, \cZ_\cA)$ is
determined inductively by lower genera via the MC equation.
At the scalar level: $F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$.
The genus axis is vertical: higher genus means more topology.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The arity axis} ($r = 2, 3, 4, \ldots$),
controlled by the arity filtration and the shadow Postnikov
tower.  The arity-$r$ component
$\Theta^{(\leq r)}_\cA$ is determined by the MC equation at
arity $\leq r$, with obstruction class
$o_{r+1}(\cA) \in H^2(\Defcyc^{\mathrm{mod}})$.  The arity axis
is horizontal: higher arity means more nonlinearity.

\sep

These two axes are orthogonal.  The scalar shadow $\kappa$
(arity~2) determines $F_g$ at \emph{all} genera: the genus
axis sees only the arity-$2$ projection.  Higher-arity shadows
are invisible at genus~$1$ and become visible at
\[
g_{\min}(S_r) \;=\; \lfloor r/2 \rfloor + 1.
\]
The cubic shadow $S_3$ first appears at genus~$2$.  The quartic
$S_4$ at genus~$3$.  The quintic $S_5$ at genus~$4$.  The arity
axis unfolds as genus increases, but the genus axis does not
unfold as arity increases.

The MC equation couples the two axes: the genus-$g$, arity-$r$
component of $D\Theta + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta, \Theta] = 0$
receives contributions from all $(g', r')$ with $g' \leq g$
and $r' \leq r$.  The coupling is triangular in genus (genus~$g$
depends on genera $< g$) and triangular in arity (arity~$r$
depends on arities $< r$).  Both filtrations are exhaustive, and
their intersection is the origin: $g = 0$, $r = 2$, the
$\lambda$-bracket.  The entire machine is an algebraic induction
from a quartic pole.


\subsection{The free fermion at Heisenberg depth}
\label{sec:free-fermion-heisenberg}

Both the Heisenberg algebra and the free fermion are class~G:
shadow depth $r_{\max} = 2$.  Both terminate at arity~$2$: no
cubic, no quartic, no infinite tower.  The mechanism is
different.

For Heisenberg: the OPE $\alpha(z)\alpha(w) = k/(z-w)^2$ has no
simple pole.  The bar differential extracts only the level (the
double pole), producing the scalar $\kappa = k$.  There is no
Lie bracket to generate higher-arity corrections.

For the free fermion: the OPE $\psi(z)\psi(w) = 1/(z-w)$ has a
simple pole, but the cyclic forms
$\langle \psi, \ldots, \psi \rangle_{\mathrm{cyc}}$ vanish at
arities $\geq 3$ by antisymmetry: cyclic symmetry forces
$\langle \psi^{\otimes n} \rangle_{\mathrm{cyc}} = 0$ for odd~$n$
and sign cancellation kills even~$n$.

The two class~G algebras differ in every other respect:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lcc@{}}
& \textbf{Heisenberg} & \textbf{Free fermion} \\
\hline
Sewing & determinant: $\det(1 - qA)^{-1}$ & Pfaffian \\
Partition function & $\eta(\tau)^{-2k}$ &
  $\theta_\sigma(\tau)/\eta(\tau)$ \\
Spin structure & none & $2^{2g}$ choices at genus~$g$ \\
Bosonisation & $\cF \otimes \cF \cong \cH_1$ &
  $\cH_1 \cong \cF \otimes \cF$ \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

The bosonisation isomorphism $\cF \otimes \cF \cong \cH_1$ is
\emph{not} Koszul duality.  It is a tensor product decomposition
in the category of vertex algebras, not a bar-cobar adjunction.
Koszul duality for the fermion produces $\cF^! \cong \cF$ (the
fermion is quadratically self-dual at $c = 1/2$, the Ising
critical point $M(3,4)$).


\subsection{The modular Koszul triple}
\label{sec:modular-koszul-triple}

The minimal datum from which the entire machine is reconstructed
is a triple
\[
(\cA,\; \cA^!,\; r(z)),
\]
where $r(z) = \Res^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)$ is the
collision $r$-matrix: the binary genus-$0$ projection of the
universal MC element.  Equivalently, $r(z)$ is the image of
$\Theta_\cA$ under the forgetful map from the modular
convolution algebra to the genus-$0$, arity-$2$ component.

DS reduction acts as a functor on triples.  For the principal
reduction $\widehat\fsl_N \to \cW_N$:
\[
\bigl(V_k(\fsl_N),\; V_{k'}(\fsl_N),\; k\,\Omega/z\bigr)
\;\longmapsto\;
\bigl(\cW^k_N,\; \cW^{k'}_N,\; r^{\cW}(z)\bigr).
\]
The ghost sector is the kernel of this functor: the BRST
differential acts as a quotient map on triples, and the ghost
fields generate the kernel ideal.  The functoriality of DS on
triples is the content of the DS-shadow intertwining, verified
computationally to arity~$20$ for $N = 2, \ldots, 5$.

The triple embeds into larger structures by successive
enrichment:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\arabic*),nosep]
\item The \textbf{modular Koszul datum} $\Pi_X(\cA)$: the triple
  plus the factorisation coalgebra $\B_X(\cA)$, the shadow
  tower $\{S_r\}$, and the quartic resonance class $R_4^{\mathrm{mod}}$.
  Six-fold datum.
\item The \textbf{completed modular Koszul datum} $\Pi^{\mathrm{oc}}_X(\cA)$:
  the package plus the chiral derived centre
  $\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ (universal bulk) and
  the annulus trace $\mathrm{Tr}_\cA \simeq HH_*(\cA)$.
  Eight-fold datum.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
The triple is the seed.  The full MC element $\Theta_\cA$ is
the tree that grows from it.


\subsection{$\Theta_\cA$ as protagonist}
\label{sec:theta-protagonist}

The five main theorems are five projections of a single object.
\begin{align*}
\text{Theorem A (adjunction):}\qquad
  & \bD_{\Ran}(\B(\cA)) \simeq \B(\cA^!)
    \quad\Longleftarrow\quad
    \Theta_\cA \in \MC(\gAmod) \\
\text{Theorem B (inversion):}\qquad
  & \Omega(\B(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA
    \quad\Longleftarrow\quad
    \Theta_\cA \text{ bar-intrinsic} \\
\text{Theorem C (complementarity):}\qquad
  & Q_g \oplus Q_g^!
    \quad\Longleftarrow\quad
    \text{arity-$0$ projection of } \Theta_\cA \\
\text{Theorem D (modular char.):}\qquad
  & \mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g
    \quad\Longleftarrow\quad
    \text{scalar shadow of } \Theta_\cA \\
\text{Theorem H (Hochschild):}\qquad
  & \ChirHoch^*(\cA)
    \quad\Longleftarrow\quad
    \text{tangent complex of } \Theta_\cA
\end{align*}

The MC element is defined as $\Theta_\cA := D_\cA - d_0$,
where $D_\cA$ is the full bar differential and $d_0$ is the
genus-$0$ collision differential.  It is MC because
$D_\cA^2 = 0$.  The shadow Postnikov obstruction tower consists of
finite-order projections $\Theta_\cA^{(\leq r)}$.  The full
element lives in the completed modular convolution algebra
$\gAmod = \Convstr(\cC^!_{\mathrm{ch}}, \cA)$.

In the open/closed framework, $\Theta_\cA$ is the
\emph{closed projection} of the full open/closed MC element
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}} = \Theta_\cA + \sum \mu^{M_j}$,
where the $\mu^{M_j}$ are open-sector operations.  The
primitive object is the open-sector factorisation
dg-category~$\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$; the boundary algebra
$\cA_b = \operatorname{End}(b)$ is a Morita-dependent chart;
the bulk is the chiral derived centre
$\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$.  The bar complex
classifies twisting morphisms (couplings between $\cA$ and
$\cA^!$); the derived centre classifies bulk operators acting
on the boundary.  These are different functors applied to the
same seed.


\subsection{The corrected Picard--Fuchs equation}
\label{sec:corrected-picard-fuchs}

The shadow connection $\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}} = d - Q_L'/(2Q_L)\,dt$
has flat sections $f(t) = C\sqrt{Q_L(t)}$.  The flatness
condition $\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}} f = 0$ is
\[
f' \;=\; \frac{Q_L'}{2Q_L}\, f.
\]
Differentiating and eliminating $f$ via the first-order equation
gives the second-order ODE satisfied by the flat sections:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:picard-fuchs-corrected}
2Q_L\, f'' + Q_L'\, f' - Q_L''\, f \;=\; 0.
\end{equation}
This corrects an earlier version that stated the equation as
$Q_L f'' + \tfrac{1}{2}Q_L' f' = 0$ (which omits the
$Q_L'' f$ term and has the wrong coefficient on~$f''$).  The
correct derivation: from $2Q_L f' = Q_L' f$, differentiate
to get $2Q_L f'' + 2Q_L' f' = Q_L'' f + Q_L' f'$, hence
$2Q_L f'' + Q_L' f' - Q_L'' f = 0$.

The equation has regular singular points at the zeros of $Q_L$
(the branch points of the shadow extension).  The local exponents
at each zero are $0$ and $1/2$: the flat section $\sqrt{Q_L}$
has a square-root branch point, and the second solution is
regular.  The monodromy around each singular point is $-1$: the
Koszul sign.


% ============================================================
\section{The Koszul--Epstein frontier}
\label{sec:koszul-epstein-frontier}
% ============================================================

The shadow obstruction tower of a modular Koszul algebra~$\cA$ produces
numerical invariants~$\{S_r(\cA)\}_{r \ge 2}$ that, through the
graph sum and the Rankin--Selberg integral, determine a regularised
two-variable $L$-object $L_\cA(s,u)$.  In
the lattice (Euler--Koszul) corner, this object is a product of
standard $L$-functions; for Virasoro and principal~$W_N$, it
acquires a finite Miura defect.  The question is whether the
algebraic structure of the Maurer--Cartan element~$\Theta_\cA$
constrains the analytic properties of~$L_\cA$ beyond what is
already known from automorphic spectral theory.  This section
records the definitive assessment after a full Beilinson pass.

\subsection{What is proved}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{MC recursion and Carleman uniqueness.}
The MC equation at arity~$r+1$ imposes a polynomial relation on
the shadow coefficients $\{S_2, \ldots, S_{r+1}\}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc-recursion-moment}).
For $r \ge 2m+2$ (where $m$ is the number of spectral atoms),
the system is overdetermined
(Proposition~\ref{prop:mc-constraint-counting}).
The Carleman condition holds
(Proposition~\ref{prop:carleman-virasoro}):
$\sum |S_r|^{-1/(2r)} = \infty$.
Therefore the Hamburger moment problem has a unique solution:
the spectral measure~$\rho$ is uniquely determined by finitely
many parameters $(\kappa, \alpha, S_4)$.

\item \emph{Route~C prime-locality.}
If the low-arity shadow data $(\kappa, \alpha)$ are determined
by Hecke-equivariant character data, then the MC recursion
propagates Hecke equivariance to all arities
(Theorem~\ref{thm:route-c-propagation}).
This is proved for the entire standard landscape
(Corollary~\ref{cor:route-c-standard-landscape}).

\item \emph{Shadow--spectral correspondence for lattice VOAs.}
Shadow depth equals the number of critical lines minus one
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-spectral-correspondence}).

\item \emph{Verdier--Hecke commutation.}
At self-dual points ($c = 13$ for Virasoro), Verdier duality
commutes with Hecke operators, forcing the constrained Epstein
zeta to factor into standard $L$-functions
(Theorem~\ref{thm:hecke-verdier-commutation}).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{What is false and dismissed}

Seven false ideas, each identified during the Beilinson pass on
the research programme (raeeznotes105), are now permanently
dismissed.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{``Bar--cobar forces Epstein zeros onto the critical
line.''} False.  Davenport--Heilbronn counterexamples exist for
generic Epstein zeta functions of non-unimodular lattices
($h(D) \ge 2$).  Bar--cobar provides homotopy equivalence, not
arithmetic positivity.

\item \emph{``The MC equation implies Li positivity.''}  False.
The MC equation is a flatness condition (quadratic consistency).
Li positivity is a sign-definiteness condition.  The
Rankin--Selberg transform connecting them is not
sign-preserving: the Mellin transform of a positive function
can be negative.

\item \emph{``The shadow obstruction tower descends to a functional equation
of~$S_\cA(u)$.''}  False.  The shadow obstruction tower acts on the arity
variable~$t$; the sewing lift acts on the spectral
variable~$u$.  The complementarity identities
$\kappa + \kappa' = 13$ are algebraic constraints in~$c$,
orthogonal to the $u$-variable analytic structure.  The function
$S_\cA(u)$ depends only on the conformal weight multiset
$W(\cA) = \{w_i\}$ and is independent of the central
charge~$c$.

\item \emph{``Narain radius variation gives zero-location
leverage.''}  False.  Varying the radius changes the
coefficient factor, not the zero locations.

\item \emph{``The $\zeta$-proxy is a valid test.''}  False.
The proxy does not preserve the safe point $\sigma = 1/2$.

\item \emph{``Bare spectral measures close the quartic gap.''}
False.  The mismatch for Liouville and $A_2$-Toda is four to
five orders of magnitude.  The crossing-weighted bilinear
residue kernel (involving the actual DOZZ/Toda structure
constants and the modular transform kernel) is required.

\item \emph{``The Li coefficients for the Heisenberg sewing lift
are all positive.''}  False.  The completed Li coefficients
turn negative at $n = 974$, driven by the exponential growth
of contributions from zeros on $\Re = -1/2$.  The uncompleted
Li coefficients turn negative at $n = 7$.  Both failures are
structural consequences of the two-critical-line architecture
of $\zeta(u)\zeta(u+1)$, not evidence against the Riemann
hypothesis.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{The structural obstruction}

The shadow spectral measure~$\rho$ (atoms at effective
couplings~$\lambda_i$ of the MC element~$\Theta_\cA$) and the
automorphic spectral measure (Maass eigenvalues, scattering
poles of the Laplacian on
$\mathrm{SL}(2,\bZ)\backslash\mathfrak{H}$) are different
objects (Remark~\ref{rem:moment-problem-vs-zero-location}).
The map from~$\rho$ to the automorphic spectrum goes through
the Rankin--Selberg integral.  This map is injective for
lattice VOAs but ill-conditioned for non-lattice theories.
The structural obstruction
(Remark~\ref{rem:structural-obstruction}) is that this map is
not surjective: the shadow spectral measure does not determine
the automorphic spectral measure on the moduli space.  In
particular, the MC equation constrains data on the real spectral
axis, while the zeta zeros live at complex spectral parameters.

\subsection{Honest status}

The Koszul--Epstein programme produced genuine arithmetic results
about the shadow obstruction tower: Carleman uniqueness, Route~C
prime-locality, the shadow--spectral correspondence.
These results stand on their own mathematical merit.  They
illuminate the arithmetic structure of modular Koszul algebras.

The programme did not produce, and cannot produce in its current
form, a critical-line theorem or a positivity result.  The gap
between the algebraic content (MC flatness, moment determination,
Hecke propagation) and the analytic conclusion (zero location,
sign definiteness) remains unbridged.  No mechanism for
positivity has been identified.  No construction of the
conjectured modular surface with the required polarisation
exists.

The correct statement of the surviving programme is:
\emph{the MC element~$\Theta_\cA$, through the graph sum and
Rankin--Selberg integral, determines a regularised two-variable
$L$-object~$L_\cA(s,u)$ whose quartic resonance section is the
first nonlinear place where Koszul duality constrains the
automorphic spectral decomposition beyond the character level.
Whether this constraint carries critical-line or positivity
information is open, with no positive evidence and no definitive
obstruction.}


% ============================================================
\section{The spectral question}
\label{sec:spectral-question}
% ============================================================

The constrained Epstein series
\begin{equation}\label{eq:constrained-epstein-def}
\varepsilon^c_s(\cA)
\;=\;
\sum_{\Delta \in \mathrm{Spec}_{\mathrm{sc}}(\cA)} (2\Delta)^{-s},
\end{equation}
where the sum runs over scalar primary dimensions
$\Delta$ with multiplicity, is the genus-one spectral invariant
that couples to the scattering resonances of $\mathrm{SL}(2,\bZ)
\backslash\mathfrak{H}$.  It is the Eisenstein spectral coefficient
of the primary-counting function $\hat Z^c(\tau)
= y^{c/2}\,|\eta(\tau)|^{2c}\,Z(\tau,\bar\tau)$.
The question of this section: does the bar construction see this
object?  The answer is structured.  Five partial constructions
each capture a projection; none captures the full spectrum; the
gap is structural; and the deepest proposed identification is
false.

\subsection{Five partial captures}

\paragraph{(i) Zhu's algebra.}
Zhu's algebra $A(V)$ captures the weight-$0$ structure of the
representation category.  For $V = V_c$ (universal Virasoro):
$A(V_c) \cong \C[x]$, polynomial in $[\omega]$.  The simple
modules of $A(V_c)$ correspond to highest-weight representations,
and the augmentation ideal encodes the ground-state structure.
But $A(V)$ sees only the weight-$0$ part of the category: the
lowest weights $\Delta$ of simple modules, not the full
primary spectrum at arbitrary conformal weight.  Higher Zhu
algebras $A_n(V)$ extend the reach to weight~$n$, but no single
$A_n$ captures the entire tower.  The Zhu filtration gives a
spectral sequence $E_2 = \mathrm{Ext}^*_{A(V)}(\C,\C)
\Rightarrow H^*(B(V))$ at weight~$0$, but it does not extend
to a full spectral sequence in weight.  \emph{Partial:
captures the set of lowest weights $\{\Delta_0\}$, not the
multiplicities or the higher spectrum.}

\paragraph{(ii) Associated variety.}
The associated variety $X_V = \mathrm{Specm}(R_V)$ of the Zhu
$C_2$-algebra $R_V = V/C_2(V)$ captures the singular support
of~$V$.  For affine Kac--Moody at non-critical level:
$X_{V_k(\fg)} = \overline{\cO}$, the closure of a nilpotent
orbit (Arakawa).  For Virasoro: $X_{V_c} = \C$.  The
associated variety controls the \emph{asymptotic} growth of
the character (Arakawa--Kawasetsu): $\chi_V(q) \sim
q^{-c/24}\,(1-q)^{-\dim X_V}$ as $q \to 1$.  This gives
the leading Weyl-type asymptotics of the primary-counting
function, hence the leading pole of $\varepsilon^c_s$ at
$s = c/2$.  But it captures only the leading asymptotics, not
the full Dirichlet series.  \emph{Partial: captures the growth
rate $\dim X_V$ and the leading pole.}

\paragraph{(iii) Bar cohomology.}
For a chirally Koszul algebra~$\cA$, the bar cohomology
$H^*(B(\cA))$ is concentrated in bar degree~$1$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-equivalences-meta}, item~(i)).
The graded dimension $\dim H^1(B(\cA))_h$ at conformal
weight~$h$ counts the generators of the Koszul dual
algebra~$\cA^!$ at weight~$h$:
\[
\dim H^1(B(\cA))_h \;=\; \dim (\cA^!)_h.
\]
For the Virasoro algebra: $\dim H^1(B(\mathrm{Vir}))_2 = 1$
(the generator~$T$), $\dim H^1(B(\mathrm{Vir}))_3 = 0$,
$\dim H^1(B(\mathrm{Vir}))_4 = 1$, and in general the
dimensions are given by the Motzkin difference formula
$M(h+1) - M(h)$.  These dimensions are \emph{independent of
the central charge}~$c$ (the Lie bracket on $\mathrm{Vir}_-
= \bigoplus_{n \geq 2} \C\,L_{-n}$ has no central extension:
$[L_{-m}, L_{-n}] = (n{-}m)\,L_{-m-n}$ with
$\delta_{m+n,0} = 0$ for $m,n \geq 2$).

The quasi-primary count at weight~$h$ is a \emph{different}
sequence.  For the universal Virasoro vacuum module:
\[
d_{\mathrm{qp}}(h)
\;=\; p_{\geq 2}(h) - p_{\geq 2}(h{-}1),
\]
the number of states at weight~$h$ minus the number of
$L_{-1}$-descendants (partitions of $h$ into parts $\geq 2$
minus partitions of $h{-}1$ into parts $\geq 2$).  This
sequence is $0, 1, 0, 1, 1, 1, 2, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 9, \ldots$
The bar cohomology dimensions $\dim H^1(B(\mathrm{Vir}))_h$
are $0, 1, 0, 1, 0, 2, 0, 5, 0, 12, 0, 30, \ldots$
(Motzkin differences), which are supported on even weights
and grow as $3^h/(h\sqrt{\pi h})$.  These two sequences do
not agree.

\emph{Bar cohomology captures the Koszul dual, not the
primary spectrum.}

\paragraph{(iv) Conformal blocks.}
The space of conformal blocks
$\cV(\Sigma_{g,n}; V_1, \ldots, V_n)$ for a vertex
algebra~$V$ on a genus-$g$ surface with $n$ insertions is the
coinvariant space $V_1 \otimes \cdots \otimes V_n /
(\text{holomorphic sections of } V \otimes \omega_\Sigma)$.
At genus~$1$ with no insertions, the conformal block is the
character $\chi_V(\tau) = \mathrm{tr}_{V}\, q^{L_0 - c/24}$.
The primary-counting function $\hat Z^c$ is constructed from
this character by stripping the Casimir factor.  So the
genus-$1$ conformal block \emph{does} capture the full spectrum
(it is the generating function of the spectrum).  But conformal
blocks are not invariants of the bar complex: they depend on
the surface, the insertions, and the full representation theory
of~$V$, which the bar construction does not control.
\emph{Full capture at genus~$1$, but external to the bar
machine.}

\paragraph{(v) Shadow obstruction tower.}
The shadow obstruction tower $\{S_r\}_{r \geq 2}$ is an arity-varying,
genus-$0$ invariant determined by three OPE numbers
$(\kappa, \alpha, S_4)$.  The constrained Epstein
$\varepsilon^c_s$ is a weight-varying, genus-$1$ invariant
determined by the full scalar primary spectrum (an infinite
sequence).  The shadow obstruction tower determines a shadow-metric
Epstein zeta $\varepsilon_{Q_L}(s)$ (a binary quadratic form
zeta), which is a \emph{different} object from the constrained
Epstein $\varepsilon^c_s$.  The relationship is a chain of
projections:
\[
\text{full CFT data}
\;\xrightarrow{\text{primary spectrum}}\;
\varepsilon^c_s
\;\xrightarrow[\text{(information loss)}]{\text{low moments}}\;
\varepsilon_{Q_L}
\;\xrightarrow{\text{Taylor coeff.}}\;
\{S_r\}.
\]
The shadow obstruction tower sees the quadratic approximation to the spectral
data.  For lattice VOAs, the shadow--spectral correspondence
recovers the full $L$-function package.  For non-lattice
algebras, the projection loses infinitely many degrees of
freedom.  \emph{Partial: captures three moments of the spectral
data.}

\subsection{The gap: shadow versus spectrum}

The shadow obstruction tower lives on the genus-$0$ side of the bar complex
(the MC element $\Theta_\cA$ is a graph sum over planted trees
on the disc, with arity~$r$ counting the number of boundary
insertions).  The constrained Epstein lives on the genus-$1$
side (the partition function $Z(\tau,\bar\tau)$ is a trace over
the vacuum module, which is a genus-$1$ datum).

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
& \textbf{Shadow obstruction tower} & \textbf{Constrained Epstein} \\
\hline
Genus & $0$ & $1$ \\
Variable & Arity $r$ & Weight $h$ \\
Parameters & $3$ ($\kappa, \alpha, S_4$) & $\infty$ ($\{\Delta_i, m_i\}$) \\
Functional equation & Complementarity ($c \to 26-c$) & Modular ($s \to c/2+1-s$) \\
$c$-dependence & Rational in $c$ & Transcendental in $c$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The shadow obstruction tower and the constrained Epstein are related by the
same chiral algebra, but they extract different projections.
Neither determines the other.  The shadow obstruction tower is
determined by three numbers; the constrained Epstein encodes
infinitely many independent primary dimensions.

\subsection{The deepest question: is $\varepsilon^c_s
= \sum H^1(B(V))_h \cdot (2h)^{-s}$?}

\begin{proposition}[Bar cohomology $\neq$ quasi-primary count]
\label{prop:bar-neq-quasiprimary}
The Dirichlet series
$\sum_{h \geq 2} \dim H^1(B(\cA))_h \cdot (2h)^{-s}$
is \emph{not} the constrained Epstein zeta
$\varepsilon^c_s(\cA)$, for any chirally Koszul
algebra~$\cA$ with more than one generator.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Two independent obstructions.

\textbf{(a) Different sequences.}
For the Virasoro algebra: $\dim H^1(B(\mathrm{Vir}))_h$ is the
Motzkin difference $M(h+1) - M(h)$, which vanishes at all odd
weights and is independent of~$c$.  The quasi-primary count
$d_{\mathrm{qp}}(h) = p_{\geq 2}(h) - p_{\geq 2}(h-1)$ is
nonzero at odd weights ($d_{\mathrm{qp}}(5) = 1$,
$d_{\mathrm{qp}}(7) = 2$) and also independent of~$c$ for the
universal Virasoro.  These are different sequences.

At weight~$5$: $\dim H^1(B(\mathrm{Vir}))_5 = 0$,
$d_{\mathrm{qp}}(5) = 1$.  The bar cohomology misses the
quasi-primary at weight~$5$ because the Koszul dual $\mathrm{Vir}^!$
has no generator at weight~$5$ (the dual algebra has generators
only at even weights, by the parity of the Virasoro bracket).

\textbf{(b) The bar construction sees the Koszul dual, not
the original.}
By the Koszul property,
$H^1(B(\cA))_h \cong (\cA^!)_h^{\mathrm{gen}}$: bar cohomology
in degree~$1$ counts generators of the \emph{dual} algebra, not
quasi-primaries of the \emph{original}.  For Kac--Moody:
$\dim H^1(B(\hat\fg))_1 = \dim\fg$ (the dual has $\dim\fg$
generators at weight~$1$), while the quasi-primary count at
weight~$1$ is also $\dim\fg$ (the currents $J^a$).  The
coincidence at weight~$1$ is a consequence of the KM algebra
being generated in weight~$1$, so the generators of $\cA$ and the
generators of $\cA^!$ both live at weight~$1$.  For Virasoro,
with a weight-$2$ generator, the sequences diverge starting at
weight~$4$.

The constrained Epstein $\varepsilon^c_s$ sums over primary
dimensions of the \emph{original} algebra~$\cA$ (with
multiplicity, over all representations appearing in the
partition function).  Bar cohomology counts states of the
\emph{Koszul dual}~$\cA^!$.  These are different algebras
(unless $\cA$ is self-dual at $c = 13$), and even at $c = 13$
the quasi-primary count is not the bar cohomology dimension.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why the identification is tempting]
\label{rem:spectral-temptation}
For free-field algebras (Heisenberg, free fermion), the
quasi-primary count at weight~$h$ equals the bar cohomology
dimension at weight~$h$, because the algebra is \emph{generated}
by a weight-$1$ field and the Koszul dual is the symmetric/exterior
algebra on the same space.  The coincidence is a special-case
phenomenon (AP3): it holds when the algebra is both free and
generated in weight~$1$, which forces the Koszul dual to have
the same Hilbert series as the quasi-primary tower.  For
algebras with generators of weight $\geq 2$, the Koszul dual's
weight distribution diverges from the quasi-primary distribution.
\end{remark}

\subsection{What does capture the full spectrum?}

No single object in the bar-cobar machine captures the full
primary spectrum.  The spectrum is an invariant of the
\emph{representation category} $\cA\text{-}\mathrm{mod}$, not
of the algebra $\cA$ alone.  The bar complex $B(\cA)$ is built
from the algebra (the vacuum module), not from its modules.  The
partition function $Z(\tau,\bar\tau)$, which encodes the full
spectrum, requires the \emph{category of modules} together with
a modular-invariant pairing on characters.

\begin{observation}[The categorical gap]
\label{obs:categorical-gap}
The bar construction is a functor from chiral algebras to
factorisation coalgebras.  The primary spectrum is a function
from the \emph{representation category} to Dirichlet series.
These have different domains.  The bar complex sees the
algebra; the spectrum sees the category.

For rational VOAs, Zhu's correspondence provides a bridge:
the simple modules of $A(V)$ biject with simple modules
of~$V$, so the set of primary dimensions~$\{\Delta_i\}$ is
determined by $A(V)$.  But the multiplicities in the partition
function are determined by the modular $S$-matrix, which is
categorical data (the braiding of the modular tensor category
$V\text{-}\mathrm{mod}$), not algebra data.
\end{observation}

The genus-$1$ factorisation homology $\int_{E_\tau} \cA$
is a single object that sees both the algebra and the genus-$1$
categorical data: it computes the character (via the trace over
the vacuum representation) and thereby encodes the full
primary spectrum.  But it is a genus-$1$ object, not a genus-$0$
object, and it is not a projection of the MC element
$\Theta_\cA$ (which lives at genus~$0$).  The genus-$1$
amplitude $F_1(\cA) = \kappa(\cA)/24$ is the \emph{integrated}
form of this datum: one number extracted from the full partition
function.  The rest of the partition function (the full Fourier
expansion in~$q$) is inaccessible to the shadow obstruction tower.

\subsection{The single object that sees both}

The full modular Koszul datum
\[
\bigl(\cA,\; B(\cA),\; \Theta_\cA,\;
\cA\text{-}\mathrm{mod}^{\mathrm{ss}},\;
Z(\tau,\bar\tau)\bigr)
\]
sees both the shadow data (from $\Theta_\cA$) and the spectral
data (from $Z$).  But this is the \emph{entire theory}, not a
single mathematical object.  The question was whether a single
object captures both.  The answer: the partition function
$Z(\tau,\bar\tau)$ captures the spectral data by definition,
and it determines the shadow data (by extracting OPE coefficients
from the $q$-expansion).  The reverse is false: the shadow data
does not determine the partition function.

This asymmetry is structural.  The partition function encodes
the full genus-$1$ trace, which involves all states of the
algebra at all weights.  The shadow obstruction tower encodes three OPE
coefficients extracted from genus-$0$ collision residues.  The
genus-$1$ object is strictly richer.

For the Koszul--Epstein programme, the implication is decisive:
the constrained Epstein $\varepsilon^c_s$ cannot be recovered
from the bar complex alone.  It requires the partition function,
which is external to the bar construction.  The bar complex
provides the \emph{algebraic} constraints on $\varepsilon^c_s$
(the MC equation, the shadow obstruction tower, the depth classification),
but not the \emph{spectral} content (the primary dimensions and
multiplicities).

\subsection{Summary}

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lccl@{}}
\textbf{Construction} & \textbf{Captures spectrum?} & \textbf{Bar-internal?}
  & \textbf{What it sees} \\
\hline
Zhu's algebra $A(V)$ & Partially (weight $0$)
  & No (Zhu $\neq$ bar) & Lowest weights \\
Associated variety $X_V$ & Partially (asymptotics)
  & No & Growth rate \\
Bar cohomology $H^*(B)$ & No (Koszul dual)
  & Yes & Generators of $\cA^!$ \\
Conformal blocks & Fully (genus $1$)
  & No & Full primary spectrum \\
Shadow obstruction tower & Partially ($3$ moments)
  & Yes (from $\Theta_\cA$) & $\kappa, \alpha, S_4$ \\
Factorisation homology & Fully (genus $1$)
  & No (requires trace) & Full partition function
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

The bar complex is the algebraic engine.  The primary spectrum
is the analytic output.  The two are connected by the
representation category, which the bar complex constrains but
does not determine.  A smaller true theorem: the bar complex
determines the Koszul dual and the shadow obstruction tower, which together
give three constraints on the spectrum.  A larger false theorem:
the bar complex determines the full spectrum.


% ============================================================
\section{Algebraic integration and the spectral question}
\label{sec:algebraic-integration-spectral}
% ============================================================

The naive claim that ``integration over moduli space is analytic,
not algebraic'' is false.  The bar complex defines a sheaf on
$\overline{\cM}_g$ whose algebraic invariants are nontrivial
and proved.  But the deeper question, whether these algebraic
invariants capture the primary spectrum, has a structured answer
that is neither trivially positive nor trivially negative.

\subsection{What is algebraically available}

The manuscript already constructs three algebraic objects from
the bar complex over moduli space:

\paragraph{(1) The virtual bar $K$-class.}
$V_\cA := [R\pi_{g*}\,\barB^{(g)}_X(\cA)] \in K^0(\overline{\cM}_g)$
(Definition~\ref{def:virtual-bar-k-class}).  This is the
derived pushforward of the bar complex along the universal curve
$\pi_g\colon \overline{\cC}_g \to \overline{\cM}_g$.  By the
perfectness criterion (Lemma~\ref{lem:perfectness-criterion}:
Koszul acyclicity + finite-dimensional fiber cohomology
$\Rightarrow$ perfect complex), this is well-defined in the
bounded derived category $D^b(\overline{\cM}_g)$.

\paragraph{(2) The center sheaf.}
$\cZ_\cA := R^*\pi_{g*}(\barB^{(g)}_X(\cA), \dfib) \in
\mathrm{Loc}(\overline{\cM}_g)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-homology-recovery}(ii)).
Its fiber over $[\Sigma_g]$ is the chiral homology
$H^{\mathrm{ch}}_*(\Sigma_g, \cA)$.  This is a local system
carrying a flat Gauss--Manin connection.

\paragraph{(3) The ambient complementarity complex.}
$C_g(\cA) = R\Gamma(\overline{\cM}_g, \cZ_\cA)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-homology-recovery}(iii)).
This is the derived global sections of the center sheaf:
a purely algebraic operation on a coherent/constructible sheaf
on a proper Deligne--Mumford stack.

\paragraph{(4) The GRR computation.}
By Grothendieck--Riemann--Roch on the universal curve
(Proposition~\ref{prop:characteristic-hierarchy}):
\[
c_1(\det V_\cA) = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda,
\qquad
\mathrm{ch}(V_\cA) \leftrightarrow \Delta_\cA(x),
\qquad
\mathrm{Hol}(V_\cA) = \Pi_\cA.
\]
These are the scalar level (the modular characteristic $\kappa$),
the spectral level (the discriminant $\Delta$), and the
holonomy level (the periodicity profile $\Pi$).  All three
are computed algebraically from the $K$-class $V_\cA$.

\medskip

So the bar complex \emph{does} define a sheaf on~$\overline{\cM}_g$
whose $R\Gamma$ is computable.  The derived global sections, the
Chern character, the monodromy representation---all of these are
algebraic operations on algebraic objects.  The statement
``integration over moduli space is analytic, not algebraic'' is
a false idea in the Beilinson sense.  Derived global sections
$R\Gamma(\overline{\cM}_g, \cZ_\cA)$ \emph{is} algebraic
integration, and it produces the ambient complementarity complex,
which is a proved algebraic invariant.

\subsection{What $R\Gamma$ does not capture}

The question now becomes precise: does $R\Gamma(\overline{\cM}_g,
\cZ_\cA)$ capture the primary spectrum?

The answer is \textbf{no}, and the obstruction is not
``analysis vs.\ algebra'' but something deeper: the bar
complex is built from the \emph{vacuum module's OPE data},
not from the representation category.

\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item \emph{The sheaf $\cZ_\cA$ is an algebra invariant.}
  The center sheaf $\cZ_\cA$ is functorial in morphisms of
  chiral algebras.  Its fiber $H^{\mathrm{ch}}_*(\Sigma_g, \cA)$
  depends only on the algebra~$\cA$ and the curve~$\Sigma_g$,
  not on the category $\cA\text{-}\mathrm{mod}$ or the modular
  invariant.

\item \emph{The primary spectrum is a categorical invariant.}
  Two non-isomorphic modular-invariant partition functions for
  the same chiral algebra produce different constrained Epstein
  series but the same center sheaf $\cZ_\cA$.  Example: the
  $D$-type and $E$-type modular invariants for
  $\widehat{\mathfrak{su}(2)}_k$ at $k \geq 10$ (Cappelli--Itzykson--Zuber)
  have the same bar complex but different primary spectra.

\item \emph{The partition function is a trace, not a global section.}
  The character $\chi_V(\tau) = \mathrm{tr}_V\, q^{L_0 - c/24}$
  is a \emph{trace} over a module, not a derived global section
  of a sheaf on $\overline{\cM}_g$.  The genus-$1$ factorization
  homology $\int_{E_\tau} \cA$ computes this trace, but it
  depends on the genus-$1$ curve $E_\tau$ (hence on $\tau$) and
  produces a function on $\mathcal{M}_{1,1}$, not a single
  cohomology class.  The \emph{integrated} invariant
  $F_1(\cA) = \kappa(\cA)/24$ is the single number obtained by
  extracting the leading Hodge class from~$R\Gamma$; the full
  partition function (the $q$-expansion) is not captured by
  $R\Gamma$ of the center sheaf.

\item \emph{The GRR hierarchy is strictly coarser than the spectrum.}
  The three-level hierarchy $\kappa \to \Delta \to \Pi$ captures:
  (L1)~one number ($\kappa$),
  (L2)~the bar cohomology dimensions at all weights (the
  Koszul dual's Hilbert series), and
  (L3)~the monodromy of the bar cohomology local system.
  None of these is the primary spectrum.  The bar cohomology
  dimensions count generators of~$\cA^!$, not primaries of~$\cA$
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:bar-neq-quasiprimary}).  The monodromy
  of $\cZ_\cA$ encodes the action of
  $\mathrm{MCG}(\Sigma_g)$ on chiral homology, which is the
  Hitchin/KZ connection---an invariant of the algebra, not of its
  module category.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{The precise obstruction}

The obstruction to recovering the spectrum from $R\Gamma$ is not
``analysis vs.\ algebra.''  It is the distinction between two
algebraic categories:

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
& \textbf{Algebra invariants} & \textbf{Categorical invariants} \\
\hline
Input & $\cA$ (the chiral algebra) & $(\cA\text{-}\mathrm{mod}, M_{ij})$ \\
Construction & $B(\cA)$ (bar complex) & partition function $Z(\tau,\bar\tau)$ \\
Sheaf on $\overline{\cM}_g$ & $\cZ_\cA$ (center sheaf) & conformal blocks $\cV_{g,n}$ \\
$R\Gamma$ & $C_g(\cA)$ (complementarity) & $\chi_V(\tau)$ (character) \\
GRR output & $\kappa \cdot \lambda$ & $\sum m_i \chi_i(\tau)\overline{\chi_j(\tau)}$ \\
Information & Finitely many invariants & Infinitely many primary dims
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip

The right column requires the module category and a modular
invariant as additional input.  No algebraic operation on the
\emph{left column} can produce the \emph{right column}, because
the domain is strictly smaller.  This is a theorem
(Proposition~\ref{prop:constrained-epstein-not-bar}), not a
limitation of current technology.

\subsection{What would bridge the gap}

Three constructions could, in principle, extend the bar complex's
reach toward the spectrum:

\paragraph{(a) The module bar construction with all modules.}
The module bar complex
$\barB_\cA(\cM)$ for a chiral module $\cM$ produces a comodule
over $\barB(\cA)$
(Chapter~\ref{chap:chiral-modules}).  If one applies the bar
construction to \emph{every} simple module $L_i$ of~$\cA$, one
obtains a family of comodules $\{\barB_\cA(L_i)\}_{i \in I}$
whose $K$-classes
$[R\pi_{g*}\, \barB_\cA(L_i)] \in K^0(\overline{\cM}_g)$
carry the conformal dimension $h_i$ in their Chern character
(the fiber Euler characteristic is $\chi(L_i) = q^{h_i - c/24}
\prod (1-q^n)^{-1}$).  Summing with the modular invariant
multiplicities:
\[
\sum_{i,j} M_{ij}\,\mathrm{ch}\bigl(
R\pi_{1*}\, \barB_\cA(L_i)\bigr)
\cdot \overline{\mathrm{ch}(R\pi_{1*}\, \barB_\cA(L_j))}
\]
would recover the partition function at genus~$1$, and hence the
primary spectrum.  But this construction takes $\cA\text{-}\mathrm{mod}$
and $M_{ij}$ as \emph{input}, not output; it does not extract the
spectrum from the bar complex alone.

\paragraph{(b) The factorization homology sheaf as a $D$-module.}
The factorization homology $\int_X \cA$, viewed as a function of
$X \in \cM_g$, defines a $D$-module on~$\cM_g$ (the conformal blocks
local system with its flat connection).  The \emph{spectral data of
this $D$-module}---its characteristic variety, monodromy, and
irregular singular structure---is an algebraic invariant that encodes
more than $R\Gamma$ of the center sheaf.  For integrable affine
Kac--Moody algebras, this $D$-module is the Hitchin connection
on the Verlinde bundle, and its monodromy recovers the modular
$S$-matrix (hence the fusion rules, hence the primary dimensions
via the Verlinde formula).  Whether a similar construction works
for non-rational algebras (Virasoro at generic~$c$) is open:
the conformal blocks local system has irregular singularities
along the boundary of~$\overline{\cM}_g$, and the spectral
theory of such irregular $D$-modules is a frontier topic
(Boalch, Sabbah, Mochizuki).

\paragraph{(c) A motivic spectral zeta.}
A construction
$\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}_V(s) := \sum_i [L_i] \cdot
(L_0|_{L_i})^{-s} \in K_0(\cA\text{-}\mathrm{mod})
\otimes \C$
would categorify the constrained Epstein series.  For rational
VOAs this reduces to a finite sum; for irrational VOAs it requires
a continuous $K$-theory with weight topology.  The functional
equation would come from the modular tensor category structure
(the $S$-matrix as categorical Frobenius).  No such construction
exists.  The structural obstruction: the spectral decomposition on
$\mathrm{SL}(2,\Z)\backslash\mathfrak{H}$ uses the hyperbolic
Laplacian, which is a real-analytic operator without algebraic
meaning.  A categorical/motivic version would require categorifying
the Roelcke--Selberg decomposition---a problem at the frontier
of geometric Langlands.

\subsection{Beilinson verdict}

The claim ``the bar complex cannot see the spectrum because
integration over moduli space is analytic'' was a false idea.
The corrected diagnosis:

\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item The bar complex \emph{does} define a sheaf
  $\cZ_\cA$ on $\overline{\cM}_g$ with well-defined algebraic
  invariants ($R\Gamma$, $\mathrm{ch}$, $\mathrm{Hol}$,
  GRR pushforward).  These invariants are proved and nontrivial.

\item The algebraic invariants of $\cZ_\cA$ capture
  the \emph{algebra's} modular structure ($\kappa$, the bar
  cohomology dimensions, the KZ/Hitchin monodromy), not
  the \emph{module category's} spectral content (the primary
  dimensions and multiplicities).

\item The obstruction is not ``analysis vs.\ algebra''
  but \emph{algebra vs.\ category}: the bar complex is
  functorial in~$\cA$, while the spectrum is functorial in
  $(\cA\text{-}\mathrm{mod}, M_{ij})$.  These are different
  functors with different domains.

\item The ``analytic'' step that is genuinely unavoidable
  is the spectral decomposition on the modular curve
  $\mathrm{SL}(2,\Z)\backslash\mathfrak{H}$
  (Roelcke--Selberg), which maps the partition function
  (a categorical invariant) to the constrained Epstein
  series (an analytic invariant).  This step involves the
  hyperbolic Laplacian and has no known algebraic/categorical
  substitute.  But the partition function
  \emph{itself} is an algebraic invariant of the module
  category (it is a finite sum of characters for rational VOAs,
  determined by the modular tensor category structure).
  The ``analytic'' content resides entirely in the last step:
  from characters to spectral coefficients.

\item Status: \textbf{OPEN} (the algebraic construction
  exists but does not reach the spectrum; the gap is
  algebra-vs-category, not algebra-vs-analysis).
  The precise frontier question is whether the $D$-module
  structure of the conformal blocks local system on~$\cM_g$
  (whose construction is algebraic via Beilinson--Drinfeld)
  has spectral invariants that recover the primary spectrum
  at genus~$1$ without invoking the Roelcke--Selberg
  decomposition.  For rational VOAs with the Hitchin
  connection, the monodromy of this $D$-module \emph{does}
  recover the $S$-matrix, hence the primary dimensions.
  For non-rational VOAs, this is a geometric Langlands
  frontier.
\end{enumerate}

% ============================================================
\section{The real-to-complex frontier}
\label{sec:real-to-complex-frontier}
% ============================================================

The bar complex produces spectral data that is inherently
\emph{real}: the shadow coefficients $S_r(\cA)$ are rational
functions of the central charge~$c$, the MC equation constrains
these coefficients along the real spectral axis, and the
Carleman condition ensures that the resulting moment problem has
a unique solution on the real line.  The zeros of the Riemann
zeta function live at complex spectral parameters.  The central
question of the arithmetic frontier is whether any mathematical
mechanism bridges this gap.

After a complete investigation across eight candidate
approaches, the definitive assessment is as follows.

\subsection{The eight candidates}

\paragraph{1.~Deligne categories.}
The Deligne category $\underline{\mathrm{Rep}}(S_t)$ for
$t \notin \mathbf{Z}_{\ge 0}$ gives a semisimple rigid tensor
category interpolating between representation categories of
symmetric groups.  The idea: the shadow obstruction tower at
non-integer~$c$ lives in a Deligne-type interpolation, and the
analytic continuation in~$c$ might produce complex spectral data.

\emph{Status: dead end.}  The Deligne category is a purely
algebraic interpolation in a \emph{categorical} variable
(the rank of the symmetric group).  It does not produce
analytic continuation in a \emph{spectral} variable (the
Mellin parameter~$s$ of an $L$-function).  The shadow obstruction tower
at non-integer~$c$ is already well-defined by rational
interpolation of the OPE coefficients; no Deligne category is
needed.  The continuation in~$c$ gives a continuation of the
shadow \emph{coefficients} $S_r(c)$, not a continuation of the
sewing Dirichlet series $S_\cA(u)$ off the real spectral axis.
These are different variables parametrising different structures.

\paragraph{2.~Wick rotation / analytic continuation in~$c$.}
Rotate $c$ into the complex plane and study the shadow obstruction tower
at complex~$c$.

\emph{Status: dead end.}  The sewing Dirichlet series
$S_\cA(u) = \zeta(u{+}1)\,(\zeta(u) - H_{w-1}(u))$ is
independent of~$c$.  The central charge enters the shadow obstruction tower
through the OPE structure constants, not through the weight
multiset.  Continuing $c$ to complex values changes the shadow
coefficients $S_r(c)$ but does \emph{not} change $S_\cA(u)$,
which depends only on the conformal weights of the generators.
The two variables are orthogonal: $c$ acts on the arity axis;
$u$ acts on the prime axis.  No rotation in one can reach the
other.

\paragraph{3.~Analytic continuation of the shadow obstruction tower.}
Continue the arity variable~$t$ in the shadow generating
function $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_L(t)}$ to complex values,
obtaining a Riemann surface.

\emph{Status: genuine mathematics, no bridge.}
The shadow generating function is algebraic of degree~$2$
over $\mathbf{Q}(c)(t)$.  Its analytic continuation
produces a branched double cover of the $t$-line, ramified at
the zeros of the shadow metric~$Q_L$.  The Galois group
$\mathrm{Gal}(K_L/F) = \mathbf{Z}/2$ is the Koszul sign.
The branch points determine a quadratic number field at
each rational~$c$ (for instance $\mathbf{Q}(\sqrt{-10})$
for the Ising model).

This is a proved result about the \emph{algebraic} structure
of the shadow obstruction tower.  But the resulting number field lives on
the arity axis, not on the spectral axis.  The discriminant
of~$Q_L$ at a rational specialisation of~$c$ determines a
quadratic Dirichlet $L$-function $L(s, \chi_d)$, which \emph{is}
an object on the spectral axis.  However, this $L$-function is
a classical object from algebraic number theory (determined by
the Legendre symbol); it is not a new $L$-function produced by
the bar construction.  The bridge from the arity axis to the
spectral axis goes through the graph sum, which is an
irreducible intermediary, not an integral transform.

\paragraph{4.~Resonances and the completed bar complex.}
The MC4 resonance-filtered bar-cobar machine
(Theorem~\ref{thm:resonance-filtered-bar-cobar}) produces a
completed bar complex $\hat{B}(\cA)$ with a finite resonance
rank~$\rho(\cA)$.  The resonance data might carry complex
spectral information.

\emph{Status: dead end for zeta zeros.}  The resonance rank
classifies the \emph{algebraic} completion difficulty of the
bar-cobar tower.  For Virasoro, $\rho = 1$ (the curvature
$m_0$ is the single resonance).  The resonance data controls
the convergence of the shadow partition function (the growth
rate $\rho(\cA)$ determines the radius of convergence), which
is a statement about the arity expansion.  It does not
constrain the analytic properties of $L$-functions.  The
completed bar complex solves the MC4 problem (bar-cobar for
non-quadratic infinite-generator algebras), which is a
homological algebra problem, not an analytic number theory
problem.

\paragraph{5.~Borel resummation and resurgence.}
The shadow partition function $Z^{\mathrm{sh}}(\hbar)
= \sum_{g \ge 1} F_g\, \hbar^{2g}$ is convergent for
the scalar (leading $\kappa$) sector.  The string partition
function $\sum F_g (2g)!\, \hbar^{2g}$ is factorially
divergent.  Borel resummation might connect the perturbative
(convergent) shadow series to the non-perturbative (resurgent)
string series.

\emph{Status: genuine mathematics, wrong target.}
Borel resummation applies when a formal power series has
known factorial growth.  The shadow series \emph{converges
absolutely} for $|\hbar| < 2\pi$ (the Bernoulli decay gives
coefficients of order $(2\pi)^{-2g}$, not $(2g)!$).  There is
nothing to resummate.  The Borel transform of the string series
$\sum (2g)!\, \hbar^{2g}$ has a non-trivial Stokes structure
(action singularities on the Borel plane), and the resurgent
trans-series involves non-perturbative effects (D-branes, ZZ
instantons) that are \emph{external} to the bar construction.
The bar complex is the perturbative algebraic engine; it does
not access non-perturbative data.

More precisely: the shadow series captures the
\emph{tautological} genus expansion $F_g = \kappa\,
\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$, which is a polynomial in~$\kappa$
at each genus.  The string partition function involves
the \emph{full} genus expansion including non-tautological
classes on $\overline{\cM}_g$.  These are different objects.
The shadow obstruction tower is the Hodge-tautological projection of the
full amplitude; the non-tautological part is invisible to the
bar complex.

\paragraph{6.~Spectral curves and topological recursion.}
The Eynard--Orantin topological recursion produces a spectral
curve from genus-$0$ data, and the higher-genus amplitudes
$\omega_{g,n}$ are residues on this curve.  The spectral curve
has complex branch points, which might serve as a bridge to
complex spectral data.

\emph{Status: genuine mathematics, not a bridge to zeta zeros.}
The shadow CohFT (Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-cohft}) satisfies
equivariance and splitting.  The flat identity is conditional
(the vacuum $|0\rangle$ must lie in the generating space~$V$).
Without the flat unit, Teleman reconstruction does not apply,
and the shadow CohFT does not arise from a Frobenius manifold
or a spectral curve in the standard sense.

Even with a spectral curve, the relationship to zeta zeros
would require identifying the branch points of the curve with
the zeros of an $L$-function.  No such identification exists.
The spectral curve encodes the genus-$0$ OPE data (the same
three parameters $\kappa, \alpha, S_4$ that determine the
shadow obstruction tower), not the analytic number theory of the partition
function.  The ``spectral'' in ``spectral curve'' refers to the
spectrum of a matrix model, not to the automorphic spectrum.

\paragraph{7.~Non-commutative geometry (Connes--Marcolli).}
The Bost--Connes system produces a quantum statistical
mechanical system whose partition function is $\zeta(s)$,
with the zeta zeros appearing as the KMS states at inverse
temperature~$\beta = s$.  The Connes trace formula approaches
$\mathrm{RH}$ through a Weil-type positivity on a
non-commutative space.

\emph{Status: the most structurally compatible approach, but
no bridge has been constructed.}  The Bost--Connes system has
a Hecke algebra of symmetries that is compatible with the
Verdier--Hecke commutation
(Theorem~\ref{thm:hecke-verdier-commutation}).  The
non-commutative geometry approach replaces the function field
with a non-commutative adele class space, and the Weil
positivity criterion becomes a trace-class condition on a
specific operator.  In principle, the bar complex at the
self-dual point $c = 13$ (where Verdier self-duality gives an
involution on the factorization coalgebra) could feed into the
non-commutative trace formula through the sewing determinant.

In practice, no such construction exists.  The Bost--Connes
system is defined over $\mathbf{Q}$ (the rational numbers as a
number field); the bar complex is defined over $\mathbf{C}$
(complex algebraic curves).  The arithmetic descent from
function fields to number fields (Gap~B in the Langlands
analysis) is the fundamental obstruction, and it applies with
full force here.  The non-commutative geometry approach provides
a framework in which the question could in principle be asked,
but the bar construction does not supply the input data that the
framework requires.

\paragraph{8.~Analytic Langlands.}
The analytic Langlands programme (Etingof--Frenkel--Kazhdan)
studies the spectral decomposition of the Hecke operators on
the space of half-densities on $\mathrm{Bun}_G(X)$ for a
curve~$X$ over $\mathbf{C}$.  The opers (which the bar complex
at critical level computes, Theorem~\ref{thm:oper-bar}) appear
as the spectral side.

\emph{Status: the most mathematically natural connection, but
pertains to the geometric (function-field) Langlands, not the
arithmetic (number-field) Langlands.}  The bar complex at
critical level~$k = -h^\vee$ provides a chain-level model for
the oper side of the geometric Langlands correspondence.
At generic level, the shadow obstruction tower deforms the oper data.
This interpolation across levels is genuinely new and is not
visible in the original Langlands framework.

However, the geometric Langlands programme operates over
function fields (algebraic curves over~$\mathbf{C}$), where the
analogue of the Riemann Hypothesis is Weil's theorem (proved by
Deligne).  The number-field Riemann Hypothesis requires
arithmetic descent, which is the deepest unsolved problem in the
Langlands programme and is not addressed by the bar construction.
The analytic Langlands provides the correct categorical
framework for the oper/shadow interpolation, but it does not
bridge the real-to-complex spectral gap for number-field
$L$-functions.


\subsection{The structural verdict}

Three of the eight approaches produce genuine mathematics
(analytic continuation of the shadow obstruction tower, spectral curves,
analytic Langlands).  The remaining five are dead ends for the
real-to-complex question.  None of the eight bridges the gap
from the bar complex to zeta zeros.

The structural reason is a theorem, not a conjecture.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{The shadow obstruction tower is determined by three numbers.}
The MC equation on a single primary line determines the
infinite shadow obstruction tower from $(\kappa, \alpha, S_4)$.  These
three OPE coefficients are a finite-dimensional algebraic
datum.

\item \emph{The zeros of an $L$-function encode infinitely
many independent quantities.}  The zero set
$\{\rho_n\}$ of $\zeta(s)$ is a countably infinite collection
of complex numbers, each carrying independent transcendental
data (the imaginary parts~$\gamma_n$ are believed to be
algebraically independent).
