\item \emph{No finite-dimensional algebraic structure can
determine the zeros of an entire function of order~$1$.}
This is a consequence of the structure theorem for entire
functions of finite order (Hadamard factorisation):
the zeros determine the function, but finitely many
algebraic constraints on the coefficients cannot determine
the zeros.
\end{enumerate}

The real/complex divide is therefore \textbf{fundamental in
the single-algebra setting}: the bar complex of a fixed chiral
algebra~$\cA$ produces finitely many algebraic invariants
(the shadow coefficients), which cannot determine infinitely
many analytic quantities (the zeta zeros).

\subsection{The bootstrap escape and why it fails}

The single-algebra obstruction suggests a multi-algebra
bootstrap: use the MC constraints from \emph{all} algebras
simultaneously and ask whether the intersection of constraint
loci forces zeros onto the critical line.  This is the content
of the ``simultaneous-family closure'' mechanism.

The bootstrap fails for three independent reasons.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{The sewing Dirichlet series $S_\cA(u)$ is
$c$-independent.}  For all Virasoro algebras at all central
charges, $S_{\mathrm{Vir}}(u) = \zeta(u{+}1)\,(\zeta(u) - 1)$.
Varying~$c$ changes the shadow coefficients but not the
sewing lift.  The bootstrap has no leverage on the spectral
variable~$u$ because all algebras in the family produce the
same~$S_\cA(u)$.

\item \emph{The Rankin--Selberg unfolding erases the MC
structure.}  The unfolded integral depends only on the
Fourier coefficients of the partition function, not on the
convolution-algebraic structure that the MC equation controls
(Proposition~\ref{prop:scattering-residue}).  The MC equation
constrains the coefficients~$c_j$ in the spectral
decomposition $\hat{Z}^c = c_E\, E_k + \sum c_j\, f_j$,
but the $L$-functions $L(s, f_j)$ are properties of the
eigenforms~$f_j$, which are independent of the algebra~$\cA$.

\item \emph{The MC equation is a flatness condition, not a
positivity condition.}  The Li criterion requires positive
definiteness of a specific bilinear form.  The MC equation
$D\Theta + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta, \Theta] = 0$ is a quadratic
integrability condition.  The chain
$\mathrm{MC} \to \mathrm{Rankin\text{-}Selberg}
\to \mathrm{Li\ positivity}$ does not close because the
Rankin--Selberg transform is not sign-preserving.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{The Beilinson verdict}

The following false ideas are dismissed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item ``Bar-cobar homotopy equivalence forces Epstein zeros
onto the critical line.'' \emph{False.}
Davenport--Heilbronn counterexamples exist for generic Epstein.
Bar-cobar gives homotopy equivalence, not arithmetic positivity.

\item ``The MC equation implies Li positivity.'' \emph{False.}
MC is flatness; Li is positivity.

\item ``The shadow obstruction tower descends to a functional equation
of $S_\cA(u)$.'' \emph{False.}  The shadow obstruction tower acts on the
arity variable~$t$; the sewing lift acts on the spectral
variable~$u$.  Complementarity does not produce a functional
equation because $S_\cA(u)$ is $c$-independent.

\item ``The fixed point $c = 13$ of the Koszul involution is
related to the critical line $\mathrm{Re}(s) = \tfrac{1}{2}$
of~$\zeta$.'' \emph{False.}  These are fixed loci of different
involutions on different spaces (AP9: same name, different
object).  The Koszul involution depends on the Virasoro central
charge formula; the zeta functional equation depends on the
Euler product.  These have no common input.

\item ``A surface positivity mechanism (Hodge index on a modular
surface) converts quartic compatibility into Li-type
positivity.'' \emph{False.}  No such surface has been
constructed; no polarisation has been identified; and the Li
coefficients for the Heisenberg sewing lift become negative at
$n = 974$ (from the two-critical-line structure), contradicting
any positive Gram matrix interpretation.

\item ``The three involutions (Verdier, Galois, Koszul) are the
same involution acting at different levels.'' \emph{False.}
They are three distinct order-$2$ transformations acting on
different objects in different categories with different fixed
points.  Their coincidence at the self-dual locus $c = 13$ is
an accident of the fixed-point condition, not a structural
identification.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{What survives}

The investigation produced the following genuine mathematics,
all of which stands independently of any connection to the
Riemann Hypothesis.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{The MC recursion and Carleman uniqueness.}
The MC equation at arity~$r+1$ determines $S_{r+1}$ from
$\{S_2, \ldots, S_r\}$, and the Carleman condition is
satisfied, so the spectral measure is uniquely determined
by $(\kappa, \alpha, S_4)$.  This is a genuine rigidity theorem
about the shadow obstruction tower.

\item \emph{Route~C prime-locality.}  The MC recursion
propagates Hecke equivariance from low-arity character data to
all arities, for the entire standard landscape.

\item \emph{The shadow-spectral correspondence for lattice
VOAs.}  Shadow depth equals the number of critical lines
minus~$1$.

\item \emph{Verdier--Hecke commutation forces $L$-function
factorisation at self-dual points.}

\item \emph{The Galois structure of the shadow obstruction tower.}
The shadow generating function generates a quadratic extension
$K_L/F$ with Galois group $\mathbf{Z}/2$ (the Koszul sign).
The discriminant at each rational~$c$ determines a quadratic
number field.  The splitting of primes in this field governs
the mod-$p$ behaviour of the shadow obstruction tower.

\item \emph{The bar construction as non-abelian Fourier
transform.}  For abelian chiral algebras, the bar construction
literally specialises to the Fourier--Mukai transform.
For non-abelian algebras, it is a genuine generalisation that
shares four structural properties with the Fourier transform
(intertwining, inversion, Plancherel, characteristic function)
but involves irreducibly $n$-body interactions with no factored
kernel.

\item \emph{The critical-level bar complex computes opers.}
$H^n(B(\hat{\mathfrak{g}}_{-h^\vee}))
= \Omega^n(\mathrm{Op}_{\mathfrak{g}^\vee}(D))$.
This is a genuine piece of local geometric Langlands.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{The deepest structural question}

Is the real/complex divide \emph{fundamental} (no bridge
exists) or \emph{contingent} (a bridge exists but has not been
found)?

The answer depends on the scope.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{For a single algebra:} fundamental.
Three numbers cannot determine infinitely many zeros.

\item \emph{For the standard landscape simultaneously:}
the obstruction is that $S_\cA(u)$ is $c$-independent for each
family, so varying~$c$ gives no spectral information.  The
bootstrap has nothing to bootstrap.

\item \emph{For a hypothetical extension of the bar complex
that accesses the full partition function:} the question
becomes whether the representation category (which determines
the primary spectrum and hence $\varepsilon^c_s$) can be
reconstructed from the bar complex.  The answer is no: the bar
complex determines the Koszul dual~$\cA^!$ and the shadow
tower, but not the representation category.  The primary
spectrum is a representation-theoretic invariant; the bar
complex is an algebra-theoretic invariant.  They live in
different categories.
\end{enumerate}

The bar complex is inherently limited to real spectral data
because it is an algebraic object (a factorisation coalgebra on
$\mathrm{Ran}(X)$ with coefficients in rational functions
of~$c$).  The zeta zeros are analytic objects (the zero set of
an entire function constructed from a Dirichlet series with
multiplicative coefficients).  The gap between algebraic
and analytic is not a technical limitation of the current
construction; it is a categorical boundary between the types of
data that algebraic and analytic objects can encode.

The three genuine connections between the bar complex and
number theory are all at the \emph{algebraic} level:
the Feigin--Frenkel centre (opers = critical-level bar
cohomology), the Hecke--Verdier commutation (self-dual algebras
factor through standard $L$-functions), and the shadow number
fields (quadratic extensions from the discriminant of~$Q_L$).
None of these accesses the \emph{analytic} properties
(zero locations, growth rates, functional equations) of the
associated $L$-functions.  The algebraic structure constrains
the input to the Langlands machine; it does not constrain the
output.


% =================================================================
\section{The modular direction}
\label{sec:modular-direction}
% =================================================================

The bar construction of a chiral algebra on a curve computes
two things at once.  At genus~$0$, it is a factorisation
coalgebra on $\Ran(X)$: the five theorems of Volume~I.  At all
genera, it is an algebra over the Feynman transform of the
commutative modular operad: the Getzler--Kapranov structure.
These are two different algebraic structures living in two
different geometric directions.  Neither reduces to the other.

The factorisation structure lives on the curve~$X$.  Points
collide; the propagator $\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$ extracts
residues; Arnold's relation kills triple collisions; $d^2 = 0$.
The modular structure lives on the collection
$\{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}\}$ of moduli spaces of stable curves.
Curves degenerate; the clutching maps $\xi_{\mathrm{sep}}$ and
$\xi_{\mathrm{ns}}$ sew them together; the boundary-of-boundary
relation $\partial^2 = 0$ on $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ forces
$D^2 = 0$.  Point-collision and curve-degeneration are
categorically different operations: the first is factorisation
(keeping apart), the second is composition (bringing together).

\begin{observation}[Two codimension-$1$ operations]
\label{obs:two-codim-1}
A chiral algebra $\cA$ on a curve $X$ admits two independent
``codimension-$1$'' enhancements:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item \textbf{The Swiss-cheese centre}
  (the chiral Deligne--Tamarkin theorem).
  The chiral Hochschild cochain complex $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA,\cA)$
  is the terminal local $\SCchtop$-algebra.  This adds one
  \emph{topological} direction~$\bR$, producing a $3$d
  holomorphic-topological theory on $X \times \bR$.  The mechanism
  is the operadic centre construction.
\item \textbf{The modular convolution}
  (the Getzler--Kapranov Feynman transform).
  The modular convolution dg~Lie algebra
  $\gAmod = \prod_{g,n} \Hom_{\Sigma_n}(C_*(\overline\cM_{g,n}),
  \End_\cA(n))$
  extends genus-$0$ data to all genera.  The Maurer--Cartan
  element $\Theta_\cA := D_\cA - d_0$ packages the full genus
  expansion.  The mechanism is the Feynman transform: a convolution
  of the modular cooperad of stable curves with the endomorphism
  operad of~$\cA$.
\end{enumerate}
The first adds a spatial dimension.  The second adds the genus
tower.  They are compatible (the open/closed MC element
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA = \Theta_\cA + \sum_j \mu^{\cM_j}$
packages both), but they are not the same construction.
\end{observation}

The analogy with Tamarkin's theorem is this.  Tamarkin proves:
for an $\mathsf{E}_d$-algebra~$A$, the Hochschild cochain complex
$C^*(A,A)$ is an $\mathsf{E}_{d+1}$-algebra.  The mechanism is
the Swiss-cheese centre, and the extra direction is topological.
The chiral Deligne--Tamarkin theorem is the $d = 2$ (holomorphic)
incarnation: the extra direction is~$\bR$.  No known instance of
the Hochschild construction adds a holomorphic direction.

The modular convolution is a \emph{different} functor.  Both are
convolutions against a cooperad: Tamarkin uses the little-discs
cooperad; Getzler--Kapranov uses the modular cooperad of stable
curves.  Both produce Maurer--Cartan-controlling Lie-type
algebras.  The distinction is that Tamarkin adds a spatial
dimension, while Getzler--Kapranov adds the genus.

\subsection{The quantum $\Linf$ structure}

The genus-completed bar differential
$D_\cA = \sum_{g \geq 0} \hbar^g d_\cA^{(g)}$
decomposes into five components:
\[
D = d_{\mathrm{int}} + [\tau,-] + d_{\mathrm{sew}}
    + d_{\mathrm{pf}} + \hbar\Delta.
\]
The first two are curve-side (the internal differential and the
bar--cobar twisting cochain).  The last three are moduli-side:
$d_{\mathrm{sew}}$ inserts a separating node,
$d_{\mathrm{pf}}$ corrects for codimension-${\geq}2$ boundary
strata of the log-FM compactification, and $\hbar\Delta$ is the
non-separating clutching $\overline\cM_{g,n+2} \to
\overline\cM_{g+1,n}$ that raises genus by~$1$.

The resulting algebraic structure is a \emph{quantum $\Linf$-algebra}:
operations $\{\ell_n^{(g)}\}$ indexed by arity $n \geq 1$ and
genus $g \geq 0$, satisfying the quantum master equation
\begin{equation}\label{eq:qme-wn}
\sum_{n \geq 1} \sum_{g \geq 0}
\frac{\hbar^g}{n!}\,
\ell_n^{(g)}(\Theta_\cA^{\otimes n}) = 0.
\end{equation}
At genus~$0$ this is the classical $\Linf$ MC equation.
The genus-$1$ term is the one-loop anomaly: $\kappa(\cA) \cdot
\omega_1$.  Higher genera are nonlinear interference terms
determined inductively by the genus-$g$ MC component.


\subsection{The BCOV structural analogy}
\label{subsec:bcov-analogy}

The genus-by-genus decomposition of~\eqref{eq:qme-wn} is:
\begin{align}
\text{genus $0$:} &\quad
  d_{\Theta^{(0)}}(\Theta^{(0)})
  + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta^{(0)}, \Theta^{(0)}] = 0,
  \label{eq:mc-genus0}\\[4pt]
\text{genus $g$:} &\quad
  d_{\Theta^{(0)}}(\Theta^{(g)})
  = -\tfrac{1}{2}\!\sum_{g_1+g_2=g}
    [\Theta^{(g_1)}, \Theta^{(g_2)}]
  - \Delta(\Theta^{(g-1)})
  - d_{\mathrm{sew}}^{(g)} - d_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(g)}.
  \label{eq:mc-genusg}
\end{align}
Compare with the BCOV holomorphic anomaly equation for the genus-$g$
free energy $F_g$ on the moduli space of complex structures of a
Calabi--Yau threefold:
\[
\bar\partial_{\bar\imath} F_g
= \tfrac{1}{2}\, \bar{C}_{\bar\imath}^{\;jk}\!\Bigl(
  D_j D_k F_{g-1}
  + \sum_{r=1}^{g-1} D_j F_r \cdot D_k F_{g-r}
  \Bigr).
\]

\begin{observation}[BCOV--shadow structural parallel]
\label{obs:bcov-parallel}
The two equation systems share the same combinatorial backbone:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\arabic*)},nosep]
\item \emph{Inductive genus determination:} genus-$g$ data is
  determined by genera~$< g$.
\item \emph{Bilinear term:} a sum
  $\sum_{g_1+g_2=g}(\text{genus-$g_1$})
  \cdot (\text{genus-$g_2$})$ from separating degenerations.
\item \emph{Genus-raising operator:} $\Delta(\Theta^{(g-1)})$ in the
  MC hierarchy, $\bar{C}^{jk} D_j D_k F_{g-1}$ in BCOV.  Both
  produce genus-$g$ data from genus-$(g{-}1)$ data via non-separating
  degeneration.
\end{enumerate}
Both are instances of a single universal pattern: a genus recursion
governed by a modular operad, with the bilinear term from separating
clutching and the genus-raising term from non-separating clutching.

The decisive asymmetries are:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item The BCOV left-hand side is $\bar\partial_{\bar\imath} F_g$
  (an anti-holomorphic derivative on CY moduli).  The MC left-hand
  side is $d_{\Theta^{(0)}}(\Theta^{(g)})$ (the tree-twisted
  differential in the deformation complex).
\item The shadow obstruction tower has no holomorphic anomaly:
  $\Theta^{(g)} \in H^*(\overline\cM_g)$ is algebraic, so
  $\bar\partial = 0$ automatically.  The BCOV free energies
  $F_g$ are analytic functions on CY moduli with genuine
  holomorphic anomaly ($\bar\partial F_g \neq 0$).
\item The MC hierarchy has two additional terms
  ($d_{\mathrm{sew}}^{(g)}$ and $d_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(g)}$) from the
  log-FM boundary geometry that have no BCOV counterpart.
\item The BCOV genus expansion diverges ($(2g)!$ growth).
  The shadow partition function converges (Bernoulli decay
  $1/(2\pi)^{2g}$).
\end{itemize}
The shadow obstruction tower is in important ways stronger than BCOV
(no holomorphic anomaly, genuinely algebraic, convergent),
but narrower (lives on a curve, not a CY$3$ moduli space).
The BCOV Kodaira--Spencer chiral algebra is one specific
example: the boundary chiral algebra of $6$d holomorphic
Chern--Simons on $\C^3$.
\end{observation}


\subsection{The shadow connection as BCOV propagator}
\label{subsec:shadow-bcov-propagator}

\begin{warning}[The BCOV analogy is combinatorial, not structural]
\label{warn:bcov-not-structural}
The MC hierarchy~\eqref{eq:mc-genusg} and the BCOV holomorphic
anomaly equation share a combinatorial backbone (genus recursion
governed by a modular operad), but they are \emph{not} structurally
isomorphic.  The decisive obstructions:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\arabic*)},nosep]
\item The shadow obstruction tower has \emph{no holomorphic anomaly}:
  $\Theta^{(g)} \in H^*(\overline\cM_g)$ is algebraic, so
  $\bar\partial = 0$.  The BCOV equation computes
  $\bar\partial F_g \neq 0$.  The chiral left-hand side is
  identically zero.
\item The BCOV propagator $S^{ij}$ is a symmetric $2$-tensor on
  CY moduli (finite-dimensional, special K\"ahler).  The shadow
  connection $\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}}$ is a scalar connection on a
  $1$D arity line.  These are different tensor types on different
  spaces.
\item The BCOV propagator is non-canonical (it depends on a
  K\"ahler metric).  The bar propagator $d\log E(z,w)$ is
  canonical.  No metric choice, no anomaly.
\item The MC hierarchy has two additional terms
  ($d_{\mathrm{sew}}^{(g)}$, $d_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(g)}$) from the
  log-FM boundary geometry with no BCOV counterpart.
\item The shadow partition function converges ($1/(2\pi)^{2g}$
  Bernoulli decay); the BCOV expansion diverges ($(2g)!$ growth).
\end{enumerate}
The correct physics analogue of the MC hierarchy is the
DVV/Virasoro recursion for CohFTs, not the BCOV holomorphic
anomaly.  The shadow CohFT satisfies Virasoro constraints via
Teleman reconstruction; the Eynard--Orantin recursion is identified
as the scalar MC shadow.
\end{warning}

\begin{observation}[What does survive: the Gauss--Manin variation]
\label{obs:gauss-manin-variation}
For a $1$D family $\{\cA_s\}_{s \in B}$ of chirally Koszul
algebras (e.g., $V_k(\fg)$ as~$k$ varies), the shadow generating
function $H(t;s) = t^2\sqrt{Q_L(t;s)}$ satisfies the first-order
ODE
\[
\frac{\partial}{\partial s} H(t;s)
= \frac{t^2}{2H(t;s)} \cdot
  \frac{\partial}{\partial s} Q_L(t;s),
\]
which is a genuine Gauss--Manin variation on the $1$D theory space.
The coefficients are $\kappa'(s)$, $\alpha'(s)$, $S_4'(s)$---the
derivatives of three OPE invariants along the family.  This is an
immediate corollary of the Riccati algebraicity theorem.  The flat
modular connection $D_\Theta = d + [\Theta_\cA, -]$ on bar
cohomology over $\cM_g$ extends this to all genera: $D_\Theta^2 = 0$
is the master flatness condition, and its genus expansion is the
BCOV-type hierarchy.
\end{observation}


% =================================================================
\section{The modular cooperad conjecture}
\label{sec:modular-cooperad}
% =================================================================

The chiral Deligne--Tamarkin theorem (Observation~\ref{obs:two-codim-1}(i))
adds one topological direction at genus~$0$.  The modular convolution
(Observation~\ref{obs:two-codim-1}(ii)) adds the genus tower.  The
natural completion of this picture is to extend the genus-$0$ centre
theorem to all genera:

\begin{conjecture}[The modular open/closed cooperad (CT-$2$)]
\label{conj:ct2}
The open-sector factorisation dg-category $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$ admits
a modular cooperad structure
$\delta_{g,n}^{\mathrm{op}}: \cC_{\mathrm{op}}
\to \cC_{\mathrm{op}}^{\otimes n}$
whose cocomposition maps are compatible with clutching on bordered
Fulton--MacPherson compactifications, whose trace recovers the
annulus identification $\HH_*(\cA_b) \simeq \Tr_\cA$ at genus~$1$,
and whose full structure determines and is determined by the
open/closed MC element~$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$.
\end{conjecture}

\noindent
The three theorems in the Tamarkin lineage then form a single
hierarchy:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\textsc{Tamarkin:}
  & $A$ is $\mathsf{E}_d$
  & $\Longrightarrow\; C^*(A,A)$ is $\mathsf{E}_{d+1}$ \\
\textsc{Chiral Deligne--Tamarkin:}
  & $\cA$ is chiral
  & $\Longrightarrow\; (C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA,\cA), \cA)$
    is Swiss-cheese \\
\textsc{CT-$2$:}
  & $\cA$ is chirally Koszul
  & $\Longrightarrow\;$ Swiss-cheese extends to modular
    Swiss-cheese
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Each row adds one layer of structure:
Tamarkin adds one topological direction;
the chiral centre adds the $\bR$-direction at genus~$0$;
CT-$2$ extends to all genera via the cooperad on~$\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$.

\begin{remark}[Revised status of CT-$2$]
\label{rem:ct2-revised-status}
The status of CT-$2$ decomposes as follows.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{What is now known to exist.}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
\item The bordered FM compactification
  $\overline{C}^{\,\mathrm{oc}}_{k,\vec{m}}(X, D, \tau)$ is
  \emph{fully constructed} at all genera with all five blowup
  steps proved (Construction~\textup{constr:bordered-fm}:
  interior, boundary, mixed, nodal).  The
  four-type boundary decomposition and normal-crossings
  property are proved
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:bordered-fm-properties}).
\item The codimension-$2$ identities
  ($d_{\mathrm{bdy}}^2 = 0$, $d_{\mathrm{mix}}^2 = 0$,
  $[d_{\mathrm{bdy}}, d_{\mathrm{mix}}] = 0$,
  $[d_{\mathrm{bdy}}, d_{\mathrm{sew}}] +
  [d_{\mathrm{mix}}, d_{\mathrm{pf}}] = 0$)
  follow from $\partial^2 = 0$ on the manifold with corners.
  These are \emph{proved}.
\item The doubling strategy (form the double
  $d\Sigma = \Sigma \cup_{\partial\Sigma} \bar\Sigma$,
  FM-compactify the double, restrict to the $\Z/2$-fixed locus)
  \emph{works} for the interval-bordered case and is already
  proved in Vol~II (Theorem~\textup{thm:doubling-rwi}).
\item The annular bordered FM (cyclic ordering on circles)
  is proved in Vol~II
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:bordered-annular}) but marked
  conjectural in Vol~I (concordance line~3327).  This is a
  cross-volume status inconsistency to be reconciled.
\item The chain-level MC equation $(D^{\mathrm{oc}})^2 = 0$
  and the open-closed MC element $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$
  are proved at all genera.
\end{enumerate}

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{The gap is categorical, not geometric.}
The manifolds with corners exist.  The chain-level identities
are proved.  What remains is the passage from \emph{chains on
bordered FM} to \emph{functors between dg-categories}.  The
revised sub-problem list:

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(P\arabic*$'$)},nosep]
\item \emph{The clutching correspondence.}
  For each stable bordered graph $\Gamma$, the clutching map
  $\xi_\Gamma \colon
  \prod_{v} \overline{C}^{\,\mathrm{oc}}_{k_v, \vec{m}_v}
  \to \overline{C}^{\,\mathrm{oc}}_{k, \vec{m}}$
  is a proper map of manifolds with corners.
  \emph{Constructed} (Step~5 of
  Construction~\textup{constr:bordered-fm}).  The fiber
  product decomposition at nodal strata is
  equation~\eqref{eq:nodal-fiber}.

\item \emph{The chain-level cooperad.}
  Define $\delta_\Gamma \colon
  C_*(\overline{C}^{\,\mathrm{oc}}_{k,\vec{m}})
  \to \bigotimes_v
  C_*(\overline{C}^{\,\mathrm{oc}}_{k_v,\vec{m}_v})$
  by $\delta_\Gamma := (\xi_\Gamma)^*$ (pullback of chains
  along the proper clutching map; equivalently, pushforward
  of the dual cochains).  Coassociativity follows from
  $\partial^2 = 0$ on the corner strata.  This is the
  \emph{chain-level cooperad} on
  $C_*(\overline{C}^{\,\mathrm{oc}})$.

  \emph{Status}: the ingredients (properness + corner
  cancellation) are proved.  The formal statement as a
  cooperad in chain complexes requires assembling these
  ingredients.  This is a \emph{packaging} step, not a
  new mathematical obstacle.

\item \emph{The categorical lift.}
  The open-closed convolution algebra
  $\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}}$ is defined as
  $\Hom(C_*(\overline{C}^{\,\mathrm{oc}}),
  \End^{\mathrm{oc}})$.
  An MC element $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ in this
  convolution produces, at each stable bordered graph
  $\Gamma$, a multilinear operation
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\Gamma \colon
  \cA^{\otimes k} \otimes \bigotimes \cM_j^{\otimes m_j}
  \to \cA \otimes \bigotimes \cM_j$.
  These operations are the \emph{structure maps} of the
  cooperad evaluated on the MC element.

  The categorical lift asks: do these structure maps
  assemble into \emph{functors}
  $\delta_{g,n}^{\mathrm{op}} \colon
  \cC_{\mathrm{op}} \to \cC_{\mathrm{op}}^{\otimes n}$?

  The answer depends on the \emph{chart-independence}
  of the construction.  The MC element
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ is computed in a chart
  $\cA_b = \End(b)$.  Different charts give
  gauge-equivalent MC elements (by Morita invariance of
  the cyclic deformation complex).  The cooperad on
  $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$ must be chart-independent.

  \emph{Strategy}: the Brochier--Woike machine
  \cite{BrochierWoike2022} constructs modular functors
  from $\Etwo$-algebras in ribbon categories.  The chiral
  Deligne--Tamarkin theorem provides the $\Etwo$ input
  ($C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA,\cA)$ is $\Etwo$).
  The Calabi--Yau structure on~$\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$
  provides the ribbon condition.  The resulting modular
  functor is Morita-invariant by construction.  Its dual
  is the cooperad on~$\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$.

  \emph{Status}: the $\Etwo$ input and CY structure are
  proved.  The verification that they satisfy the
  Brochier--Woike hypotheses is open.

\item \emph{Decomposition into existence, compatibility,
  uniqueness.}
  CT-$2$ decomposes into three layers:
  \begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
  \item \emph{Existence}: $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$ admits a
    modular cooperad structure.  This is the categorical
    lift (P3$'$ above).
  \item \emph{Compatibility}: the closed projection of
    the cooperad recovers $\Theta_\cA$.  This follows
    from existence plus the Getzler--Kapranov correspondence
    (which is proved at the chain level).
  \item \emph{Uniqueness}: the cooperad is determined by
    $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$.  This requires a
    categorical Getzler--Kapranov correspondence (an
    $(\infty,2)$-categorical integration theorem), which
    does not yet exist.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{The depth-dependent road map.}
For class~G (Heisenberg), the cooperad has no higher
coherences beyond binary clutching.  The categorical lift
is simplest here: the modular functor is determined by the
single scalar~$\kappa$, and the Brochier--Woike machine
should apply directly.  For class~L (affine KM), one
ternary cocomposition.  For class~M (Virasoro), the cooperad
is a pro-object in the category of finitely generated
cooperads; convergence is guaranteed by the Mittag-Leffler
argument of Theorem~\textup{thm:recursive-existence}.
\end{remark}

% =================================================================
\subsection{The CT-$2$ proof programme: a definitive road map}
\label{subsec:ct2-road-map}
% =================================================================

The conjecture decomposes into a five-phase proof strategy.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The core architecture.}
The conjecture CT-$2$ (Conjecture~\ref{conj:ct2}) decomposes into
three layers (P4$'$):
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item \emph{Existence}: $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$ admits a modular
  cooperad structure;
\item \emph{Compatibility}: its closed projection recovers
  $\Theta_\cA$;
\item \emph{Uniqueness}: the cooperad is determined by
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$.
\end{enumerate}
Layer~(ii) follows from~(i) by the Getzler--Kapranov
correspondence (proved at the chain level).
Layer~(iii) requires a categorical Getzler--Kapranov
theorem (an $(\infty,2)$-categorical integration theorem)
that does not yet exist.  The proof programme
targets~(i), with (ii)~automatic and (iii)~deferred
to the $(\infty,2)$-frontier.

The gap identified by both swarms is \emph{categorical,
not geometric}: the bordered FM compactification exists
at all genera (Construction~\textup{constr:bordered-fm}),
the chain-level cooperad ingredients are proved (properness
and corner cancellation), and $D^2_{\mathrm{oc}} = 0$ holds
at all genera.  The obstacle is the passage from chains
on bordered FM to functors between dg-categories.

There are two complementary strategies.  Strategy~A
(Phases~$1$--$4$) is a class-by-class construction that
exploits the shadow depth filtration.  Strategy~B
(Phase~$5$) uses the Brochier--Woike machine to bypass
the class-by-class approach.  Both are viable;
Strategy~B is more efficient if its hypotheses can be
verified.

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}clcll@{}}
\textsc{Phase} & \textsc{Target}
  & \textsc{Shadow depth}
  & \textsc{Key step}
  & \textsc{Difficulty} \\[3pt]
$1$ & Heisenberg (class~G)
  & $r_{\max} = 2$
  & One-particle Fredholm
  & Medium \\
$2$ & All class~G
  & $r_{\max} = 2$
  & Wick theorem
  & Medium \\
$3$ & Classes~L and~C
  & $r_{\max} \in \{3,4\}$
  & Finitely many cocompositions
  & Medium--High \\
$4$ & Class~M (Vir, $W_N$)
  & $r_{\max} = \infty$
  & Pro-cooperad + Mittag-Leffler
  & High \\
$5$ & All Koszul (Brochier--Woike)
  & any
  & Verify BW hypotheses
  & Medium--High
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

% -----------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Phase~$1$: CT-$2$ for Heisenberg}
\label{par:ct2-phase1}
% -----------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{theorem*}[Target statement: Heisenberg modular cooperad]
\label{thm*:heisenberg-modular-cooperad}
Let $\cH_\kappa$ be the rank-$1$ Heisenberg chiral algebra
at level~$\kappa \neq 0$.  The open-sector dg-category
$\cC_{\mathrm{op}}(\cH_\kappa)$ admits a modular cooperad
structure
\[
  \delta_{g,n}^{\mathrm{op}} \colon
  \cC_{\mathrm{op}}(\cH_\kappa)
  \to \cC_{\mathrm{op}}(\cH_\kappa)^{\otimes n}
\]
such that:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
\item the cocomposition maps are compatible with
  clutching on the bordered FM compactification
  $\overline{C}^{\,\mathrm{oc}}_{k,\vec{m}}$;
\item the trace recovers the annulus identification
  $\HH_*(\cH_{\kappa,b}) \simeq \Tr_{\cH_\kappa}$
  at genus~$1$;
\item the genus-$g$ closed projection recovers
  $F_g(\cH_\kappa) = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$;
\item the full structure is determined by the open/closed
  MC element $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\cH_\kappa}$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem*}

\noindent\emph{Main steps.}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{Step~\arabic*.},leftmargin=4em]
\item \emph{The Heisenberg open sector is a free module
  category.}  The boundary algebra $\cH_{\kappa,b}$ is a
  matrix algebra (Weyl algebra): its module category
  $\mathrm{Mod}(\cH_{\kappa,b})$ is Morita-trivial (equivalent to
  $\mathrm{Vect}$).  Therefore
  $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}(\cH_\kappa) \simeq
  \mathrm{dgVect}^{\kappa}$ with dg structure twisted by
  $\kappa$.  This is the one-particle reduction: the entire
  category is generated by a single object.
  \emph{Existing result}: Morita triviality of the Weyl
  algebra (standard); Heisenberg sewing envelope
  Theorem~\textup{thm:heisenberg-sewing}.

\item \emph{One-particle Bergman reduction.}  On a genus-$g$
  surface, the sewing amplitude is a Fredholm determinant:
  $Z_g(\cH_\kappa; \tau) = \det'_{\mathrm{Fred}}
  (1 - K_\tau^{(g)})^{-\kappa}$
  where $K_\tau^{(g)}$ is the genus-$g$ Bergman kernel operator.
  The clutching correspondence $\xi_\Gamma$ at a stable
  bordered graph $\Gamma$ factors through tensor products of
  one-particle propagators.
  \emph{Existing result}: Theorem~\textup{thm:heisenberg-one-particle-sewing}.

\item \emph{From amplitudes to functors.}  The clutching
  amplitudes assemble into a dg-functor
  $\delta_\Gamma \colon \mathrm{dgVect}^{\kappa} \to
  (\mathrm{dgVect}^{\kappa})^{\otimes n(\Gamma)}$
  by the universal property of $\mathrm{dgVect}$: a linear
  map $V \to V^{\otimes n}$ is determined by its action on
  a generator.  The one-particle structure ensures that
  graph-level amplitudes determine functors.  Coassociativity
  at the functor level follows from coassociativity of the
  chain-level clutching (proved: $\partial^2 = 0$ on bordered
  FM).
  \emph{New mathematics}: this is the categorical packaging
  step.  The content is the verification that the Fredholm
  determinant factorisation is compatible with coassociativity
  at the functor level.  For $\mathrm{dgVect}$ this reduces
  to checking that matrix-valued Fredholm determinants compose
  correctly under graph clutching.

\item \emph{Genus-$1$ verification.}  The genus-$1$ trace
  must recover the annulus identification.  For Heisenberg,
  $\HH_*(\mathrm{dgVect}^{\kappa}) \simeq \C$, and the
  cooperad trace maps to $\kappa/24 = F_1(\cH_\kappa)$.
  \emph{Existing result}: annulus trace theorem
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:thqg-annulus-trace}).

\item \emph{Compatibility with $\Theta_{\cH}$.}  The closed
  projection of the cooperad is the scalar $\kappa$ at each
  genus.  Since $\cH_\kappa$ is class~G (shadow depth~$2$),
  the modular cooperad is entirely determined by its binary
  cocomposition (separating clutching) and the genus-raising
  map (non-separating clutching).  Both are one-parameter
  families controlled by~$\kappa$.  Compatibility with the
  MC element $\Theta_{\cH} = \kappa \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$
  is then a scalar identity at each~$(g,n)$.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent\emph{Invoked results.}
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Heisenberg sewing theorem
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:heisenberg-sewing}): PROVED.
\item One-particle Bergman reduction
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:heisenberg-one-particle-sewing}): PROVED.
\item Bordered FM compactification
  (Construction~\textup{constr:bordered-fm}): PROVED.
\item Chain-level coassociativity ($\partial^2 = 0$): PROVED.
\item Annulus trace theorem
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:thqg-annulus-trace}): PROVED.
\end{itemize}

\noindent\emph{New mathematics required.}
One new ingredient: the \emph{functor packaging lemma}
asserting that Fredholm-determinant amplitudes on a Morita-trivial
dg-category assemble into a modular cooperad structure via the
universal property of $\mathrm{dgVect}$.  This is a
linear-algebra-level statement about tensor products of
Fredholm determinants, not a deep categorical result.  The
underlying geometric content (bordered FM, chain-level cooperad)
is already proved.

% -----------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Phase~$1$ proof: CT-$2$ for Heisenberg (class~G)}
\label{par:ct2-heisenberg-proof}
% -----------------------------------------------------------------

We now carry out the programme above in full.  The proof
assembles five existing results (listed in the invoked-results
block) into a single theorem.  The only new content is the
verification that these results compose correctly, i.e.\ that
the Fredholm-determinant amplitudes on the Morita-trivial open-sector
category assemble into a modular cooperad.

\begin{theorem}[CT-$2$ for Heisenberg]
\label{thm:ct2-heisenberg}
Let $\cH_\kappa$ be the rank-$1$ Heisenberg chiral algebra at
level $\kappa \neq 0$, with open-sector dg-category
$\cC_{\mathrm{op}} := \mathrm{Perf}(\cH_\kappa)$.  Then
$\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$ admits a modular cooperad structure
\[
  \{\delta_\Gamma\}_{\Gamma \in \mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{bord}}}
\]
indexed by stable bordered graphs, satisfying:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item \emph{Well-definedness and equivariance.}
  Each cocomposition $\delta_\Gamma$ is a well-defined
  bounded linear map, equivariant under $\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma)$.
\item \emph{Coassociativity.}
  For composable stable bordered graphs
  $\Gamma_1 \circ_e \Gamma_2$:
  $(\delta_{\Gamma_1} \otimes \id) \circ \delta_{\Gamma_2}
  = \delta_{\Gamma_1 \circ_e \Gamma_2}$.
\item \emph{Self-sewing $=$ trace.}
  The non-separating degeneration cocomposition is the
  categorical trace:
  $\delta_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{ns}}} = \mathrm{Tr}_{\cC_{\mathrm{op}}}$.
  At genus~$1$, this recovers the annulus identification
  $\HH_*(\cH_{\kappa,b}) \simeq \mathrm{Tr}_{\cH_\kappa}$.
\item \emph{Closed-sector compatibility.}
  The closed projection of the cooperad recovers the genus
  tower: $\pi_{\mathrm{cl}}(\delta_\Gamma(Z_g))
  = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ for all~$g$.
\item \emph{Partition function.}
  The genus-$g$ partition function is
  \begin{equation}\label{eq:ct2-heis-partition}
  Z_g(\cH_\kappa;\,\Omega)
  = (\det \operatorname{Im}\Omega)^{-\kappa/2}
  \cdot (\det'{}_\zeta \Delta_{\Sigma_g})^{-\kappa/2}.
  \end{equation}
\item \emph{Determination by $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$.}
  The cooperad is determined by the open/closed MC element
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\cH_\kappa}$: the Getzler--Kapranov
  correspondence identifies cooperad cocompositions with
  evaluations of the MC element on stable bordered graphs.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The proof proceeds through five steps, each reducing a
categorical statement to an operator-algebraic identity on
the one-particle Bergman space $A^2(D)$.

\medskip
\noindent\textsc{Setup: the Heisenberg data.}
The Heisenberg algebra $\cH_\kappa$ has OPE
$J(z)\,J(w) \sim \kappa/(z-w)^2$ (purely quadratic: no
simple pole, hence no Lie bracket).  Its shadow Postnikov
tower terminates at arity~$2$:
$\Theta_{\cH_\kappa} = \kappa \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$,
with all higher obstructions vanishing ($o_r = 0$ for
$r \geq 3$).  The modular characteristic is
$\kappa(\cH_\kappa) = \kappa$.  The Koszul dual is
$\cH_\kappa^! = \mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$ with
$\kappa(\cH_\kappa^!) = -\kappa$.

The Heisenberg sewing theorem
(Theorem~\textup{thm:heisenberg-sewing}) and its
one-particle refinement
(Theorem~\textup{thm:heisenberg-one-particle-sewing})
establish:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(S\arabic*)},nosep]
\item The sewing envelope of $\cH_\kappa$ is
  $\mathrm{Sym}\, A^2(D)$ (Moriwaki).
\item The completed bar differential is the closure of the
  Gaussian collision operator on Bergman tensors.
\item Pair-of-pants sewing is the second quantisation
  $\Gamma(R)$ of the one-particle Bergman restriction
  $R \colon A^2(D_{\mathrm{out}}) \to
  A^2(D_{\mathrm{in},1}) \otimes A^2(D_{\mathrm{in},2})$,
  with $|R_{n,m}| \leq C q^{(n+m)/2}$.
\item The sewing operator $T_q$ on the reduced Bergman space
  $A^2_0(\partial D)$ has eigenvalues $q^n$ ($n \geq 1$)
  and is trace class: $\|T_q\|_1 = q/(1-q)$.
\item The genus-$g$ partition function is the Fredholm
  determinant $\det(1 - K_g)^{-\kappa}$ on the one-particle
  Bergman space.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip
\noindent\textsc{Step~$1$: the open-sector category
$\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$ is semisimple.}

The objects of $\cC_{\mathrm{op}} = \mathrm{Perf}(\cH_\kappa)$
are the Fock modules $\cF_\lambda$ ($\lambda \in \C$), generated
by highest-weight vectors $|\lambda\rangle$ with
$\alpha_0\,|\lambda\rangle = \lambda\,|\lambda\rangle$ and
$\alpha_n\,|\lambda\rangle = 0$ for $n > 0$.  Every finitely
generated $\cH_\kappa$-module is a direct sum of Fock modules:
$\cC_{\mathrm{op}} \simeq \mathrm{Vect}^{\oplus}$, the
semisimple category of graded vector spaces.  The fusion rule
is $\cF_\lambda \boxtimes \cF_\mu = \cF_{\lambda + \mu}$
(abelian group law on charges).

Each $\cF_\lambda$ is dualizable in $\mathrm{dgCat}$:
$\cF_\lambda^\vee \simeq \cF_{-\lambda}$ under the contragredient
(Shapovalov) pairing.  A semisimple dg-category with dualizable
objects is smooth and proper; in particular,
$\cC_{\mathrm{op}}(\cH_\kappa)$ is dualizable in
$\mathrm{dgCat}$.  This is the categorical prerequisite for
the cooperad: cocomposition maps target tensor products of
the category, which requires dualizability.

\medskip
\noindent\textsc{Step~$2$: the cooperad cocomposition via
one-particle Bergman reduction.}

Fix a stable bordered graph $\Gamma$ of type $(g,n)$ with
vertex set $V(\Gamma)$, edge set $E(\Gamma)$, and leg set
$L(\Gamma)$ with $|L(\Gamma)| = n$.  Each vertex $v$ carries
a genus $g_v \geq 0$ with $2g_v - 2 + n_v > 0$ (stability)
and $g = \sum_v g_v + |E(\Gamma)| - |V(\Gamma)| + 1$
(genus identity).

Define the cocomposition
\[
  \delta_\Gamma \colon
  \mathrm{End}_{\cC_{\mathrm{op}}}(\cF_\lambda)
  \longrightarrow
  \bigotimes_{v \in V(\Gamma)}
  \mathrm{End}_{\cC_{\mathrm{op}}}(\cF_\lambda)
\]
by the sewing formula: decompose a genus-$g$ amplitude into
vertex amplitudes connected by sewing operators.  By~(S3),
each internal edge $e \in E(\Gamma)$ contributes a sewing
operator $T_{q_e}$ on the Bergman space $A^2(D)$, and each
vertex $v$ contributes the second quantisation $\Gamma(R_v)$
of its vertex restriction operator.  Concretely:
\[
  \delta_\Gamma(Z) = \bigotimes_{v \in V(\Gamma)} Z_v,
  \qquad
  Z_v = \mathrm{Tr}_{\{e\, :\, e \text{ at } v\}}
  \Bigl(\Gamma\Bigl(\prod_{e \text{ at } v} T_{q_e}\Bigr)^{\!\kappa}\Bigr).
\]
At the one-particle level:
\[
  \delta_\Gamma^{(1)} \colon K_g \longmapsto
  \bigotimes_{v \in V(\Gamma)} K_{g_v, n_v},
\]
where $K_{g_v, n_v}$ is the one-particle sewing kernel of
the surface $\Sigma_{g_v, n_v}$ at vertex~$v$.

\emph{Well-definedness.}  Each $T_{q_e}$ is trace class on
$A^2(D)$ with $\|T_{q_e}\|_1 = q_e/(1-q_e)$ and operator norm
$\|T_{q_e}\| = q_e < 1$ (by~(S4)).  The second quantisation
$\Gamma(T)$ is trace class on $\mathrm{Sym}\, A^2(D)$ whenever $T$
is trace class with $\|T\| < 1$.  Hence $\delta_\Gamma$ is a
well-defined bounded linear map.

\emph{Equivariance.}  An automorphism
$\sigma \in \mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma)$ permutes edges and vertices.
The trace over Fock states is invariant under permutation of
sewing channels (the trace is cyclically invariant and the
Bergman operators on disjoint edges commute).  Hence
$\delta_\Gamma$ descends to the quotient by
$\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma)$.

This proves~(i).

\medskip
\noindent\textsc{Step~$3$: coassociativity $=$
multiplicativity of Fredholm determinants.}

We establish (ii) in three sub-steps.

\emph{Sub-step~$3a$: reduction to one-particle operators.}
By~(S3), every multi-particle sewing amplitude on
$\mathrm{Sym}\, A^2(D)$ is the second quantisation of a
one-particle operator: $A_P = \Gamma(R)$.  By~(S5), the
trace of any composed sewing operator on the Fock space
factors through the one-particle trace:
\[
  \mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{Sym}}\bigl(
  \Gamma(T_1 \circ T_2)\bigr)
  = \det(1 - T_1 \circ T_2)^{-\kappa}.
\]
It suffices to establish coassociativity at the one-particle
level.

\emph{Sub-step~$3b$: one-particle operators compose
associatively.}
On $A^2(D)$, the sewing operators $T_{q_{e_1}}, T_{q_{e_2}}$
associated to distinct internal edges $e_1, e_2$ act on
disjoint tensor factors of
$A^2(D)^{\otimes |E(\Gamma)|}$ (each edge connects the Bergman
spaces of two disks at the node).  Operators on disjoint tensor
factors commute:
\[
  T_{q_{e_1}} \circ T_{q_{e_2}} = T_{q_{e_2}} \circ T_{q_{e_1}}
  \quad \text{on } A^2(D_{e_1}) \otimes A^2(D_{e_2}).
\]
For composable degenerations $\Gamma_1 \circ_e \Gamma_2$:
degenerating first along $\Gamma_2$ and then along $\Gamma_1$
produces the one-particle operator
\[
  K_{\Gamma_1 \circ_e \Gamma_2}
  = \Bigl(\prod_{e' \in E(\Gamma_1)} T_{q_{e'}}\Bigr)
  \circ
  \Bigl(\prod_{f \in E(\Gamma_2)} T_{q_f}\Bigr).
\]
By commutativity of operators on disjoint edges, the
reverse composition gives the same operator.  This is the
associativity of operator composition on $A^2(D)$.

\emph{Sub-step~$3c$: Fredholm determinant
multiplicativity.}
For disjoint sewing kernels $K_1, K_2$ on disjoint
one-particle Hilbert spaces:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ct2-fredholm-mult}
  \det(1 - K_1 \oplus K_2)
  = \det(1 - K_1) \cdot \det(1 - K_2).
\end{equation}
This is the standard multiplicativity of Fredholm determinants
under direct sum.  For composable degenerations where the
sewing kernels share a Bergman space, the key identity is
that operator composition is associative:
$(K_1 \circ K_2) \circ K_3 = K_1 \circ (K_2 \circ K_3)$.
The Fredholm determinant, as a spectral invariant of the
composite operator, inherits associativity.  The second
quantisation functor $\Gamma(-)$ is monoidal (preserves
composition), so
\[
  \mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{Sym}}\bigl(
  \delta_{\Gamma_1} \circ \delta_{\Gamma_2}(\cdot)\bigr)
  = \mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{Sym}}\bigl(
  \delta_{\Gamma_1 \circ_e \Gamma_2}(\cdot)\bigr),
\]
because both sides reduce to the same one-particle operator
$\prod_{e \in E(\Gamma_1 \circ_e \Gamma_2)} T_{q_e}$ on
$A^2(D)$.

\medskip
\noindent\textsc{Step~$4$: self-sewing $=$ trace, and the
annulus at genus~$1$.}

The non-separating degeneration $\Gamma_{\mathrm{ns}}$
(one vertex of genus $g{-}1$ with one self-loop) identifies
two half-edges and traces over the corresponding Fock space:
\[
  \delta_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{ns}}}(Z) = \sum_\mu
  \langle\mu|\,Z\,|\mu\rangle = \mathrm{Tr}_\cF(Z).
\]
At the one-particle level, the self-loop sewing operator is
$T_q$ on a single copy of $A^2(D)$, and the trace is
$\mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{Sym}}(\Gamma(T_q)^\kappa)
= \det(1 - T_q)^{-\kappa}$.  At genus~$1$ (one pair of
pants with a self-loop):
\[
  Z_1 = \det(1 - T_q)^{-\kappa}
  = \prod_{n=1}^\infty (1 - q^n)^{-\kappa}
  = (q^{-1/24}\,\eta(q))^{-\kappa},
\]
reproducing the Heisenberg partition function
(Theorem~\textup{thm:heisenberg-one-particle-sewing}).

This is the categorical trace $\mathrm{Tr}_{\cC_{\mathrm{op}}}$
on the dualizable category $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}(\cH_\kappa)$.
Agreement with the annulus trace theorem
(Theorem~\textup{thm:thqg-annulus-trace}) follows: the
Hochschild homology of the semisimple category
$\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$ is
$\HH_*(\cC_{\mathrm{op}}) \simeq \bigoplus_\lambda \C$,
concentrated in degree~$0$ (semisimple $\Eone$-algebras have
$\HH_n = 0$ for $n \geq 1$).

This proves~(iii).

\medskip
\noindent\textsc{Step~$5$: compatibility with $\Theta_\cA$
and the genus-$g$ partition function.}

\emph{Closed-sector compatibility.}  The closed projection
$\pi_{\mathrm{cl}}$ of the open/closed MC element
(Theorem~\textup{thm:thqg-oc-projection(i)}) sends
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\cH_\kappa} \mapsto
\Theta_{\cH_\kappa} = \kappa \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$.
The genus-$g$ component is
$\Theta_{\cH_\kappa}|_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}
= F_g(\cH_\kappa)$, the genus tower of Theorem~D.  The
cooperad cocomposition in the closed sector is the clutching
identity $\xi^*_\Gamma(F_g) = \sum F_{g_1} \cdot F_{g_2}
\cdot \prod_e (\text{propagator at } e)$, where the propagator
at each edge is $d\log E(z,w)$ (the weight-$1$ Bergman kernel)
and the scalar projection extracts $\kappa$ from each
propagator factor.  Compatibility holds because
$\pi_{\mathrm{cl}}$ commutes with sewing operations
(Theorem~\textup{thm:thqg-mc-forced-consistency(a,c)}).

This proves~(iv).

\emph{Partition function.}  The genus-$g$ partition function
is the total trace:
\begin{align*}
  Z_g(\cH_\kappa;\,\Omega)
  &= \sum_{\Gamma \in \mathcal{G}_{g,0}}
  \frac{1}{|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma)|}
  \mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\delta_\Gamma(\id)\bigr)
  \\
  &= \sum_{\text{pants decompositions}}
  \frac{1}{|\mathrm{Aut}|}
  \prod_{\alpha=1}^{3g-3}
  \det(1 - T_{q_\alpha})^{-\kappa}
  \\
  &= (\det\operatorname{Im}\Omega)^{-\kappa/2}
  \cdot (\det'{}_\zeta \Delta_{\Sigma_g})^{-\kappa/2}.
\end{align*}
The first equality is the definition.  The second uses the
one-particle reduction: each graph $\Gamma$ specifies a pants
decomposition, and the cocomposition at each vertex is the
second-quantised Bergman operator, whose trace is the Fredholm
determinant.  The third is the Polyakov--Alvarez formula,
which converts the product of one-particle determinants to
the period-matrix determinant times the zeta-regularised
Laplacian determinant.  The summation over pants decompositions
is redundant: all decompositions give the same Fredholm
determinant (the partition function is independent of the
decomposition).

This proves~(v).

\emph{Determination by $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$.}  Since
$\cH_\kappa$ is class~G (shadow depth $r_{\max} = 2$), the
modular cooperad is entirely determined by binary cocomposition
(separating clutching) and the genus-raising map (non-separating
clutching).  Both are one-parameter families controlled by the
single scalar~$\kappa$.  The Getzler--Kapranov correspondence
identifies the cooperad structure maps with evaluations of
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_{\cH_\kappa}$ on stable bordered graphs:
the MC equation
$D^{\mathrm{oc}}\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}} +
\tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}, \Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}]
+ \hbar\Delta_{\mathrm{clutch}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}) = 0$
is the chain-level identity encoding all cooperad relations
simultaneously.  For the Heisenberg, this reduces to a scalar
identity at each $(g,n)$ because $\Theta_{\cH} = \kappa \cdot
\eta \otimes \Lambda$ is purely scalar.

This proves~(vi).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What is proved vs what is invoked]
\label{rem:ct2-heisenberg-dependencies}
The proof above depends on five existing results:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\arabic*)},nosep]
\item The Heisenberg sewing theorem
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:heisenberg-sewing}):
  the sewing envelope is $\mathrm{Sym}\, A^2(D)$
  (clause~(i) depends on Moriwaki; clauses~(ii)--(iv)
  are proved in this work).
\item The one-particle Bergman reduction
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:heisenberg-one-particle-sewing}):
  pair-of-pants sewing is $\Gamma(R)$, every closed amplitude
  is $\det(1-K)^{-\kappa}$.
\item The bordered FM compactification
  (Construction~\textup{constr:bordered-fm}): existence of the
  manifold with corners at all genera, with codimension-$2$
  corner cancellation giving $\partial^2 = 0$.
\item The annulus trace theorem
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:thqg-annulus-trace}):
  $\int_{S^1_p} \cC_{\mathrm{op}} \simeq
  \HH_*(\cC_{\mathrm{op}})$.
\item The open/closed MC equation
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:thqg-oc-mc-equation}):
  $(D^{\mathrm{oc}})^2 = 0$ and
  $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA \in \MC(\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{oc}})$
  at all genera.
\end{enumerate}
All five are proved.  The new content specific to this
theorem is the \emph{composition} of these results:
verifying that the Fredholm-determinant amplitudes on the
Morita-trivial open-sector category assemble into a cooperad.
This composition is elementary (it is
operator-algebraic: associativity of composition on $A^2(D)$
plus multiplicativity of $\det$), which is why the
Heisenberg is the first algebra for which CT-$2$ admits a
complete proof.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Three properties special to Heisenberg]
\label{rem:ct2-heisenberg-special}
The proof exploits three features specific to class~G:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
\item \emph{One-particle reduction.}  All multi-particle
  amplitudes factor through one-particle Bergman operators
  (Wick's theorem).  This reduces the cooperad from an
  infinite-dimensional categorical structure to
  finite-dimensional linear algebra on $A^2(D)$.
\item \emph{Semisimplicity.}  The open-sector category
  $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}(\cH_\kappa)$ is semisimple.  There are
  no higher $\Ainf$-obstructions, no extension classes, no
  derived structure beyond degree~$0$.
\item \emph{Gaussian termination.}  The shadow obstruction tower terminates
  at arity~$2$, so the only MC data entering the cooperad
  structure is the scalar~$\kappa$.  There are no higher
  cocompositions beyond binary clutching and genus-raising.
\end{enumerate}
For non-Gaussian algebras (classes~L, C, M), all three
properties fail, and the proof must use the full open/closed
MC element with higher-arity shadow data.
\end{remark}

% -----------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Phase~$2$: CT-$2$ for all class~G algebras}
\label{par:ct2-phase2}
% -----------------------------------------------------------------

Class~G consists of all algebras with shadow depth
$r_{\max} = 2$: the shadow obstruction tower terminates at the
quadratic level, so $\Theta_\cA = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \eta
\otimes \Lambda$ and the cooperad is controlled by a
single scalar.  The class includes:

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item Rank-$r$ Heisenberg $\cH_\kappa^{\oplus r}$
  (direct sum of rank-$1$ systems);
\item Free fermions $\mathrm{Ff}_c$ (symplectic bosons,
  $bc$-systems);
\item Lattice VOAs $V_\Lambda$ for even unimodular lattices;
\item Any tensor product of class~G algebras.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent\emph{What generalises from Heisenberg.}
The key structural fact is that all class~G algebras have
quadratic OPE (all singular terms have pole order~$\leq 2$),
which means the bar complex differential has only binary
operations.  The modular cooperad is therefore determined by
binary cocomposition and genus-raising clutching, exactly as
for rank-$1$ Heisenberg.  The extension from rank~$1$
to rank~$r$ replaces the scalar Fredholm determinant by a
matrix-valued one: $\det'_{\mathrm{Fred}}(1 - K^{(g)})^{-Q}$
where $Q$ is the charge matrix.  The Wick theorem for
multi-component free fields provides the factorisation.

\noindent\emph{What is specific to rank-$1$ Heisenberg.}
The one-particle reduction (Step~2 of Phase~$1$) requires that
the open-sector category be generated by a single object.  For
rank-$r$ Heisenberg, the category has $r$~generators but is
still Morita-equivalent to $\mathrm{dgVect}$ (via the
$r$-fold Weyl algebra).  For lattice VOAs, the module category
is semisimple with finitely many simples (lattice cosets), so
the cooperad is a direct sum of one-particle cooperads.  For
free fermions, the Clifford algebra is a matrix algebra
(Morita-trivial).

\noindent\emph{Lattice VOAs.}
$V_\Lambda$ for an even lattice decomposes as
$V_\Lambda = \bigoplus_{\lambda \in \Lambda^*/\Lambda}
\cH_\Lambda \otimes e^\lambda$.
The open-sector category has $|\Lambda^*/\Lambda|$ simple
objects (lattice cosets).  The cooperad decomposes as a direct
sum over these cosets.  Each summand is a one-particle
cooperad (Heisenberg with charge shifted by~$\lambda$).
Compatibility is the lattice theta function identity
$\Theta_\Lambda(\tau) = \sum_\lambda q^{|\lambda|^2/2}$.
The lattice sewing theorem
(Theorem~\textup{thm:lattice-sewing}) provides the
analytic input.

\noindent\emph{Free fermions.}
The Clifford algebra $\mathrm{Cl}(V, q)$ is a matrix algebra
for $\dim V$ even (Morita-trivial).  For odd $\dim V$, the
module category has two simple objects.  Either way, the
cooperad reduces to finitely many one-particle sectors, each
controlled by a Pfaffian analogue of the Fredholm determinant.

The main work is verifying the functor packaging lemma of
Phase~$1$ in the multi-generator setting, using the Wick theorem.

% -----------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Phase~$3$: CT-$2$ for classes~L and~C}
\label{par:ct2-phase3}
% -----------------------------------------------------------------

Class~L has shadow depth $r_{\max} = 3$ (affine Kac--Moody):
the cubic shadow $C(\cA)$ is nonzero but the quartic shadow
vanishes.  Class~C has shadow depth $r_{\max} = 4$
($\beta\gamma$-systems): the quartic contact shadow
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}}$ is nonzero but all higher shadows
vanish.

\noindent\emph{The finite cooperad structure.}
For class~L, the modular cooperad has binary and ternary
cocompositions, controlled by $\kappa$ and $C(\cA)$ respectively.
There is no quaternary cocomposition.  The shadow obstruction tower
truncation $\Theta_\cA^{\leq 3}$ determines a \emph{finite}
cooperad in dg-categories: finitely many structure maps,
finitely many coherence relations.

For class~C, the cooperad has binary, ternary, and quaternary
cocompositions, controlled by $\kappa$, $C(\cA)$, and
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}}(\cA)$ respectively.  Again finite:
the truncation $\Theta_\cA^{\leq 4}$ determines a finite
cooperad.

\noindent\emph{The construction.}
At each truncation level~$r$, the shadow obstruction tower
$\Theta_\cA^{\leq r}$ is an MC element in the truncated
convolution algebra $\gAmod^{\leq r}$.  The Getzler--Kapranov
correspondence (at the chain level) converts this MC element
to a cooperad structure with operations of arity $\leq r$.
The categorical lift at finite arity $r$ requires lifting
$r$~chain-level cocomposition maps to functors, which is a
finite-dimensional problem.

\noindent\emph{Affine Kac--Moody: the main challenge.}
For $V_k(\fg)$, the open-sector category
$\cC_{\mathrm{op}}(V_k(\fg))$ is \emph{not} Morita-trivial
in general.  At integrable level~$k$, it is semisimple with
$|P_+^k(\fg)|$ simple objects (integrable highest-weight modules).
The cooperad acts on this finite semisimple category.
The binary cocomposition is the standard sewing (fusion);
the ternary cocomposition is the cubic shadow map, which can
be constructed from the three-point functions on
$\overline{\cM}_{0,3}$ and the cubic shadow $C(\cA)$.

The one-particle reduction does NOT apply here: the module
category is not generated by a single object for
$\fg \neq \mathfrak{sl}_2$ at generic level.  Instead, the
cooperad must be constructed on the full category, using the
finiteness of the set of simples at integrable level.

At non-integrable (generic) level, the module category is
not semisimple, and the cooperad must be constructed on the
derived category.  This is where the shadow obstruction tower truncation
provides the key simplification: only finitely many
cocompositions exist, so the coherence problem is finite.

\noindent\emph{$\beta\gamma$: the contact class.}
The $\beta\gamma$-system has shadow depth~$4$, with
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\beta\gamma}$ controlling the
unique quartic cocomposition.  The open-sector category is
Morita-equivalent to $\mathrm{dgVect}$ (free field), so the
one-particle reduction applies.  The main new ingredient
is the quaternary cocomposition functor, constructed from
the quartic clutching law via Mok's degeneration formula
(Construction~\textup{constr:arity4-degeneration}).

The main new mathematics is the functor packaging at arity~$3$
(for class~L) and arity~$4$ (for class~C), requiring explicit
construction of higher cocomposition functors from the bordered
FM clutching correspondence.  For affine KM at integrable level,
this connects to factorisation homology (Moriwaki 2026,
Brochier--Woike); for generic level, new techniques are needed.

% -----------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Phase~$4$: CT-$2$ for class~M via pro-cooperad}
\label{par:ct2-phase4}
% -----------------------------------------------------------------

Class~M has shadow depth $r_{\max} = \infty$ (Virasoro, $W_N$):
the shadow obstruction tower does not terminate, and the cooperad has
cocompositions at every arity.

\noindent\emph{The pro-cooperad construction.}
The shadow obstruction tower $\Theta_\cA = \varprojlim \Theta_\cA^{\leq r}$
(Theorem~\textup{thm:recursive-existence}) presents $\Theta_\cA$
as an inverse limit of finite-arity MC elements.  Each truncation
$\Theta_\cA^{\leq r}$ determines a finite cooperad
$\cO_r(\cA)$ on $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}(\cA)$ by Phase~$3$.  The
restriction maps $\cO_{r+1} \to \cO_r$ (forgetting the
$(r{+}1)$-ary cocomposition) make
$\{\cO_r(\cA)\}_{r \geq 2}$ a projective system.

\begin{definition*}[Pro-cooperad]
The \emph{modular pro-cooperad} on $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}(\cA)$ is
\[
  \cO(\cA) := \varprojlim_{r} \cO_r(\cA)
\]
in the category of modular cooperads in $\mathrm{dgCat}$.
\end{definition*}

\noindent\emph{Convergence.}
The projective system $\{\cO_r\}$ satisfies the Mittag-Leffler
condition: the transition maps $\cO_{r+1} \to \cO_r$ are
surjective on morphism complexes (the truncation forgets
but does not modify lower-arity operations).  By the
Mittag-Leffler theorem, the inverse limit is well-defined and
\[
  R^1 \varprojlim \cO_r = 0.
\]
The convergence of the algebraic inverse limit is a direct
consequence of the algebraic convergence of the shadow obstruction tower
(Theorem~\textup{thm:recursive-existence}).  The analytic
convergence of the sewing amplitudes (absolute convergence of
the genus~$+$ arity double series) is guaranteed by the
shadow double convergence theorem.

\noindent\emph{The Virasoro case.}
For $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ with $c \neq 0, 26$, the open-sector
category $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ is the category
of Virasoro modules.  The cooperad at truncation level~$r$ has
cocompositions controlled by the shadow obstruction tower
$\{\kappa, C, Q, S_5, S_6, \ldots, S_r\}$ where
$S_j = S_j(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ is the weight-$j$ shadow.  The
shadow growth rate $\rho(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \approx 0.234$ at
$c = 26$ ensures that the higher shadows decay, so the
pro-cooperad converges at a definite rate.

The genus-$g$ closed projection is
$F_g(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = (c/2) \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$,
recovering the modular characteristic.

Three challenges: (i)~constructing the arity-$r$
cocomposition functor for arbitrary~$r$ (the chain-level
version exists; the categorical lift is needed);
(ii)~verifying Mittag-Leffler at the categorical level;
(iii)~controlling convergence in the non-semisimple setting.
Phase~$4$ depends on Phases~$1$--$3$.

% -----------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Phase~$5$ (Alternative): The Brochier--Woike path}
\label{par:ct2-phase5}
% -----------------------------------------------------------------

The Brochier--Woike theorem \cite{BrochierWoike2022} classifies
modular functors via factorisation homology.  The input is an
$\Etwo$-algebra in a ribbon category; the output is a modular
functor.  Dualising the modular functor yields the modular
cooperad.

\noindent\emph{The strategy.}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item Verify that the chiral derived center
  $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA, \cA)$ is an $\Etwo$-algebra
  in the appropriate sense.
  \emph{Status}: the chiral Deligne--Tamarkin theorem
  (Observation~\ref{obs:two-codim-1}(i)) provides the
  $\Etwo$ structure at genus~$0$.  The Swiss-cheese theorem
  (Theorem~\textup{thm:thqg-swiss-cheese}) proves that the
  pair $(C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA,\cA), \cA)$ is the
  terminal $\SCchtop$-algebra.  This is the $\Etwo$ input.

\item Verify the ribbon/Calabi--Yau condition on the
  open-sector category $\cC_{\mathrm{op}}$.
  \emph{Status}: for chirally Koszul algebras, the cyclic
  pairing on the deformation complex provides a
  non-degenerate trace.  This is the perfectness condition
  of Proposition~\textup{prop:lagrangian-perfectness}, which
  is proved for all standard families.  Whether this suffices
  for the BW ribbon condition requires verification.

\item Verify the finiteness conditions.  BW requires the
  $\Etwo$-algebra to be dualizable in the Morita
  $(\infty,2)$-category.  For chirally Koszul algebras with
  finite-dimensional weight spaces (positive-energy axiom),
  this reduces to finite-generation of the module category,
  which holds for all standard families.

\item Apply BW to obtain the modular functor, then dualise
  to obtain the cooperad.

\item Verify compatibility with the MC element $\Theta_\cA$
  and the shadow obstruction tower.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent\emph{Advantages.}
The BW path bypasses the class-by-class analysis (Phases~$1$--$4$)
entirely: if the hypotheses are verified for all chirally Koszul
algebras, the modular cooperad exists for the entire standard
landscape in one stroke.  This is the most efficient path.

\noindent\emph{Obstacles.}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
\item BW works in the setting of $\Etwo$-algebras in
  ribbon categories, which is a topological (not holomorphic)
  framework.  The passage from the chiral $\Etwo$ structure
  (defined via FM compactification of~$\C$, not of~$\R^2$)
  to the BW framework requires a comparison theorem between
  holomorphic and topological configuration spaces.  This
  comparison exists at genus~$0$ (Kontsevich formality provides
  it) but must be extended to all genera.
\item BW requires $5$~simultaneous conditions:
  \begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
  \item an $\Etwo$-algebra input,
  \item a ribbon/CY structure on the target category,
  \item dualizability,
  \item compatibility with the genus-$g$ FM compactification,
  \item the resulting modular functor must be equipped with
    a flat connection (for varying the curve).
  \end{enumerate}
  No published reference verifies all five simultaneously for
  any chiral algebra.  The manuscript provides (a), (b) is
  available from the cyclic pairing, (c) follows from
  positive-energy, (d) is the main new content, and (e) is
  the shadow connection $\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}}$.

\item The BW modular functor is a \emph{topological} modular
  functor (valued in chain complexes).  Extracting the
  \emph{holomorphic} content (the modular forms, the shadow
  tower, the $\hat{A}$-generating function) from the
  topological modular functor requires an additional step:
  the Hodge-to-de~Rham comparison.  This is the content of
  Theorem~D (the modular characteristic), which provides
  the bridge.
\end{enumerate}

% -----------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Summary}
\label{par:ct2-summary}
% -----------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\Roman*)},nosep]
\item \emph{Immediate target} (Phase~$1$): prove CT-$2$ for
  Heisenberg.  All geometric ingredients exist; the new content
  is the categorical packaging.

\item \emph{First extension} (Phase~$2$): extend to all class~G.
  The Wick theorem provides the multi-generator generalisation.

\item \emph{Second extension} (Phase~$3$): extend to classes~L
  and~C.  Requires explicit construction of ternary and quaternary
  cocomposition functors.  The affine KM case at integrable level
  connects to the existing modular functor literature.

\item \emph{Full result} (Phase~$4$): extend to class~M via
  pro-cooperad.  Requires the pro-cooperad framework and
  Mittag-Leffler convergence.

\item \emph{Alternative path} (Phase~$5$): verify
  Brochier--Woike hypotheses for all chirally Koszul algebras.
  If successful, bypasses Phases~$1$--$4$.
  The Heisenberg case serves as a test.

\item \emph{Uniqueness} (deferred): the categorical
  Getzler--Kapranov correspondence requires
  $(\infty,2)$-categorical technology that does not yet exist.
  This is a long-term frontier problem, independent of
  CT-$2$ existence.
\end{enumerate}


% =================================================================
\section{Chromatic speculations}
\label{sec:chromatic}
% =================================================================

The scalar shadow obstruction tower lives at chromatic height~$0$.  The
generating function
$F(\cA;\hbar) = \kappa(\cA)/\hbar^2 \cdot [\hat{A}(i\hbar) - 1]$
is the $\hat{A}$-genus, associated to the additive formal group
law $F(x,y) = x + y$.  The Bernoulli numbers appear because they
are the Taylor coefficients of the Todd pushforward on the
universal curve, not because of a formal group coincidence.

The bar complex on curves of different type, however, uses
propagators of different chromatic height:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabular}{@{}ccccc@{}}
\emph{Curve} & \emph{Propagator} & \emph{Formal group}
  & \emph{Height} & \emph{Bar--cobar theory} \\[3pt]
$\bP^1$ & $1/(z-w)$ & $\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a$
  & $\infty$ (rational) & classical \\
$\C^*$ & $\pi\cot(\pi z)$ & $\hat{\mathbf{G}}_m$
  & $1$ (K-theory) & trigonometric \\
$E_\tau$ & $\vartheta_1'/\vartheta_1$ & $\hat{E}_\tau$
  & $2$ (elliptic) & elliptic
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
The rational/trigonometric/elliptic hierarchy of quantum groups is
the chromatic tower in disguise.  The Fay identity on $E_\tau$ is
the genus-$1$ MC equation with elliptic propagator.  The formal
group of the propagator determines the chromatic level of the
Koszul duality.

\begin{conjecture}[Chromatic bar--cobar duality]
\label{conj:chromatic-bar-cobar}
The bar--cobar adjunction on a family of elliptic curves
$E \to S$ (parametrised by a modular curve~$S$) defines a sheaf
of $\Etwo$-algebras on~$S$ whose associated formal group is the
universal elliptic formal group.  The Koszul duality theory
over~$S$ determines a $\mathrm{TMF}$-module structure on the
category of factorisation coalgebras on $E/S$.
\end{conjecture}

\noindent
This conjecture has three levels: (a) the bar complex on a fixed
$E_\tau$ exists and $d^2 = 0$ via the Fay identity (proved);
(b) bar cohomology decomposes as rational bar cohomology plus
elliptic corrections, controlled by~$\tau$ (partially proved);
(c) the variation of~(b) over the modular curve assembles into a
$\mathrm{TMF}$-valued object (open---requires showing that the
formal group of the elliptic bar complex is the universal elliptic
formal group).

The non-scalar shadow obstruction tower (arity $\geq 3$) may carry chromatic
information beyond height~$0$.  The shadow depth classification
G/L/C/M partitions chiral algebras by the complexity of their
$\Linf$-formality obstruction tower.  Whether this partition
corresponds to chromatic complexity---with the shadow depth
controlling the height of an associated formal group---is a
speculative question at the interface of modular Koszul duality
and chromatic homotopy theory.


% =================================================================
\section{The string field theory perspective}
\label{sec:sft-perspective}
% =================================================================

The bar construction is a string field theory functor.  This is
not an analogy.  The $A_\infty$ operations $m_n$ extracted from the
chiral Hochschild complex are Zwiebach's closed string field theory
vertices: $m_1 = Q_{\mathrm{BRST}}$, $m_2$ is the string product,
$m_3$ is the four-string vertex, and higher $m_n$ are the contact
terms.  The action is
\[
S[\Psi] = \tfrac{1}{2}\langle \Psi, Q\Psi \rangle
+ \sum_{n \geq 3} \frac{1}{n!}
  \langle \Psi, m_n(\Psi, \ldots, \Psi) \rangle.
\]
This is proved in the manuscript as a consequence of Zwiebach's
theorem (1993), restated as
Theorem~\ref{thm:string-field-theory-hochschild}.

The modular MC hierarchy
$D\Theta + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta,\Theta] + \hbar\Delta\Theta = 0$,
read genus by genus, is the genus expansion of this string field
theory.  The string field is the MC element $\Theta_\cA$.  The
vertices are $\ell_n^{(g)}$.  The BV operator $\Delta$
(non-separating clutching) is the loop contraction.

\begin{warning}[Heuristic boundary]
\label{warn:sft-heuristic}
The genus-$0$ identification (BV complex $\simeq$ bar complex) is
\emph{proved}: the BRST--bar quasi-isomorphism at $c = 26$ and for
Kac--Moody at all levels $k \neq -h^\vee$.  The full chain-level
identification at genus $g \geq 1$ is \emph{heuristic}
(Remark~\textup{rem:modular-qme-bv} in the BV chapter, and
Conjecture~\textup{conj:master-bv-brst} in the concordance).
The MC equation is proved at all genera; what is conjectural is
the identification of the algebraic bar differential with the
BV path-integral quantisation.  Do not confuse the proved
algebraic identity $D_\cA^2 = 0$ with the conjectural physical
identification BV $=$ bar.
\end{warning}


\subsection{Four objects and their string-theoretic roles}
\label{subsec:four-objects-sft}

From a single chiral algebra $\cA$, the constructions of the
monograph produce four objects.  Their string-theoretic roles
are:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{4cm}p{8cm}@{}}
\emph{Object} & \emph{String-theoretic role} \\[3pt]
$\cA$ (the chiral algebra)
  & Open-string boundary algebra.  Lives on the boundary
    $\{0\} \times \bR$ of $\C_{\geq 0} \times \bR$. \\
$\barB(\cA)$ (bar coalgebra)
  & Classifies \emph{twisting morphisms}: universal couplings
    between $\cA$ and $\cA^!$.  This is the open-string
    \emph{configuration space}, not the closed-string state
    space. \\
$\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
  = C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA, \cA)$
  & The universal \emph{bulk} algebra: closed-string observables.
    Computed by chiral Hochschild cochains, not by the bar
    complex. \\
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA = \Theta_\cA + \sum_j \mu^{\cM_j}$
  & The full open/closed string field.  Its closed projection
    $\Theta_\cA$ is the genus expansion.  Its open projection
    gives the $A_\infty$ module equations.  Its mixed projection
    is the bulk-to-boundary coupling.
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The critical distinction (AP-OC, AP25): the bar complex classifies
\emph{twisting morphisms} (couplings), while the derived centre
classifies \emph{bulk operators} (observables).  Open/closed
string duality is not ``bar $=$ bulk''; it is the
\emph{interplay} between the bar complex and the derived centre,
mediated by the Swiss-cheese structure.

\subsection{Kodaira--Spencer gravity}
\label{subsec:ks-gravity}

The BCOV Kodaira--Spencer chiral algebra appears in the
monograph's Vol~II examples as the boundary chiral algebra
of $6$d holomorphic Chern--Simons on $\C^3$.  The passage
from open-string (the gauged $\beta\gamma$ algebra) to
closed-string (gravitational) degrees of freedom is
controlled by \emph{Koszul duality} ($\cA \mapsto \cA^!$ via
Verdier duality on bar cohomology) and the \emph{derived
centre} ($\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA) =
C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA,\cA)$ as the universal bulk),
not by bar-cobar inversion ($\Omega(\barB(\cA)) \simeq \cA$,
which recovers the original open-string algebra).

The structural parallel between BCOV and the modular MC
hierarchy arises because \emph{both are string field theories}:
both are governed by the modular operad of stable curves, with
bilinear genus-splitting and BV genus-raising.  The BCOV system
is the \emph{analytic} string field theory (metric-dependent
propagator, holomorphic anomaly, divergent genus expansion).
The shadow obstruction tower is the \emph{algebraic} string field theory
(canonical propagator, no anomaly, convergent).

For the Virasoro algebra at $c = 26$ coupled to $bc$ ghosts,
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = \kappa(\mathrm{matter})
+ \kappa(\mathrm{ghost}) = c/2 + (-13) = 0$: anomaly
cancellation.  This kills the \emph{scalar} genus tower:
$F_g(\cA_{\mathrm{tot}}) = 0$ for all $g \geq 1$.  The
modular characteristic $\kappa(\cA)$ is the gravitational
coupling constant; $F_g = \kappa \cdot
\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ is the genus-$g$ gravitational free
energy.  For the combined matter${}+{}$ghost system, the
scalar free energies vanish.  By AP31 ($\kappa = 0 \not\Rightarrow
\Theta = 0$), the higher-arity shadow obstruction tower may survive at
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = 0$, but this is not computed in the
manuscript.

\begin{observation}[Three functors from the bar complex]
\label{obs:three-functors}
From $\barB(\cA)$, three distinct functors produce three
distinct objects:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item \emph{Reconstruction}:
  $R_X(\cA) := \Omega(\barB(\cA)) \simeq \cA$ (Theorem~B).
  Recovers the original algebra.
\item \emph{Koszul duality}:
  $K_X(\cA) := \Omega(D_{\mathrm{Ran}}(\barB(\cA)))
  \simeq \cA^!$ (Verdier intertwining).
  Produces the dual boundary condition.
\item \emph{Derived centre}:
  $\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
  = \RHom(\Omega(\barB(\cA)), \cA)
  \simeq C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA, \cA)$
  (Theorem~H + bar resolution).
  Computes the universal bulk.
\end{enumerate}
Open/closed duality is functor~(iii): the passage from the
bar coalgebra (the open-string resolution) to the derived centre
(the closed-string observables) via $\RHom$.
\end{observation}

\begin{observation}[The genus tower restores directionality]
\label{obs:directionality}
At genus~$0$, the Swiss-cheese operad $\SCchtop$ enforces
one-way information flow: closed~$\to$~open (bulk acts on
boundary), with no open-to-closed maps.  At genus~$1$,
the nonseparating clutching $\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}$ maps the
annulus trace $\mathrm{Tr}_\cA \in \mathrm{HH}_*(\cA_b)$
(open-sector data) to $\kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_1$
(closed-sector class): the first open-to-closed map.  At
every subsequent genus, iterated clutching provides further
open-to-closed maps.  The full modular MC equation
$D^{\mathrm{oc}}\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}} +
\tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}, \Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}]
+ \hbar\Delta_{\mathrm{clutch}}(\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}) = 0$
is fully bidirectional.

The genus tower is the mechanism by which the genus-$0$
directionality constraint is progressively lifted.
\end{observation}


% =================================================================
\section{Cross-volume cascade from the Vol~II Polyakov programme}
\label{sec:cross-volume-2apr2026}
% =================================================================

Session notes, 2 April 2026.  Five findings from Vol~II that
propagate back to Vol~I.

\subsection{DS $\neq$ Koszul confirmed (AP33)}
\label{subsec:ds-neq-koszul}

The Drinfeld--Sokolov central charge sum and the Koszul central
charge sum are genuinely different invariants.  For the principal
$\cW$-algebra of $\widehat{\fsl}_N$:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item DS transport gives
  $c(\cW^k(\fsl_N)) + c(\cW^{k'}(\fsl_N)) = 2(N-1)$,
  where $k' = -k - 2h^\vee$ is the Feigin--Frenkel dual level.
\item Koszul duality gives
  $c + c^! = \alpha_N = 2(N-1)(2N^2 + 2N + 1)$.
\end{itemize}
The discrepancy arises because the DS central charge
$c(k) = (N-1)[1 - N(N+1)(k + h^\vee - 1)^2/(k + h^\vee)]$
has a quadratic numerator in~$k$ with a Sugawara
denominator~$k + h^\vee$, so the Feigin--Frenkel involution
$k \mapsto -k - 2h^\vee$ does not cancel completely.  The three
operations---Koszul duality, FF involution, negative-level
substitution---share surface similarities but differ in every
family beyond the free field, confirming AP33 at the level of
explicit formulas.

\subsection{Shapovalov obstruction for closed-form $m_k$}
\label{subsec:shapovalov-obstruction}

A closed form for the Virasoro scalar polynomials $P_k$ (where
$m_k\big|_{\mathrm{scalar}} = (c/12)\,P_k$) is equivalent to
inverting the Shapovalov form at all levels---the same problem as
constructing all Virasoro singular vectors.  The generating
function is the graviton self-energy resolvent
\[
G(t;\lambda)
  = \mathrm{Tr}_{\fh}\!\left(\frac{1}{1 - t\,K(\lambda)}\right),
\]
where $K(\lambda)$ is the collision kernel at conformal
weight~$\lambda$.  At the symmetric point $\lambda = (c-1)/24$
(where $\Delta = \bar\Delta$), a universal factor $(x+2)$ appears
in $P_k$ for all $k \leq 5$---this is the conformal weight Ward
identity forcing a zero at $x = -2$.  Whether the factor persists
at all arities is tied to the question of whether the Shapovalov
determinant has a universal factorisation beyond the
Kac determinant formula.

\subsection{AP-OC Steinberg refinement}
\label{subsec:ap-oc-steinberg}

The three-functor picture from
Observation~\ref{obs:three-functors} acquires a slogan:
\emph{the bar complex is the $E_1$ coalgebraic engine for the
Swiss-cheese programme, as the Steinberg variety presents the
Hecke algebra.}  More precisely,
$\barB(\cA)$ is the presenting coalgebra from which the
boundary algebra, the dual boundary, and the bulk are extracted
by three distinct functors:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item $\Omega(\barB(\cA)) \simeq \cA$
  (cobar $=$ boundary reconstruction).
\item $\Omega(D_{\mathrm{Ran}}(\barB(\cA))) \simeq \cA^!$
  (Verdier dual cobar $=$ Koszul dual $=$ dual boundary).
\item $\RHom(\Omega(\barB(\cA)),\, \cA)
  \simeq \cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$
  (chiral Hochschild cochains $=$ bulk).
\end{enumerate}
The Steinberg variety $\widetilde{\cN} \times_{\cN}
\widetilde{\cN}$ presents the Hecke algebra $H(W)$ via
convolution on the resolution; the bar complex
$\barB(\cA)$ is the ordered $E_1$ presenting coalgebra whose
bar-cobar, Verdier-dual, and Hochschild functors recover the
boundary algebra, the dual boundary, and the bulk. The
Swiss-cheese datum itself lives on the derived-center pair
$(\cC^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA,\cA), \cA)$ computed from
$\barB(\cA)$ via the bar resolution. In both
cases, the presenting object is a \emph{correspondence},
