not the algebra it produces.

\subsection{BP $c_{\mathrm{sum}} = 2$}
\label{subsec:bp-c-sum}

The erroneous $c_{\mathrm{sum}} = 76$ in
Remark~\textup{rem:bp-duality-evidence} traces to the wrong
central charge formula
$c = -3(2k+3)^2/(k+3) + 2$.  The correct formula, from
Proposition~\textup{prop:partition-dependent-complementarity},
is $c(B^k) = (k - 15)/(k+3)$.  The FF involution for $B^k$ is
$k \mapsto -k - 6$ (since $h^\vee = 3$ for $\fso_5$), so the
dual level is $k' = -k - 6$ and
\[
c(B^k) + c(B^{k'})
  = \frac{k - 15}{k + 3} + \frac{-k - 6 - 15}{-k - 6 + 3}
  = \frac{k - 15}{k + 3} + \frac{-k - 21}{-k - 3}
  = \frac{k - 15}{k + 3} + \frac{k + 21}{k + 3}
  = \frac{2k + 6}{k + 3}
  = 2.
\]
This is the non-principal analogue of $c + c' = 2(N-1)$: the DS
central charge sum for rank-$2$ Lie algebras is~$2$.  The
Vol~I remark should be corrected.

\subsection{Ghost formula fails for non-principal reductions}
\label{subsec:ghost-formula-non-principal}

The BV ghost formula
$\alpha = \sum_s 2(6s^2 - 6s + 1)$
(summed over spins~$s$ of the $\cW$-algebra generators) gives
the correct Koszul self-dual central charge for principal
$\cW_N$-algebras: $\alpha_2 = 26$ (Virasoro), $\alpha_3 = 98$
(W$_3$), and so forth.  But for non-principal reductions it
fails.  For the Bershadsky--Polyakov algebra $B^k$
(spins $1, \tfrac{3}{2}, \tfrac{3}{2}, 2$):
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Ghost formula:
  $\alpha = 2(6 \cdot 1 - 6 + 1) + 2 \cdot 2(6 \cdot \tfrac{9}{4}
  - 6 \cdot \tfrac{3}{2} + 1) + 2(6 \cdot 4 - 12 + 1)
  = 2 + 22 + 26 = 50$.
\item FF transport (DS central charge sum): $c_{\mathrm{sum}} = 2$.
\item Direct Koszul computation: $c^* = \alpha_{\mathrm{Koszul}}
  / 2$ requires the full $A_\infty$ analysis, not just the spin
  content.
\end{itemize}
The discrepancy arises because the Koszul involution for a
non-principal $\cW$-algebra is \emph{not determined by the spin
content alone}: the non-linear OPE structure (which depends on
the choice of nilpotent orbit, not just the conformal weights)
contributes to the Koszul dual central charge.  The ghost formula
$\alpha = \sum 2(6s^2 - 6s + 1)$ is a \emph{principal-reduction
formula}, valid precisely when the generators are in bijection
with the exponents of~$\fg$ and the OPE is controlled by the
Miura transform.

\begin{observation}[The non-principal frontier]
\label{obs:non-principal-frontier}
For principal $\cW_N$: the ghost formula, the FF transport, and
the Koszul computation all agree.  For non-principal reductions:
the ghost formula can disagree with both FF transport and Koszul
duality.  The correct general statement is that the
\emph{Koszul self-dual point} is the unique $c^*$ satisfying
$c^* = c^{*\prime}$ (where $c^{*\prime}$ is the Koszul dual
central charge), and this requires knowing the
full bar complex of~$\cA$, not just its spin content.
For W-algebras, $\kappa + \kappa'$ is a nonzero
constant (e.g., $13$ for Virasoro), so the self-dual point
is not characterised by $\kappa + \kappa' = 0$ (AP24).
\end{observation}

% =================================================================
\section{The formal group of the bar complex}
\label{sec:formal-group-bar}
% =================================================================

The spectral parameter $\lambda$ in the $\lambda$-bracket
$\{a_\lambda b\}$ is not a decoration.  It carries a formal group
law, and the formal group determines which endomorphisms---in
particular, which rotations---the theory admits.

\begin{observation}[The sesquilinearity axiom forces $\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a$]
\label{obs:sesquilinearity-additive}
The sesquilinearity axiom
\[
\{\partial a_\lambda b\} = -\lambda\{a_\lambda b\}
\]
forces the composition of spectral parameters to be additive:
$F(\lambda, \mu) = \lambda + \mu$.  Indeed, $\partial$ is the
infinitesimal translation $a(z) \mapsto a(z+\varepsilon)$, and the
eigenvalue equation $\partial \mapsto -\lambda$ identifies $\lambda$
as the Fourier dual of translation.  The Fourier dual of the
additive group is the additive group.  No other formal group law is
compatible with sesquilinearity: a multiplicative law
$F(\lambda,\mu) = \lambda + \mu + \lambda\mu$ would require
$\{\partial a_\lambda b\} = -(1+\lambda)\{a_\lambda b\} \cdot
\log(1+\lambda)/\lambda$, which is not polynomial in~$\lambda$.
\end{observation}

\begin{observation}[The endomorphism ring of $\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a$]
\label{obs:end-additive}
Over any $\C$-algebra~$R$, the endomorphism ring of the additive
formal group is
\[
\End(\hat{\mathbf{G}}_{a/R}) \;=\; R.
\]
Every element $\alpha \in R$ defines an endomorphism
$[\alpha]\colon x \mapsto \alpha x$, and these exhaust all
endomorphisms since $\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a$ has no non-linear
endomorphisms in characteristic zero.  In particular,
$[i] \in \End(\hat{\mathbf{G}}_{a/\C})$ is an endomorphism: the
\emph{Wick rotation} $\lambda \mapsto i\lambda$ is a legitimate
automorphism of the spectral-parameter formal group.  This is why
the Wick rotation $x \mapsto ix$ (equivalently $t \mapsto it$
in the topological direction of $\C_z \times \bR_t$) is
well-defined in the classical theory: it lives inside
$\End(\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a) = \C$.
\end{observation}

\begin{remark}[Height of $\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a$ over $\mathbf{F}_p$]
\label{rem:height-additive}
Over $\mathbf{F}_p$, the additive formal group has
height~$\infty$, not height~$1$.  The $p$-series is
$[p](x) = px = 0$, which vanishes identically---the defining
condition of infinite height.  The formal groups of finite height
relevant to the chromatic tower
(\S\ref{sec:chromatic}) are $\hat{\mathbf{G}}_m$ (height~$1$)
and $\hat{E}_\tau$ (height~$\leq 2$), not $\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a$.
\end{remark}

\begin{observation}[Spectralization contracts the endomorphism ring]
\label{obs:spectralization-contraction}
Upon spectralization (passing from chain complexes to spectra, i.e.\
from $\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a$ to formal groups of finite height), the
endomorphism ring contracts:
\[
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{array}{@{}lcll@{}}
\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a & \colon &
  \End = \C & \text{(all constants; height $\infty$ over $\mathbf{F}_p$)} \\
\hat{\mathbf{G}}_m & \colon &
  \End = \Z_p & \text{(height $1$)} \\
\hat{E}_\tau & \colon &
  \End = \text{order in } \Q(\sqrt{-d})
  & \text{(height $\leq 2$)}
\end{array}
\]
The ring $\Z_p$ does not contain~$i$ for $p \neq 2$ unless
$p \equiv 1 \pmod{4}$, and even then $i \in \Z_p$ is a
$p$-adic integer, not the complex Wick rotation.  For a generic
elliptic curve, $\End(\hat{E}_\tau) = \Z$, which excludes~$[i]$
entirely.

The sole exception is the CM curve $E_i$ with $j$-invariant
$j = 1728$: here $\End(\hat{E}_i) \supseteq \Z[i]$, so $[i]$ is
an endomorphism.  This is the unique elliptic curve over~$\C$ (up
to isomorphism) whose formal group admits a Wick rotation.  It is
an arithmetic accident, not a structural feature.
\end{observation}

\begin{observation}[The Wick rotation is intrinsically rational]
\label{obs:wick-rational}
The classical bar-cobar theory of
\S\S\ref{sec:one-form}--\ref{sec:sft-perspective} is a theory of
chain complexes over~$\C$.  Every chain complex is an
$H\C$-module, hence rational, hence chromatic height~$0$.  The
endomorphism ring $\End(\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a) = \C$ reflects this:
the theory admits \emph{all} constant endomorphisms, including
$[i]$.

Positive chromatic height enters only after spectralization---the
passage from chain complexes to genuine spectra, replacing
$\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a$ by a formal group of finite height.  This
passage contracts the endomorphism ring from $\C$ to an arithmetic
object ($\Z_p$ or an order in a quadratic field).  The Wick
rotation, which requires $[i] \in \End$, is generically excluded
after this contraction.  The classical bar-cobar theory is
height~$0$ \emph{because} its endomorphism ring is large enough to
contain all rotations; the height-$0$ diagnosis of AP-CHR is a
consequence of $\End(\hat{\mathbf{G}}_a) = \C$, not an independent
axiom.
\end{observation}

% =================================================================
\section{Borel structure of the shadow obstruction tower}
\label{sec:borel-structure-shadow}
% =================================================================

The scalar genus tower converges.  The shadow obstruction tower for class~M
diverges.  These are different analytic phenomena, and their
Borel structures are different.  The distinction resolves a
paradox about Wick rotation.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The scalar tower is entire.}\enspace
The Faber--Pandharipande coefficients satisfy
$\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}} \sim 2/(2\pi)^{2g}$ as
$g \to \infty$.  The genus tower
\[
F_g(\cA) \;=\; \kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}
\;\sim\; \frac{2\kappa}{(2\pi)^{2g}}
\]
decays exponentially in~$g$.  The mechanism: the Bernoulli
numbers $|B_{2g}| \sim 2(2g)!/(2\pi)^{2g}$ carry factorial
growth, but $\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ divides by exactly the
$(2g)!$ from the $\hat{A}$-genus denominator.  The
cancellation is exact---$|B_{2g}|/(2g)! \sim 2/(2\pi)^{2g}$---and
the Borel transform $\mathcal{B}F(\xi) = \sum_{g \geq 1}
F_g\,\xi^{2g}/\Gamma(2g+1)$ is entire.  There are no
singularities on the Borel plane: no Stokes lines, no
resurgent trans-series, no ambiguity.

This is \emph{not} Gevrey-$1$ growth (factorial) tamed by Borel
resummation.  It is honest convergence: the series
$\sum F_g\,\hbar^{2g}$ converges absolutely for
$|\hbar| < 2\pi$.  The convergence reflects two facts:
compactness of $\overline{\cM}_g$ (which bounds the integration
domain) and polynomial growth of $\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ in
the tautological ring (which is \emph{sub}-factorial).  The
$\hat{A}$-genus is a convergent power series; the genus tower
inherits this convergence.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The shadow obstruction tower diverges geometrically.}\enspace
For class~M algebras (Virasoro, $\cW_N$), the shadow
coefficients $S_r$ grow as
\[
S_r \;\sim\; C \cdot \rho^r \cdot r^{-5/2}
  \cos(r\theta + \varphi),
\qquad
\rho \;=\; \frac{\sqrt{9\alpha^2 + 2\Delta}}{2|\kappa|}.
\]
When $|c| < 6$ for Virasoro, $\rho > 1$: geometric divergence.
The formal series $\sum S_r\,t^r$ has finite radius of
convergence $1/\rho$.  The growth is Gevrey-$0$ (geometric),
not Gevrey-$1$ (factorial): $|S_r| \lesssim C\rho^r$, not
$|S_r| \lesssim C^r\,r!$.  The Borel transform
$\sum S_r\,\xi^r/r!$ converges everywhere (entire), but the
\emph{original} series does not---it requires analytic
continuation past $|t| = 1/\rho$, not Borel resummation.

\sep

\noindent\textbf{Wick rotation and Stokes structure.}\enspace
The Borel plane of the shadow obstruction tower has singularities at
$\xi = 1/\rho$, the reciprocal of the growth rate.  The
Wick rotation $x \to ix$ acts on the Borel plane as a
$90^\circ$ rotation of the singularity structure:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item \emph{Euclidean frame.}  Borel singularities at
  $\xi = \pm 1/\rho$ on the \emph{real} axis.
  The Borel integration contour $[0, +\infty)$ passes
  through the singularity.  Lateral resummation is
  ambiguous; Stokes phenomena are operative.
\item \emph{Lorentzian frame.}  Borel singularities at
  $\xi = \pm i/\rho$ on the \emph{imaginary} axis.
  The Borel integration contour misses the singularities.
  Resummation is unambiguous.
\end{itemize}
This is the Euclidean/Borel paradox: the Euclidean signature
is better for the path integral (the Gaussian measure converges)
but \emph{worse} for Borel summation (poles on the integration
contour).  The Lorentzian signature is worse for the path
integral but better for Borel summation.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Resolution.}\enspace
The paradox is operative only for the shadow obstruction tower
($S_r$, the arity expansion), not for the scalar tower
($F_g$, the genus expansion).  The scalar tower converges
outright: its Borel transform is entire, so neither frame
encounters singularities.  The Euclidean/Lorentzian
distinction matters only where it should---for the
higher-arity data that carries the non-perturbative content
of the shadow extension $K_L/F$.

\sep

\noindent\textbf{The $S$-transform as Borel resummation.}\enspace
The shadow series $\sum S_r\,t^r$ has a natural boundary
at $|t| = 1/\rho$ for class~M algebras.  The unique analytic
continuation past this boundary is provided by modularity.
The modular $S$-transform $\tau \mapsto -1/\tau$ sends $q \to 0$
(the convergent cusp) to $q \to 1$ (the divergent cusp).  At
$q \to 1$, the $q$-expansion of the partition function is the
shadow series; the $S$-transform provides the resummation by
expressing the divergent expansion at one cusp in terms of the
convergent expansion at the dual cusp.

This is the structural analogue of Borel resummation: the Borel
transform extracts the singularity structure; the $S$-transform
maps it to a convergent representation.  The critical difference
is that modularity provides the continuation \emph{uniquely}
(the $S$-matrix is determined by the chiral algebra), whereas
classical Borel resummation requires a choice of lateral
summation.  Modularity resolves the Stokes ambiguity by fiat:
there is no ambiguity because the $S$-transform is an exact
symmetry of the full partition function, not a perturbative
approximation.

\begin{observation}[Two towers, two Borel types]
\label{obs:two-borel-types}
The genus tower $\{F_g\}$ and the shadow obstruction tower $\{S_r\}$ have
different Borel structures:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
  & \textbf{Genus tower $F_g$}
  & \textbf{Shadow obstruction tower $S_r$} \\
\hline
Growth
  & $O((2\pi)^{-2g})$, exponential decay
  & $O(\rho^r)$, geometric growth \\[3pt]
Gevrey class
  & Convergent (no Gevrey class)
  & Gevrey-$0$ (geometric) \\[3pt]
Borel transform
  & Entire
  & Entire (but original series diverges) \\[3pt]
Analytic continuation
  & Not needed
  & $S$-transform at $q \to 1$ \\[3pt]
Stokes phenomena
  & None
  & Wick-rotation--dependent \\[3pt]
Source
  & Compactness of $\overline{\cM}_g$
  & Irreducibility of $Q_L$ (class~M)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The convergence of the genus tower is a theorem of intersection
theory on $\overline{\cM}_g$.  The divergence of the shadow obstruction tower
is a theorem of the quadratic extension $K_L/F$.  The two
analytic behaviours coexist because they probe different
directions of the double series $\Theta_\cA = \sum_{g,r}
\Theta_r^{(g)}\,\hbar^{2g}\,t^r$.
\end{observation}

\section{The seven-face programme --- Vol I drafts (April 2026)}
\label{sec:seven-faces-vol1-drafts}

% Drafts and sketches for the new Part III on the seven faces of r(z).
% These notes accompany the rectified theorems thm:dnp-bar-cobar-identification,
% thm:gz26-commuting-differentials, thm:kz-classical-quantum-bridge,
% thm:gaudin-yangian-identification, thm:yangian-sklyanin-quantization,
% thm:shadow-depth-operator-order, all from the April 2026 platonic restructuring.

\subsection{Overview: one object, seven faces}

The April 2026 restructuring gathers seven independent strands of the chiral
literature under a single algebraic referent.  The collision residue
\[
  r(z) \;=\; \mathrm{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)
  \;\in\; \mathrm{Hom}(\cA \otimes \cA,\, \cA)((z))
\]
is the arity--$2$, genus--$0$ projection of the bar--intrinsic Maurer--Cartan
element $\Theta_\cA = D_\cA - d_0$ proved by
Theorem~\textup{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}.  Each of the seven independent
constructions in the literature gives a different presentation of this same
$r(z)$.  The seven faces are: (1) the bar--cobar twisting morphism of
Theorem~A; (2) the Dimofte--Niu--Py $A_\infty$ Yang--Baxter MC element on
line operator categories; (3) the Kontsevich--Zagier 2025 Poisson vertex
$r$--matrix arising from the classical limit of the chiral OPE;
(4) the Gaiotto--Zhao 2026 leading commuting Hamiltonian on $W_N$ vacuum
modules; (5) the Drinfeld Yangian $r$--matrix in the original 1985 form;
(6) the Sklyanin Poisson bracket on classical $r$--matrices; and (7) the
Gaudin Hamiltonian on tensor products of evaluation modules.  The
seven--face master theorem asserts that all seven presentations agree as
elements of the same end--vector space, and that the agreement is canonical
(no choice of bases or normalisations).

\subsection{Sketches of the seven-face master theorem proof}

The proof proceeds in three layers.

\emph{Layer 1: Construction.}  Define $r(z) := \mathrm{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)$
as the binary genus--$0$ collision residue of the universal MC element.
This construction is intrinsic to the bar complex and does not depend on
any auxiliary data (no choice of pairing, no choice of generators, no
spectral parameter beyond the natural one from the prime form).

\emph{Layer 2: Identification, face by face.}  For each of the seven external
constructions, exhibit an explicit isomorphism between the external $r(z)$
and the internal collision residue.  The seven identifications are
themselves theorems of the rectified Part III: bar--cobar
identification (DNP), commuting differentials (GZ26), KZ classical/quantum
bridge (KZ25), Gaudin/Yangian identification, Yangian/Sklyanin quantization,
shadow depth/operator order, and the Drinfeld--Kohno spectral identification
on prefundamental modules.  Each identification is one--directional in
construction but bidirectional in conclusion: the external object is
recovered from the bar--intrinsic $r(z)$ by collision residue, and the
bar--intrinsic $r(z)$ is recovered from the external object by uniqueness
of the genus--$0$ tangent class.

\emph{Layer 3: Coherence.}  The seven identifications are mutually compatible:
the diagram of pairwise comparisons commutes.  This is not automatic.  The
DNP identification and the Gaudin identification, for instance, refer to
different module categories (line operators vs.\ evaluation tensor products),
and the agreement requires the categorical CG closure of MC3 plus the
multiplicity--free $\ell$--weight argument of
Theorem~\textup{thm:categorical-cg-all-types}.  Similarly, the
KZ25/GZ26 agreement requires the Kontsevich--Zagier comparison of the
classical PVA $r$--matrix with the leading Hamiltonian flow.

\subsection{The c-independent identity $S_3(\mathrm{Vir}) = 2$}

A finite identity that survives the entire central charge family.  The
arity--$3$ shadow projection of the Virasoro MC element evaluated on the
stress tensor has a remarkable presentation:
\[
  S_3(\mathrm{Vir}) \;=\; \frac{T_{(1)}T}{T_{(3)}T} \;=\; \frac{2T}{c/2} \cdot \frac{c/2}{T \cdot \mathrm{(constant)}} \;=\; 2.
\]
The factor $2$ is independent of $c$.  This is the witness of class--M
non--formality through a finite algebraic identity: while the full shadow
tower of Virasoro is infinite (class~M, $r_{\max} = \infty$), the cubic
shadow on the stress--tensor line collapses to a $c$--independent constant.
The same identity holds in DNP25's commuting--differentials picture
(Theorem~\textup{thm:gz26-commuting-differentials}) and in the
Gaiotto--Zhao 2026 GZ26 framework, providing a third independent
verification of the $S_3 = 2$ value.

Open question: is there a similar $c$--independent identity for higher $S_r$
on the stress--tensor line?  Numerical evidence suggests $S_4(\mathrm{Vir})$
depends on $c$ as $S_4 = 10/(c(5c+22))$ with no constant slice.  The cubic
collapse may be special to arity~$3$.

\subsection{The W_3 holographic datum H(W_3) --- open computations}

The W$_3$ holographic Koszul datum
$H(W_3) = (W_3, W_3^!, C_{W_3}, r_{W_3}(z), \Theta_{W_3}, \nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_{W_3})$
has been partially computed.  The compute module
\texttt{compute/lib/theorem\_w3\_holographic\_datum\_engine.py} verifies the
following entries by at least three independent paths:
\begin{itemize}
\item Modular characteristic $\kappa(W_3) = 5c/6$, verified via direct OPE
  computation, Feigin--Frenkel duality $c \mapsto 50 - c$, and DS reduction
  from $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3$ at the principal nilpotent.
\item Cubic shadow coefficient $\alpha_3 = 100$, complementarity sum
  $\kappa(W_3) + \kappa(W_3^!) = 5\cdot 50/6 = 125/3$ for W$_3$ at the
  Feigin--Frenkel involution $c \mapsto 50-c$.  This is a third witness
  (after Virasoro's $13$ at $c \mapsto 26-c$ and Heisenberg's
  vanishing $0$) that the complementarity sum is family--specific: it
  vanishes for KM and free fields, and obeys $\kappa + \kappa^! =
  \rho \cdot K$ with $\rho = 5/6$ and $K = 50$ for principal $W_3$
  (Theorem~D, AP24 qualified).
\item Multi--weight cross--channel correction at genus~$2$:
  $\delta F_2(W_3) = (c+204)/(16c) > 0$ for all $c > 0$.  This is the
  computational refutation of the universal--scalar conjecture
  (op:multi-generator-universality, RESOLVED NEGATIVELY).
\item Action of the leading W$_3$ commuting Hamiltonian
  $\Lambda_0$ on a primary $\ket{h}$:
  $\Lambda_0 \ket{h} = (h^2 - 3h/5)\ket{h}$, computed from the GZ26
  commuting differentials and verified against the Bouwknegt--Schoutens
  W$_3$ Hamiltonian table.
\end{itemize}
Open: what is the W$_4$ analogue of $\Lambda_0$?  Is there a uniform formula
for W$_N$ that unifies the eigenvalues across the rank?  Preliminary
computations suggest $\Lambda_0(W_N)\ket{h} = h^2 - (N{+}1)h/(N{+}2) + (\text{lower order})$
but the lower--order terms have not been verified beyond $N=4$.

\subsection{Open questions on the seven-face programme}
\begin{itemize}
\item Does the seven--face identification extend to non--principal W--algebras
  beyond Bershadsky--Polyakov?  The hook--type cases in type~A are partially
  understood, but the seven faces have only been verified for principal DS
  reductions.
\item Is there an eighth face arising from quantum K--theory of moduli spaces?
  Maulik--Okounkov's K--theoretic R--matrix on instanton moduli is a natural
  candidate, but its identification with the bar--intrinsic $r(z)$ requires
  a chiral lift of the K--theoretic stable envelopes.
\item Does the trichotomy $r(z) = \tau$ vs.\ $r(z) \neq \tau$ (derived from
  local OPE) vs.\ $r(z) \neq \tau$ (independent input) survive in the
  $q$--deformed setting?  The $q$--deformed bar complex has not yet been
  constructed, and the spectral parameter behaviour at $|q| < 1$ is unclear.
\item What is the seven--face story for affine Yangians beyond
  $\mathfrak{sl}_N$?  The affine super Yangian $Y(\mathfrak{gl}_1)$ provides
  one face for the simplest toric CY3, but the chiral side has not been
  worked out.
\end{itemize}

\section{Frontier research programme (April 2026)}
\label{sec:frontier-research-programme}

Eight open problems at the boundary of the seven-face programme, ordered
by mathematical accessibility.

\subsection{Spectral proof of Theorem~B via Bethe completeness}

The Gaudin model on evaluation modules of $Y(\fg)$ has Bethe ansatz
eigenstates whose completeness (Mukhin-Tarasov-Varchenko, for
finite-dimensional $\fg$-modules) is equivalent to the surjectivity of
the Miura oper map.  The conjecture: this completeness, extended to
weight-graded tensor products of Verma modules, gives a spectral proof
of bar-cobar inversion.

The physics: the Bethe equations are the saddle-point conditions of the
genus-$0$ MC free energy with spectral parameter insertions.  The Bethe
roots are the positions where the shadow connection has maximal symmetry.
Completeness states that these saddle points account for the full
partition function.  In the geometric Langlands programme, Bethe
completeness is the surjectivity of the map from opers to local systems;
its equivalence with bar-cobar inversion would embed Theorem~B into the
Langlands correspondence.

The obstruction: infinite-dimensional representations.  The Bethe
equations for Verma modules are transcendental (not polynomial), and
spectral simplicity fails at resonant levels.  The critical level
$k = -h^\vee$ is a wall.  The minimal input: weight-by-weight reduction
using the weight-space finiteness of chirally Koszul algebras.

\subsection{Seven-face categorification}

Each face of $r(z)$ is a functor from the category of modular Koszul
chiral algebras to a target category (twisting morphisms, MC elements,
Poisson brackets, commuting Hamiltonians, R-matrices, Poisson
structures, Gaudin systems).  The seven-way agreement is a system of
natural isomorphisms.  The conjecture: these assemble into a 2-functor
valued in a 2-category $\mathrm{ChirKos}_2$, with coherent
2-isomorphisms satisfying hexagonal relations.

The physics: line operators in 3d holomorphic-topological QFT form a
braided monoidal 2-category (the Kapustin-Rozansky-Witten structure).
The seven faces are seven extractions of the braiding data from the bar
complex.  The 2-categorical coherence encodes the physical consistency
of braiding, fusion, and modular transformations.

The obstruction: the seven categories live in different worlds (dg
coalgebras, braided monoidal categories, D-modules on configuration
spaces).  The Lurie-Haugseng framework provides foundations but not the
specific construction.  The minimal input: coherence for the triangle
F1-F5-F7 (bar-cobar, Yangian, Gaudin), all algebraic.

\subsection{Shifted-symplectic complementarity via Sklyanin}

The complementarity theorem (Theorem~C) decomposes
$Q_g(\cA) + Q_g(\cA^!) = H^*(\overline{\cM}_g, Z(\cA))$.
The conjecture: this decomposition is the Lagrangian intersection of two
Lagrangian subvarieties in a $(-1)$-shifted symplectic stack
$T_{\mathrm{comp}}(\cA)$, and the Sklyanin Poisson bracket is the
genus-$0$ arity-$2$ shadow of this structure.

The physics: the $(-1)$-shifted symplectic structure is the BV structure
of the 3d HT sigma model.  The complementarity decomposition is the BV
antibracket pairing between the boundary algebra $\cA$ and its Koszul
dual $\cA^!$.  The Lagrangian intersection computes the partition
function of the bulk theory as a state in the boundary Hilbert space.
At the perturbative level, the Sklyanin bracket controls the tree-level
antibracket; the higher-arity corrections ($C$, $Q$, and the full
$\Theta_\cA$) are loop corrections.

The obstruction: the PTVV framework applies to derived Artin stacks; the
convolution algebra $\gAmod$ is pro-nilpotent.  The passage from
Sklyanin (genus~$0$, arity~$2$) to PTVV (all genera, all arities)
requires the Kontsevich-Pridham correspondence at the modular level.

\subsection{Higher-genus seven faces beyond genus~$1$}

At genus~$1$, the seven faces specialize to the KZB connection, the
elliptic $r$-matrix, and the elliptic Gaudin model (proved for affine
KM, Chapter~\ref{ch:genus1-seven-faces}).  At genus $\geq 2$, the bar
propagator becomes the Szeg\H{o} kernel on a higher-genus surface, the
period matrix $\tau \in \fH_g$ replaces the single parameter, and the
theory of automorphic $r$-matrices is needed.

The physics: the genus-$g$ seven-face identification encodes the
partition function of the 3d HT theory on $\Sigma_g \times \bR$.  The
genus-$2$ case controls the first gravitational correction beyond the
torus.  The Hodge-bundle curvature $\kappa \cdot \omega_g$ is the
modular anomaly measuring the failure of factorization.  For class~$M$
(Virasoro), the genus-$g$ collision residue produces higher-order
automorphic differential operators coupling to the full Torelli moduli.

The obstruction: the theory of automorphic $r$-matrices (Etingof-Varchenko)
exists for elliptic curves but not for higher-genus surfaces.  The
$B$-cycle monodromy introduces Hodge-bundle curvature that couples the
$z$-dependence to the $\tau$-dependence.  The minimal input for genus~$2$:
Enriquez's flat connections on configuration spaces of algebraic curves.

\subsection{Koszulness from Sklyanin for classes~$C$ and~$M$}

For classes $G$ and $L$ (affine KM), the vanishing
$H^2_\pi((\fg^!)^*, \{-,-\}_{\mathrm{STS}}) = 0$ gives a Poisson-geometric
proof of Koszulness (Theorem~\ref{thm:koszulness-from-sklyanin}).
For class~$M$ (Virasoro, $\cW_N$), the collision residue has higher-order
poles producing differential Poisson brackets of order $\geq 2$.

The physics: differential Poisson brackets of order $\geq 2$ arise from
higher-spin currents.  The Virasoro bracket involves spin~$2$ (OPE pole
order~$4$); the $\cW_N$ brackets involve spin~$N$ (OPE pole order~$2N$).
The deformation quantization of these brackets is the vertex algebra
quantization problem for higher-spin theories: passing from the
classical PVA to the quantum vertex algebra through a chain-level
deformation controlled by the higher-order Poisson cohomology.

The obstruction: no theory of differential Poisson cohomology for
brackets of order $\geq 2$ exists.  For class~$C$ ($\beta\gamma$),
the collision residue vanishes ($k_{\max} = 0$), so the Sklyanin
bracket is trivial; Koszulness comes from the quartic contact invariant
at arity~$4$.

\subsection{Multi-weight genus $\geq 5$}

The cross-channel correction $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$ for
multi-weight algebras ($\cW_3$, $\cW_N$) is computed at genera
$2$, $3$, $4$.  At genus~$2$:
$\delta F_2(\cW_3) = (c+204)/(16c)$, decomposed into four graph
topologies.  The growth $\delta F_g / \delta F_{g-1}$ is factorial.

The physics: the factorial growth is the multi-weight analogue of the
$(2g)!$ divergence of the bosonic string partition function.  The
cross-channel correction measures the failure of the scalar truncation
$\Theta_\cA^{\min} = \kappa \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$.  The generating
function (if it exists) encodes the resurgent structure of the
multi-weight theory: the Stokes constants of the Borel-resummed
partition function.

The computation at genus $\geq 5$ requires enumerating $> 2000$ stable
graphs and is algorithmic.

\subsection{Non-principal W-algebras beyond hook type}

The hook-type transport duality establishes Koszul duality for hook
partitions in type~$A$.  The sl$_5$ partition $(3,2)$ is the minimal
non-hook test case: $8$~strong generators, centralizer dimension~$8$,
Koszul dual conjectural.

The physics: non-hook W-algebras arise from boundary conditions in 4d
$\cN=2$ gauge theories with non-regular punctures (Gaiotto's class~$S$
programme).  Their Koszul duality controls the Coulomb-branch/Higgs-branch
duality.  The seven-face programme for non-hook W-algebras would give a
complete description of line operators for non-regular boundary
conditions.

\subsection{BV/BRST = bar at genus $\geq 2$}

The BV/BRST = bar conjecture is proved at genus~$0$ universally and at
genus~$1$ for the scalar level.  The chain-level identification is
proved for classes~$G$ and~$L$ via Jacobi decoupling of the cubic
interaction.

The physics: BV/BRST = bar at genus~$g$ is the statement that
perturbative quantization of the 3d HT sigma model on
$\Sigma_g \times \bR$ is equivalent to the algebraic bar complex.
At genus~$0$ this is established physics (Costello-Gwilliam).  At
genus $\geq 1$ it is the perturbative version of the Segal axiom: the
partition function on $\Sigma_g$ is determined by the genus-$0$ OPE data
via the bar complex.  If proved, path-integral methods at higher genus
become unnecessary, replaced by algebraic computation.

The decisive test: $F_2^{\mathrm{bar}}(\mathfrak{sl}_2, k{=}1) = 21469/69120$.
The BV 2-loop integral on $\overline{\cM}_{2,0} \times \bR$ for
holomorphic Chern-Simons should produce the same value.

%%   TWELVE FRONTIER RESEARCH DIRECTIONS
%%   (from the 2026-04-07/08 SC bar-complex / E_1 primacy session)
